<p> <strong>Arizona State University</strong> (also referred to as <strong>ASU</strong>, or <strong>Arizona State</strong>) is the largest <a>public</a> <a>research university</a> in the <a>United States</a>, with a 2010 student enrollment of 70,440.
In 1945, the school came under control of the <a>Arizona Board of Regents</a> and was renamed &quot;Arizona State College.&quot;&lt;ref&gt;<a>History of ASU</a> Arizona State University&lt;/ref&gt; In 1958, a statewide ballot measure renamed the school &quot;Arizona State University.&quot;

<p><strong>Brown University</strong> is a <a>private</a> <a>Ivy League</a> <a>university</a> located in <a>Providence, Rhode Island</a>.
Detail from an oil painting by Cosmo Alexander, 1770; in University Hall, Brown University, Providence, R.I.]] [[Image:BrownUniversity-UniversityHall1795.jpg|thumb|This copper-plate engraving from 1795 is the first known image of Brown.
The original campus was a single academic building that was later named [[University Hall (Brown University)|University Hall]].]]</p>
<p>In 1764, Edwards joined several others as an original fellow or trustee for the chartering of the College in the English Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations (the former name for Brown University), the first Baptist college in the original <a>thirteen colonies</a> and one of the <a>Ivy League</a> universities.[<a>http://www.brown.edu/Administration/Corporation/downloads/charter-of-brown-university.pdf</a>]</p>
In 1804, a year after John Brown's death, the University was renamed Brown University in honor of John's nephew, <a>Nicholas Brown, Jr.</a>, who was a member of the class of 1786 and in 1804 contributed $5,000 toward an endowed professorship.
<p>Brown began to admit women when it established a <a>Women's College in Brown University</a> in 1891, which was later named <a>Pembroke College in Brown University</a>.
<p>The language of the Brown University charter has long been interpreted by the university as discouraging the founding of a <a>business school</a> or <a>law school</a>.
Prior to the march, Brown University served as an encampment site for French troops, and the College Edifice, now University Hall, was turned into a military hospital.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The <a>curriculum</a> was the result of a paper written by <a>Ira Magaziner</a> and Elliot Maxwell entitled &quot;Draft of a Working Paper for Education at Brown University.&quot;&lt;ref&gt;
<p><a>thumb|Brown University seal as a detail on a university building</a> As recently as 2006, there has been some debate on reintroducing plus/minus grading to the curriculum.
<p>As a part of the re-accreditation process, Brown University is undergoing an expansive reevaluation of its undergraduate education offerings through the newly appointed Task Force on Undergraduate Education.

In 1991, the school was officially renamed the Brown University School of Medicine, then renamed once more to Brown Medical School in October 2000.&lt;ref&gt;<a>History of the Brown Medical School</a>&lt;/ref&gt; In January 2007, self-made entrepreneur Warren Alpert donated $100 million to Brown Medical School on behalf of the Warren Alpert Foundation, tying <a>Sidney Frank</a> for the largest single monetary contribution ever made to the University.
In recognition of the gift, the faculty of Brown University approved changing the name of the Brown Medical School to The Warren Alpert Medical School of Brown University.
Since 2005, the MBL and Brown University have collaborated in a Ph.D.-awarding Graduate Program in Biological and Environmental Sciences, which brings together faculty from both institutions.

Barnard College is the most selective women's college in the nation;&lt;ref name=&quot;Alix Pianin&quot;/&gt; in 2008, Barnard had the lowest acceptance rate of the five <a>Seven Sisters</a> that remain single-sex in admissions.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Rankingsandreviews.com</a>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>Rankingsandreviews.com</a>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>Rankingsandreviews.com</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>

According to the <em>U.S. News &amp; World Report's</em> Best Graduate Schools 2011 ranking, &quot;California Institute of Technology headlines the new rankings, with top billing in three categories: chemistry, earth sciences and physics.&quot;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>

31, No. 2, 1997) |author=Caltech News|publisher=California Institute of Technology}}&lt;/ref&gt; <a>Hotmail</a>,&lt;ref&gt;<a>Sabeer Bhatia</a>, BS 1991&lt;/ref&gt; <a>Compaq</a>,&lt;ref&gt;Benjamin Rosen, BS 1954&lt;/ref&gt; and <a>MathWorks</a>  (which created <a>Matlab</a>),&lt;ref&gt;<a>Cleve Moler</a>, BS 1961 &lt;/ref&gt; while graduate students founded, or co-founded,  companies such as <a>Intel</a>,&lt;ref&gt;<a>Gordon Moore</a>, PhD 1954&lt;/ref&gt; <a>TRW</a>,&lt;ref&gt;<a>Simon Ramo</a>, PhD 1936 {{cite web|url=<a>http://today.caltech.edu/today/story-display.tcl?story_id=42622</a>|title=The Singular Si Ramo|date=2010-02-24|author=Caltech Public Relations|publisher=Caltech Today (via California Institute of Technology)}}&lt;/ref&gt; and the <a>Exploratorium</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Frank Oppenheimer</a>, PhD 1939 &lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p><a>ar:&#x0645;&#x0639;&#x0647;&#x062f; &#x0643;&#x0627;&#x0644;&#x064a;&#x0641;&#x0648;&#x0631;&#x0646;&#x064a;&#x0627; &#x0644;&#x0644;&#x062a;&#x0643;&#x0646;&#x0648;&#x0644;&#x0648;&#x062c;&#x064a;&#x0627;</a> <a>az:Kaliforniya Texnologiya &#x0130;nstitutu</a> <a>bn:&#x0995;&#x09cd;&#x09af;&#x09be;&#x09b2;&#x09bf;&#x09ab;&#x09cb;&#x09b0;&#x09cd;&#x09a8;&#x09bf;&#x09af;&#x09bc;&#x09be; |name = Columbia University in the City of New York |motto = <em>In lumine Tuo videbimus lumen</em> (<a>Latin</a>) |mottoeng = In Thy light shall we see light (<a>Psalm</a> 36:9) |established = 1754 |type = <a>Private</a> |endowment = <a>US $</a>6.5 <a>billion</a>&lt;ref&gt;As of 2010.
|logo = <a>center|225px</a> }} <strong>Columbia University in the City of New York</strong> (<strong>Columbia University</strong>) is a private research <a>university</a> in New York City and one of the eight members of the <a>Ivy League</a>.
<p><a>thumb|Development of the Morningside Heights campus by 1915</a> In 1896, the trustees officially authorized the use of yet another new name, Columbia University, and today the institution is officially known as &quot;Columbia University in the City of New York.&quot;
  <li>Robert A. McCaughey: <em>Stand, Columbia: A History of Columbia University in the City of New York, 1754&#x2013;2004</em>, Columbia University Press, 2003, ISBN 0231130082</li>
<p>:<em>Not to be confused with <a>New York University</a>, formerly known as the <strong>University of the City of New York</strong>.</em> :<em>For similar uses, see <a>University of New York (disambiguation)</a>.</em>  The <strong>City University of New York</strong> (<strong>CUNY</strong>), <a>acronym</a> , is the public <a>university system</a> of <a>New York City</a>, with its administrative offices in <a>Yorkville</a> in <a>Manhattan</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&quot;<a>Administrative
City University of New York.
It is the largest urban university in the <a>United States</a>, consisting of 23 institutions: 11 senior colleges, six <a>community colleges</a>, the <a>William E. Macaulay Honors College</a> at CUNY, the doctorate-granting <a>Graduate School and University Center</a>, the <a>City University of New York School of Law</a>, <a>CUNY Graduate School of Journalism</a>, and the <a>Sophie Davis School of Biomedical Education</a>.
Chancellor <a>Matthew Goldstein</a>, who recently championed higher education as critical to the nation's economic recovery efforts, said enrollment at City University of New York is at its highest level in more than three decades.</p>
<a>&quot;City University of New York&quot;</a> <em>U.S. History Encyclopedia</em>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>In 1961, Governor Nelson Rockefeller signed the bill that formally created the City University of New York to integrate these institutions, and a new graduate school, together into a coordinate system of higher education for the city, and by 1979, the Board of Higher Education had become the Board of Trustees of the CUNY.&lt;ref
<a>1986 Memo from Bogdan Denitch to Joseph S. Murphy, Chancellor City University of New York in 1980s</a>.
<p>In September 2006, The City University of New York received a $30,000,000 gift from philanthropist and <a>City College</a> alumnus, William E. Macaulay, Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of <a>First Reserve Corporation</a>.
  <li><a>Iris Weinshall</a> (B.A. 1975), <a>vice chancellor</a> at the City University of New York and a former commissioner of the <a>New York City Department of Transportation</a></li>
  <li><a>City University of New York Athletic Conference</a></li>

<p><a>de:City University of New York</a> <a>es:Universidad de la Ciudad de Nueva York</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x0634;&#x0647;&#x0631;&#x06cc; &#x0646;&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0631;&#x06a9;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; de la Ville de New York</a> <a>it:Universit&#x00e0; della Citt&#x00e0; di New York</a> <a>ja:&#x30cb;&#x30e5;&#x30fc;&#x30e8;&#x30fc;&#x30af;&#x5e02;&#x7acb;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:City University of New York</a> <a>pt:Universidade da Cidade de Nova Iorque</a> <a>uk:&#x041c;&#x0456;&#x0441;&#x044c;&#x043a;&#x0438;&#x0439; &#x0443;&#x043d;&#x0456;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442; &#x041d;&#x044c;&#x044e;-&#x0419;&#x043e;&#x0440;&#x043a;&#x0430;</a> <a>zh:&#x7ebd;&#x7ea6;&#x5e02;&#x7acb;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a></p>
<p> <strong>Drexel University</strong> is a <a>private</a> <a>coeducation</a>al <a>university</a> with the main campus located in the <a>University City</a> area within <a>Philadelphia</a>, <a>Pennsylvania</a>, <a>United States</a>.
<a>right|thumb|A machine testing laboratory at Drexel University, circa 1904.</a>
Drexel University was founded in 1891 as the Drexel Institute of Art, Science and Industry by Philadelphia financier and philanthropist <a>Anthony J. Drexel</a> to provide educational opportunities in the &#x201c;practical arts and sciences&#x201d; for women and men of all backgrounds.
Drexel became the Drexel Institute of Technology in 1936, and in 1970 Drexel Institute of Technology gained university status, becoming Drexel University.
On July 1, 2002, Drexel was officially united with the former MCP Hahnemann University, creating the Drexel University College of Medicine; and in the fall of 2006, Drexel established its School of Law.
In June 2009, the president of Drexel University, <a>Constantine Papadakis</a>, died of lung cancer.
Originally added to Drexel University as the Drexel University College of Law, the <a>Earle Mack School of Law</a> was renamed on May 1, 2008 in honor of Drexel alumnus <a>Earle I. Mack</a>.
<p>Drexel is composed of nine colleges, including the <a>College of Information Science and Technology</a> and the <a>College of Arts and Sciences</a>, two of the oldest colleges within Drexel; and the <a>Drexel University College of Engineering</a>, for which Drexel is perhaps best-known.
The <a>Drexel University College of Medicine</a> is a recent addition to the university.
<p>Drexel University is also known for creating the world's first Engineering Degree in <a>Appropriate Technology</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
In the 2006 edition of <a>U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>, Drexel University is ranked the #109 university in the National Universities Doctoral category and the LeBow College of Business is ranked #99.
<p> Drexel University's campus is divided into three parts: the <a>University City Campus</a>, the Center City Hahnemann Campus, which is comprised mainly of <a>Hahnemann University Hospital</a>, and the <a>Queen Lane College of Medicine Campus</a>.
<p><a>thumb|The southern portion of Drexel's campus</a> The  University City Main Campus of Drexel University is located just west of the <a>Schuylkill River</a> in the University City district of Philadelphia, Pennsylvania.
The two prominent performing stages at Drexel University are the Mandell Theater and the Main Auditorium.
Theater at Drexel University</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The Queen Lane Medical Campus was purchased in 2003 by Drexel University from MCP Hahnemann University.
<p>On October 29, 2007, a 40-person delegation from Drexel University completed a four-day visit to <a>Placer County, California</a> in preparation for a study on bringing a 6,000-student college campus to <a>Roseville</a>, a suburb in the <a>Sacramento metropolitan area</a>.
<p>On January 5, 2009, Drexel University opened the Center for Graduate Studies in Sacramento.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; , the Sacramento Center offers a Ed.D. program in Educational Leadership and Management, and master degree programs in:  Business Administration, Higher Education, Human Resource Development, Information Systems, Public Health, Interdepartmental Medical Science, and Library and Information Science&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;  Drexel awards students at its Sacremento Center fellowships from a $10 million annual budget allocation.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The Undergraduate Student Government Association of Drexel University works with administrators to solve student problems and tries to promote communication between the students and the administration.</p>
The student operated station is part of the Paul F. Harron Studios at Drexel University.
name=&quot;DUArch&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Other publications include <em>MAYA</em>, the undergraduate student literary and artistic magazine; <em>D&amp;M Magazine</em>, Design &amp; Merchandising students crafted magazine; <em>The Smart Set from Drexel University</em>, an online magazine founded in 2005; and <em>The Drexelist</em> a blog-style news source founded in 2010.</p>
The Drexel Publishing Group oversees <em>ASK</em> (The Journal of the College of Arts and Sciences at Drexel University), <em>Painted Bride Quarterly</em>, a 36-year-old national literary magazine housed at Drexel; <em>The 33rd</em>, an annual anthology of student and faculty writing at Drexel; <em>DPG Online Magazine</em>, and <em>Maya</em>, the undergraduate literary and artistic magazine.
Grotto:Most Expensive College Dorms for 2009-2010</a>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>About Drexel University</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The Flame of Knowledge, a fountain once located in the main quad (now relocated to the area in front of North Hall), used to be known as the &quot;Drexel Shaft&quot; in the late 70s and early 80s,&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|title=Drexel University Digital Collections - Return of the Red-Eye (Satire)|url=<a>http://www.library.drexel.edu/archives/displays/items/show/207</a>|accessdate=2009-05-11}}
<li>From July through September 2009, the movie, <a>How Do You Know</a>, starring Jack Nicholson, Reese Witherspoon, and Owen Wilson was filmed on the Drexel University main campus inside of the <a>Armory</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</li>
<p>Drexel University created the annual <a>$100,000 Anthony J. Drexel Exceptional Achievement Award</a> to recognize a faculty member from a U.S. institution whose work transforms both research and the society it serves.

<p><a>ar:&#x062c;&#x0627;&#x0645;&#x0639;&#x0629; &#x062f;&#x0631;&#x0643;&#x0633;&#x0644;</a> <a>de:Drexel University</a> <a>es:Universidad Drexel</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x062f;&#x0631;&#x06a9;&#x0633;&#x0644;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; Drexel</a> <a>is:Drexel-h&#x00e1;sk&#x00f3;li</a> <a>la:Universitas Drexel</a> <a>ja:&#x30c9;&#x30ec;&#x30af;&#x30bb;&#x30eb;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:Drexel University</a> <a>pt:Universidade Drexel</a> <a>simple:Drexel University</a> <a>vi:&#x0110;&#x1ea1;i h&#x1ecd;c Drexel</a> <a>zh:&#x5353;&#x514b;&#x7d22;&#x5927;&#x5b78;</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox university |name=Dartmouth College |image_name=Dartmouth College shield.svg
<p><strong>Dartmouth College</strong> (, ) is a <a>private</a>, <a>Ivy League</a> university, comprising a liberal arts college, <a>Dartmouth Medical School</a>, <a>Thayer School of Engineering</a>, and <a>Tuck School of Business</a>, as well as 19 graduate programs in the arts and sciences.&lt;ref
Incorporated as &quot;Trustees of Dartmouth College,&quot;&lt;ref name=&quot;irs&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; it is one of the nine <a>Colonial Colleges</a> founded before the American Revolution.&lt;ref
<p>Dartmouth College was established in 1769 by <a>Congregational</a> minister <a>Eleazar Wheelock</a>.
news | url = <a>http://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html?res=9D02E0D81F3BF934A35752C1A96F958260</a> | title = A Frat Party Is:; a) Milk and Cookies; b) Beer Pong | first = Randy | last = Kennedy | work =The New York Times | quote = ...at Dartmouth College a place where traditions die hard... | date = 1999-11-07 | accessdate = 2008-08-23 }}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>[[File:Dartmouth College campus 2007-10-02 03 - Charter.jpg.jpg|thumb|upright|The
Charter of Dartmouth College on display in [[Baker Memorial Library]].
name=&quot;CricketRauner&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;]] In 1819, Dartmouth College was the subject of the historic <a>Dartmouth College case</a>, in which the State of <a>New Hampshire</a>'s 1816 attempt to amend the College's royal charter to make the school a public university was challenged.
In 2004, <a>Booz Allen Hamilton</a> selected Dartmouth College as a model of institutional endurance &quot;whose record of endurance has had implications and benefits for all American organizations, both academic and commercial,&quot; citing <em><a>Trustees of Dartmouth College v. Woodward</a></em> and Dartmouth's successful self-reinvention in the late 19th century.&lt;ref&gt;;
section on Dartmouth College footnoted to John R. Thelin, who also selected the <a>University of Oxford</a> for inclusion as a model of institutional endurance.&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
With these professional schools and graduate programs, conventional American usage would accord Dartmouth the label of &quot;Dartmouth University&quot;;&lt;ref name=&quot;about-dartmouth-facts&quot;/&gt; however, because of historical and nostalgic reasons (such as <em><a>Dartmouth College v. Woodward</a></em>), the school uses the name &quot;Dartmouth College&quot; to refer to the entire institution.&lt;ref
<p>[[File:BakerLibrary.jpg|thumb|left|upright|[[Baker Memorial Library]] at Dartmouth College]] Dartmouth functions on a quarter system, operating year-round on four ten-week <a>academic term</a>s.
The nominees for alumni trustee are determined by a poll of the members of the Association of Alumni of Dartmouth College, selecting from among names put forward by the Alumni Council or by alumni petition.</p>
<p>Dartmouth College is situated in the rural town of <a>Hanover, New Hampshire</a>, located in the <a>Upper Valley</a> along the <a>Connecticut River</a> in <a>New England</a>.
[[File:Dartmouth College campus 2007-10-20 09.JPG|thumb|left|A view of the Sherman Fairchild Physical Science Center and Wheeler Hall from the tower of [[Baker Memorial Library]]]] In addition to its nineteen graduate programs in the arts and sciences, Dartmouth is home to three separate graduate schools.
<p>Dartmouth's nine libraries are all part of the collective Dartmouth College Library, which comprises 2.48 million volumes and 6 million total resources, including videos, maps, sound recordings, and photographs.&lt;ref
<p>[[File:Dartmouth College campus 2007-06-23 Memorial Field 02.JPG|thumb|right|[[Memorial Field (Dartmouth College)|Memorial Field]]]] Dartmouth's original sports field was <a>the Green</a>, where students played <a>cricket</a> and <a>old division football</a> during the 19th century.&lt;ref
<p> [[File:Dartmouth College campus 2007-10-03 Robinson Hall.JPG|thumb|right|Robinson Hall houses many of the College's student-run organizations, including the [[Dartmouth Outing Club]].
Dartmouth College was among the first institutions of higher education to <a>desegregate</a> fraternity houses in the 1950s, and was involved in the movement to create <a>coeducational</a> Greek houses in the 1970s.&lt;ref&gt;
As of 2007, Dartmouth College fields 34 intercollegiate varsity teams: 16 for men, 16 for women, and coeducational sailing and equestrian programs.
name=&quot;about-dartmouth-athletics&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; As is mandatory for the members of the Ivy League, Dartmouth College does not offer athletic scholarships.&lt;ref
<p>It is often pointed out that the charter of Dartmouth College, granted to <a>Eleazar Wheelock</a> in 1769, proclaims that the institution was created &quot;for the education and instruction of Youth of the Indian Tribes in this Land in reading, writing and all parts of Learning ... as well as in all liberal Arts and Sciences; and also of English Youth and any others.&quot;&lt;ref
The funds for the Charity School for Native Americans that preceded Dartmouth College were raised primarily by the efforts of a Native American named <a>Samson Occom</a>, and at least some of those funds were used to help found the College.&lt;ref
<p> <a>thumb|upright|left|Seal of Dartmouth College</a></p>
<p>On October 28, 1926, the Trustees approved a &quot;Dartmouth College Shield&quot; for general use.
<p><a>thumb|upright|Keggy posing on the Dartmouth College Green with Baker Memorial Library in the background.</a>
name=&quot;greencolor&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;History-of-Dartmouth-Hanover&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Beginning in the 1920s, the Dartmouth College athletic teams were known by their unofficial nickname &quot;the Indians,&quot; a moniker that probably originated among sports journalists.&lt;ref
<p>According to Payscale, Dartmouth College alums have among the highest average starting salaries ($58,200) in the United States, as well as the absolute highest average income ten years after graduation ($129,000).&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>In 2010, the senior class gift fund-raiser led to charges of strong-arming by Dartmouth College, which had student volunteers pressure and hassle students who refused to donate.
In particular, Dartmouth College released particulars of senior students who refused to donate as a pressure tactic.
<p>In response to the media reports, Dartmouth College stated that it regretted the releasing of the personal particulars of the student in question, and that it was &quot;highly inappropriate&quot; to have done so,&lt;ref name=&quot;nytimes1&quot;/&gt; but defended its actions as being necessary in order to obtain the donations.
<p>Dartmouth College has appeared in or been referenced by a number of popular media.</p>

<p>The Eindhoven University of Technology was founded as the <em>Technische Hogeschool Eindhoven</em> (THE) on June 23, 1956 by the Dutch government.
Yearly, the Eindhoven University of Technology produces almost 3000 scientific publications, 140 PhD-awards, and 40 patents.</p>
<p>The Eindhoven University of Technology is main participant in the technological top institutes DPI and <a>M2i</a>.
<p>The Eindhoven University of Technology is a public university of the Netherlands.

<p>On the 2009 <a>THE&#x2013;QS World University Rankings</a> (From 2010 two separate rankings will be produced by the <a>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> and the <a>QS World University Rankings</a>) list, the Eindhoven University of Technology was ranked inside the top 200 for the fifth consecutive year.
On the <a>Times Higher Education</a> ranking of 2010&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Eindhoven University of Technology is the highest ranked (#114) University of the Netherlands.

<p>{{Infobox University |name            = University of Gothenburg |native_name     = G&#x00f6;teborgs universitet |latin_name      = Universitas Regia Gothoburgensis |image_name      = University of Gothenburg logo.svg
<p>The <strong>University of Gothenburg</strong> () is a <a>university</a> in <a>Sweden</a>'s second largest city, <a>Gothenburg</a>.
<p><a>thumb|left|The entrance of the main administrative building of the university</a> The University of Gothenburg is the third-oldest <a>Swedish university</a>, and with 24,900 full-time students&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Gothenburg, facts and figures</a>&lt;/ref&gt; it is also among the largest universities in the <a>Nordic countries</a>.
With its eight faculties and 57 departments, the University of Gothenburg is also one of the most wide-ranging and versatile universities in Sweden.
<p><a>thumb|KTB ()</a> The University of Gothenburg was founded as <em>G&#x00f6;teborgs h&#x00f6;gskola</em> (Gothenburg University College) in 1891.
<p>In 1971, the originally separate <a>Gothenburg School of Economics and Commercial Law</a> became part of the University of Gothenburg.
<p>The University of Gothenburg is a pronounced city university, that is most of its facilities are within the city centre of <a>Gothenburg</a>.
<p>The University of Gothenburg has awarded numerous <a>honorary doctorate</a>s to public figures and excellent academics, including: </p>

|logo = <a>170px</a> }} <strong>George Mason University</strong> (often referred to as <strong>GMU</strong> or <strong>Mason</strong>) is a <a>public university</a> based in <a>unincorporated</a> <a>Fairfax County</a>, <a>Virginia</a>, <a>United States</a>, south of and adjacent to the city of <a>Fairfax</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&quot;<a>City
The city of Fairfax purchased and donated  of land to the University of Virginia for the college's new site,&lt;ref&gt;<a>A Brief History of George Mason University</a> George Mason University&lt;/ref&gt; which was referred to as the <a>Fairfax Campus</a>.
Renamed that day by the legislation, George Mason College became George Mason University.</p>
<p>In 1978, the George Mason University Foundation purchased the former Kann's department store in Arlington.
In March 1979 the Virginia General Assembly authorized the establishment of the George Mason University School of Law (GMUSL) - contingent on the transfer of the Kann's building to George Mason University.
<p>While George Mason University is young compared to established research universities in Virginia, it has grown rapidly, reaching an enrollment of 30,714 students in 2008.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
The George Mason University logo, originally designed in 1982, was updated in 2004.</p>
<p>The main campus of George Mason University is situated on  just south of the <a>City of Fairfax, Virginia</a> in central <a>Fairfax County</a>, approximately  west of <a>Washington, D.C.</a></p>

<p>{{Infobox University | name = Grinnell College | image = <a>150px</a> | motto = <em>Veritas et Humanitas</em> (<a>Latin</a>) | mottoeng =Truth and Humanity | established = 1846 | type = <a>Private</a> | affiliations = <a>Midwest Conference</a> | president = <a>Raynard S. --&gt; <strong>Grinnell College</strong> is a private <a>liberal arts college</a> in <a>Grinnell</a>, <a>Iowa</a>, <a>U.S.</a> known for its strong tradition of <a>social activism</a> and rigorous academic environment.&lt;ref
name=&quot;pc&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name = &quot;tljzhk&quot;&gt;<a>&quot;Grinnell College: Academics&quot;</a>, <em>The Princeton Review'.' Retrieved April 30, 2008.&lt;/ref&gt;
Bushnell Grinnell]]: founder of Grinnell Iowa and benefactor of Grinnell College.]]
The name of the corporation &quot;The Trustees of Iowa College&quot; remained, but in 1909 the name &quot;Grinnell College&quot; was adopted by the trustees for the institution.
<p>In 1882, Grinnell College was struck by a tornado &#x2014; then called a cyclone, after which the college yearbook was named.
<p><em>When Grinnell College framed its charter in the Iowa Territory of the United States in 1846, it set forth a mission to educate its students &quot;for the different professions and for the honorable discharge of the duties of life.&quot;
<p><a>thumb|right|John H. T. Main Residence Hall</a> Grinnell College is nationally recognized as a leading undergraduate institution.
The College has been consistently ranked in the top 18 liberal arts colleges in the nation since the publication began in 1983.&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;U.S. News Rankings Through the Years&quot;</a>, <em>Chronicle of Higher Education</em>&lt;/ref&gt;   In 2009, Grinnell College was ranked by <a>The Princeton Review</a> as one of the Top 10 best values in private colleges.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Grinnell College graduates enjoy a high acceptance rate to law school; over 46% of all applications submitted by students have been accepted by law schools.&lt;ref&gt;Grinnell
evaluations, notable alumni, student debt, percentage of students graduating in four years, and the number of students or faculty receiving prestigious awards), Grinnell College has a comparatively lower rank of 107th best school overall, one behind <a>Wells College</a> and one in front of <a>Virginia Military Institute</a>.
<p>The academic program at Grinnell College emphasizes active learning and one-on-one interactions between faculty members and students.
<p>Grinnell College expects all students to possess significant academic achievements.
<p>Despite the growing trend of U.S. students taking five or more years to finish an undergraduate degree, Grinnell College is strongly oriented towards students being enrolled full time in exactly eight consecutive semesters at the college, although exceptions are available for medical issues and other emergencies.&lt;ref&gt;Grinnell

<p>Grinnell College's admissions selectivity rank according to <a>The Princeton Review</a> is a 95 out of 99.&lt;ref&gt;<a>The Princeton Review</a>.

<p>Grinnell College is one of a few dozen US colleges that maintain <a>need-blind admission</a>s and meets the full demonstrated financial need of all U.S. residents who are admitted to the college.&lt;ref
Grinnell College's basketball team attracted ESPN due to the team's <a>run and gun</a> style of playing basketball, known in Grinnell simply as &quot;The System.&quot;
Grinnell College is located in the town of <a>Grinnell, Iowa</a>, halfway between <a>Des Moines</a> and <a>Iowa City</a>.

<p>{{Infobox university | name           = Harvey Mudd College | image          = <a>150px|HMC Seal</a> | established    = 1955 | type           = <a>Private</a> | president      = <a>Maria Klawe</a> | city           = <a>Claremont</a> | state          = <a>CA</a> | country        = <a>USA</a> | undergrad      = 738 | faculty        = 83 | campus         = <a>Suburban</a>, 38 acres (0.15&nbsp;km&#x00b2;) | endowment      = $193.9
}} <strong>Harvey Mudd College</strong> is a private <a>residential</a> <a>liberal arts college</a> of <a>science</a>, <a>engineering</a>, and <a>mathematics</a>, located in <a>Claremont, California</a>.
The Bachelor of Science diploma received at graduation is issued by Harvey Mudd College.</p>
Harvey Mudd College was funded by Mudd's friends and family, and named in his honor.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p><a>thumb|left|300px|Harvey Mudd College entrance on Dartmouth Ave</a> Harvey Mudd College's mission is to educate <a>scientist</a>s, <a>engineer</a>s, and <a>mathematician</a>s to be well-versed in the <a>social sciences</a> and <a>humanities</a> so that they better understand the impact of their work on society.
<p>, Harvey Mudd College is tied for 14th with <a>Grinnell College</a>, <a>United States Military Academy</a>, and <a>Washington and Lee University</a> among liberal arts colleges in the <a>United States</a> as rated by the <a>U.S. News and World Report</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and as of 2010, is ranked second to <a>Rose-Hulman Institute of Technology</a> in <a>Terre Haute, Indiana</a> as the best undergraduate engineering program at a school whose highest degree is a bachelor's or master's&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url= <a>http://colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com/best-colleges/spec-engineering</a> |title=America's Best Colleges 2011: Best Undergraduate Engineering Programs (where doctorate not offered)|publisher=<a>U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>|accessdate=2011-01-09}}&lt;/ref&gt; by <a>U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>.
<p>Harvey Mudd College is said to be one of the few colleges in the US with very low grade inflation.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>In 1997, Harvey Mudd College became the sole American undergraduate-only institution ever to win 1st place in the <a>ACM International Collegiate Programming Contest</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;

<p><strong>Hunter College</strong>,  established in 1870 by Thomas Hunter, is a public university and one of the constituent colleges of the <a>City University of New York</a> (CUNY) system, located on <a>Manhattan</a>'s <a>Upper East Side</a>.&lt;ref
name=&quot;Undergraduate Catalog p.3&quot;&gt;Hunter College 2007-2010 Undergraduate Catalog, p.3&lt;/ref&gt; Hunter is a coeducational liberal arts and sciences college that grants undergraduate, graduate, and doctoral degrees in more than 100 fields, and is nationally recognized for its diverse student body and academic excellence.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.hunter.cuny.edu/academics/index.shtml</a>, &quot;Academics at Hunter&quot;, 1/4/08&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;hunter.cuny.edu&quot;&gt;<a>http://www.hunter.cuny.edu/communications/pressroom/news/princeton-review-again-names-hunter-one-of-america2019s-best-colleges</a>&lt;/ref&gt;
<p><a>thumb|New York Normal College seen from Park Avenue (1874)</a> Hunter College has its origins in the 19th-century movement for <a>normal school</a> training which swept across the <a>United States</a>.
(Today, the <a>elementary school</a> and the <a>high school</a> still exist at a different location, and are now called the Hunter College Campus Schools.)</p>
<p><a>thumb|The North Building (left) was added in the 1930's on the previous gardens facing Park Avenue and destroying a large part of the original building (right), today Thomas Hunter Hall</a> <a>thumb|North Building at Park Avenue (2010)</a> In 1914 the Normal College became Hunter College in honor of its first president.
By 1920, Hunter College had the largest enrollment of women of any municipally financed college in the United States.
<p>The late 1930s saw the construction of Hunter College in the Bronx (later known as the Bronx Campus).
In Spring 1969, Hunter College established Black and Puerto Rican Studies (now called Africana/Puerto Rican and Latino Studies).
<p>Today, Hunter College is a comprehensive teaching and research institution.
Hunter College is anchored by its main campus at East 68th Street and Lexington Avenue, a modern complex of three towers &mdash; the East, West, and North Buildings &mdash; and Thomas Hunter Hall, all of which are interconnected by skywalks.
&quot;Hunter College Score Program&quot;, 12/1/07&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Hunter College owns and operates property outside of its main campuses, including the MFA Building, Roosevelt House, and the Hunter College Campus Schools.
&quot;Ellen Chesler Named Director of Women and Public Policy Initiative at Hunter College&quot;, 12/1/07&lt;/ref&gt; The Hunter Campus Schools&#x2014;Hunter College High School and Hunter College Elementary School&#x2014;are publicly funded schools for the intellectually gifted.

<p>Seattle University is dedicated to educating the whole person, to professional formation, and empowering leaders for a just and humane world.</p>
<p>The Hunter College student body is governed by the Undergraduate Student Government and the Graduate Student Association (GSA), both of which offer a wide range of activities and services.</p>
<h3>Hunter College Model United Nations</h3>
<p>Hunter College currently has two bodies that participate in <a>Model United Nations</a> Conferences.
<p>The Hunter College Model U.N. course was founded by President <a>Jennifer Raab</a> and Professor Pamela Falk in the Spring of 2008.
The Hunter College Model U.N. Team has partaken in debate at the <a>Global Model United Nations</a> (GMUN) hosted by the United Nations Department of Public Information in Geneva, <a>Oxford University International Model United Nations</a> (OxIMUN), Harvard National MUN (HNMUN), <a>National Model United Nations</a> (NMUN), Columbia University Model UN (CMUNNY), and Yale's Security Council Simulation (SCSY).
In January 2003, High school students from New York City, Canada, and India were delegates during the second annual Columbia Model United Nations Conference and Exposition (CMUNCE) at Hunter College.
<p>Hunter College has a campus radio station, WHCS, which once broadcasted at 590AM, but now solely online.&lt;ref&gt;<a>WHCS
<p>According to the CUNY website, &#x201c;Hunter offers what is widely considered the premier athletic program in the City University of New York.&#x201d;&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www1.cuny.edu/about/colleges/hunter.html</a>, &quot;Hunter College&quot;, 12/1/07&lt;/ref&gt; The Hunter College's intercollegiate athletic teams have had a legacy of success in recent decades at the conference, regional, and national levels of competition.

<p> <strong>Ithaca College</strong> is a <a>private college</a> located on the South Hill of <a>Ithaca, New York</a>.
Classifications: Ithaca College</a> Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching.&lt;/ref&gt;
The college has been ranked among the top ten master's universities in the <a>North</a> by U.S. News &amp; World Report every year since 1996.&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;U.S. News &amp; World Report America's Best Colleges&quot; Ranks Ithaca College in Top Ten - News Release - Ithaca College Office of Media Relations&lt;!-- Bot generated title --&gt;</a>&lt;/ref&gt;  For the 2010 rankings, the college was ranked 7 in this category.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Master's
<p>Ithaca College was founded as the Ithaca Conservatory of Music in 1892 when a local violin teacher, William Grant Egbert, rented four rooms and arranged for the instruction of eight students.
The college was originally housed in the <a>Boardman House</a>, that later became the Ithaca College Museum of Art, and it was listed on the <a>National Register of Historic Places</a> in 1971.&lt;ref
<p>The school attracts a multicultural student body with representatives from almost every state and from 78 foreign countries.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Office of Institutional Research - Institutional Research - Ithaca College</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Ithaca College's current campus was built in the 1960s on <a>South Hill</a>.
<p>Besides its Ithaca campus, Ithaca College also operates satellite campuses in <a>London, UK</a>; <a>Washington, D.C.</a>; <a>Los Angeles, CA</a> (James B. Pendleton Center); and <a>Antigua</a>.
<p>Ithaca College also operates direct enrollment exchange programs with several universities, including <a>Griffith University</a>, <a>La Trobe University</a>, <a>Murdoch University</a>, and <a>University of Tasmania</a> (Australia); <a>Chengdu Sport University</a> and <a>Beijing Sport University</a> (China); <a>University of Hong Kong</a>; <a>Masaryk University</a> (Czech Republic); <a>Akita International University</a> and <a>University of Tsukuba</a> (Japan); <a>Hanyang University</a> (Korea); <a>Nanyang Technological University</a> (Singapore); <a>University of Valencia</a> (Spain); and <a>J&#x00f6;nk&#x00f6;ping University</a> (Sweden).&lt;ref&gt;<a>Ithaca

<p><strong>James Madison University</strong> (also known as <strong>JMU</strong>, <strong>Madison</strong>, or <strong>James Madison</strong>) is a <a>public</a> <a>coeducation</a>al <a>research</a> <a>university</a> located in <a>Harrisonburg</a>, <a>Virginia</a>, <a>U.S.</a> Founded in 1908 as the State Normal and Industrial School for Women at Harrisonburg, the university has undergone four name changes until settling with James Madison University.&lt;ref
In 1976 the university's name was changed to James Madison University.&lt;ref
<p>James Madison University is considered &quot;More Selective&quot; by the Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching.
<p>Currently, James Madison University offers 108 degree programs on the bachelor's, master's, educational specialist and doctoral levels.
<p>On October 2, 2009, James Madison University was granted a chapter by the <a>Phi Beta Kappa</a> academic honor society.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Today, the campus of James Madison University has 111 major buildings on .&lt;ref
<p>Several new construction projects on the campus of James Madison University have been included in Governor Tim Kaine's $1.65 billion higher education bond package.
<p><a>thumb|200px|right|Students on the James Madison University quad</a></p>
James Madison University's athletic teams use the name &quot;Dukes&quot; in competition, with the <a>Duke Dog</a>, a gray bulldog dressed in a purple cape and crown, as the school's mascot.
<p>Most recently, James Madison University has used funds to create a new baseball and softball field complex by Memorial Hall.
<p><a>de:James Madison University</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x062c;&#x06cc;&#x0645;&#x0632; &#x0645;&#x062f;&#x06cc;&#x0633;&#x0648;&#x0646;</a> <a>ja:&#x30b8;&#x30a7;&#x30fc;&#x30e0;&#x30ba;&#x30fb;&#x30de;&#x30c7;&#x30a3;&#x30b9;&#x30f3;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:James Madison University</a> <a>fi:James Madisonin yliopisto</a> <a>zh:&#x8a79;&#x59c6;&#x65af;&#x00b7;&#x9ea6;&#x8fea;&#x900a;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox university |name= Kansas State University  |image= <a>210px</a> |motto= Rule by Obeying Nature's Laws |established= 1863 |type= <a>Public</a>, <a>State</a>, <a>Land-grant</a>, <a>University</a> |president= <a>Kirk H. Schulz</a> |city= <a>Manhattan</a> |state= <a>Kansas</a> |country= <a>U.S.</a> |students= 23,588 (Fall 2010)&lt;ref name = Enrollment&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |undergrad= 18,778&lt;ref name= Factbook&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |postgrad= 4,366 |faculty= 1,305&lt;ref name= Factbook/&gt; |endowment= <a>$</a>259.8
|}} <strong>Kansas State University</strong>, commonly shortened to <strong>K-State</strong>, is an institution of higher learning located in <a>Manhattan</a>, <a>Kansas</a>, in the <a>United States</a>.
<p>Kansas State University, originally named Kansas State Agricultural College, was founded on February 16, 1863, during the <a>American Civil War</a>, as a <a>land-grant institution</a> under the <a>Morrill Act</a>.&lt;ref
name=Griffin/&gt;  Finally, upon the third attempt on February 16, 1863, the state accepted Manhattan's offer to donate the Blue Mont College building and grounds and established the state's land-grant college at the site &#x2013; the institution that would become Kansas State University.&lt;ref
In 1959, the name changed again to Kansas State University of Agriculture and Applied Science to reflect a growing number of graduate programs.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Jon Wefald</a> assumed the presidency of Kansas State University.
The <a>Konza Prairie</a> is a native tallgrass prairie preserve located south of Manhattan, which is co-owned by <a>The Nature Conservancy</a> and Kansas State University and operated as a field research station by the department of biology.
<p>Kansas State University offers the Landon Lecture Series for students, faculty and the community.
Presently, both <a>U.S. Senators from Kansas</a> are graduates of Kansas State University.
<p>The main campus of Kansas State University in Manhattan covers .
<p>Kansas State University also offers Army ROTC (Reserve Officers' Training Corps) and Air Force ROTC programs.</p>

<p><a>de:Kansas State University</a> <a>es:Universidad Estatal de Kansas</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x0627;&#x06cc;&#x0627;&#x0644;&#x062a;&#x06cc; &#x06a9;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0632;&#x0627;&#x0633;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; d'&#x00c9;tat du Kansas</a> <a>it:Universit&#x00e0; dello Stato del Kansas</a> <a>ja:&#x30ab;&#x30f3;&#x30b6;&#x30b9;&#x5dde;&#x7acb;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:Kansas State University</a> <a>simple:Kansas State University</a> <a>ta:&#x0b95;&#x0bc7;&#x0ba9;&#x0bcd;&#x0b9a;&#x0bb8;&#x0bcd; &#x0bae;&#x0bbe;&#x0ba8;&#x0bbf;&#x0bb2;&#x0baa;&#x0bcd; &#x0baa;&#x0bb2;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb2;&#x0bc8;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb4;&#x0b95;&#x0bae;&#x0bcd;</a> <a>th:&#x0e21;&#x0e2b;&#x0e32;&#x0e27;&#x0e34;&#x0e17;&#x0e22;&#x0e32;&#x0e25;&#x0e31;&#x0e22;&#x0e41;&#x0e04;&#x0e19;&#x0e0b;&#x0e31;&#x0e2a;&#x0e2a;&#x0e40;&#x0e15;&#x0e15;</a> <a>tr:Kansas Devlet &#x00dc;niversitesi</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox university | name           = KAIST | image_name     = Seal of KAIST.png|200px
| tagline        = Education for the world, research for the future | established    = February 16, 1971 | type           = Government-run | president      = <a>Nam-Pyo Suh</a>  | city           = <a>Yuseong</a> | province       = <a>Daejeon</a>  | country        = <a>South Korea</a>  | faculty        = 526&lt;ref name=&quot;kaist&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; (as of September, 2009) | staff          = 322&lt;ref name=&quot;kaist&quot; /&gt; (as of January, 2008) &lt;!-- is this *teaching* staff as required by the template?
--&gt; | students       = 8,929&lt;ref name=&quot;kaist&quot; /&gt; (as of September, 2009) | undergrad      = 3,839&lt;ref name=&quot;kaist&quot; /&gt; (as of September, 2009) | postgrad       = 2,213&lt;ref name=&quot;kaist&quot; /&gt; (as of September, 2009) | doctoral       = 2,877&lt;ref name=&quot;kaist&quot; /&gt; (as of September, 2009) | other          =  | campus         = <a>Urban</a>&lt;br /&gt;1,432,882m&#x00b2; (Daedeok Campus)&lt;ref name=&quot;kaist&quot; /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;413,346 m&#x00b2; (Seoul Campus) | colors         =  | nickname       = | mascot         =  | fightsong      = | affiliations   = <a>AEARU</a>, <a>LAOTSE</a>, <a>AOTULE</a> | footnotes      =  | address        =  | telephone      =  | website        = <a>http://www.kaist.edu</a>
<p><strong>KAIST</strong> (formerly the <strong>Korea Advanced Institute of Science and Technology</strong>), is located in <a>Daedeok Science Town</a>, <a>Daejeon</a>, <a>South Korea</a>.
KAIST was established by the Korean government in 1971 as the nation's first research oriented science and engineering institution.
KAIST is one of the nation's most prestigious science and technology institutions.
The QS-The Times World University Rankings in the year of 2009 placed KAIST 69th in overall ranking and 21st in technology &amp; IT subject field in the world.</p>
<p>KAIST was founded with government funding and was initially staffed with a number of Korean engineering and science talents educated in the United States.
KAIST continues to be Korea&#x2019;s foremost center of strategic R&amp;D projects.
KAIST offers grants and fellowships to international students.</p>
<p>The President of KAIST,  <a>Nam Pyo Suh</a>, is an authority in axiomatic design technology.
<p>&lt;!--<a>thumb|left|240px|KAIST Fountain and Students Hall</a>--&gt; The University has for many decades, recruited faculty from overseas.
The current KAIST President <a>Nam Pyo Suh</a> taught for many years at <a>MIT</a>.
<p>{| class=&quot;wikitable&quot; |- | February 16, 1971   | Establishment of Korea Advanced Institute of Science (KAIS), Hongneung Campus, Seoul |- | March 5, 1973  | First entrance ceremony for the master&#x2019;s program  |- | August 20, 1975  | First graduation ceremony for the master&#x2019;s program  |- | September 12, 1975  | First entrance ceremony for the doctoral program  |- | August 19, 1978  | First graduation ceremony for the doctoral program  |- | December 31, 1980  | Establishment of Korea Advanced Institute of Science and Technology (KAIST) united with KIST  |- | December 31, 1984   | Establishment of Korea Institute of Technology, newly added bachelor degree course  |- | March 3, 1986   | First entrance ceremony for Korea Institute of Technology  |- | June 12, 1989  | KIST separated from KAIST   |- | July 4, 1989   | United with Korea Institute of Technology (move to Daedeok Campus)  |- | December 17, 1990  | First graduation ceremony for bachelor&#x2019;s program  |- | October 1, 1996 | Establishment of <a>Korea Institute of Advanced Study (KIAS)</a>  |- | May 4, 2004  | Foundation of the National Nanofab Center (NNFC) |- | January 1, 2008 | Name change to only <em>KAIST</em>, replacing the spelled-out name |- | March 1, 2009 | <a>Information and Communications University</a> (ICU) was merged into KAIST as <a>KAIST Information Technology Convergence Campus</a> |}</p>
<p>KAIST was established under the name of Korea Advanced Institute of Science (KAIS) under a special law on February 16, 1971, as the first research oriented graduate school in science and engineering in Korea.
In 1989, KAIST established the education/research system of special talents in science and engineering fields in bachelor, master and doctoral degrees.
<p><a>The University of Pennsylvania Band</a> has been a part of student life since 1897.
statue of [[Jang Young Sil]], a Korean Scientist, in front of science library, Daejeon campus]] KAIST has led other colleges and research institutions in Korea and was verified by the <a>ABET</a> assessment (graduate course is within 10% of top US college level) in 1992, evaluation of nationwide colleges by Joongang Ilbo (1995, 1998&#x2013;2001, 2006, 2008-2010: number one in overall rank, and evaluation of Asian colleges by Asiaweek (1999~2000: Number one in science and technology), Chosun Ilbo evaluation of Asian colleges(2009,overall rank number one in the nation, 7th in Asia, world university ranking of The Times newspaper(2008: 34th of Top 100 world university in Technology) and others.</p>
<p>Over the past 30 years, KAIST has produced 8,453 bachelors, 17,762 masters, 6,726 doctorate holders (doctors under 30 years of age were 2,920, 43.4%) giving a total of 32,941 alumni.
The famous scientific publications such as&#x300c;Nature&#x300d; (GB, July 1993) and &#x300c;Science&#x300d; (USA, October 1993) have assessed that, &#x201c;KAIST has the potential to be the world best level education institution.&#x201d;</p>
<p>It founded the National Nano Lab in 2002 and established the KAIST Institute in 2006.</p>
<p>The first act of President Suh upon his inauguration in July 2006 was to lay out the KAIST Development Plan.
The &#x2018;KAIST Development Five-Year Plan&#x2019; was finalized on February 5, 2007 by KAIST Steering Committee after a thorough examination.
The goals of KAIST set by Suh are to become one of the best science and technology universities in the world, and to become one of the top-10 universities by 2011.</p>
<p>In January 2008, the university dropped its full name, <em>Korea Advanced Institute of Science and Technology</em>, and changed its official name to only <em>KAIST</em>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>'KAIST'
Decides Not to Use Original Full Name</a>, KAIST announcement, January 10, 2008.&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Governed by a special law, KAIST has an autonomous and flexible academic system.
<p>KAIST has produced many doctors through the Integrated Master&#x2019;s and Doctoral program and Early Completion System.
<p>In an endeavor to take the initiative in developing information technology (IT) for the 21st century, KAIST is launching the new College of Information Science and Technology in 2008 by relocating the Departments of Electrical Engineering, Computer Science and Industrial and Systems Engineering from the College of Engineering and establishing the Department of Knowledge Service Engineering.
In 2009 when ICU merge into KAIST, Department of Information and Communications Engineering at ICU comes into College of Information Science and Technology.</p>
<p>The KAIST College of Information Science and Technology is aimed at nurturing creative leaders equipped to address the world's complex problems by creating and developing information technologies.
<p>The interdisciplinary major program at KAIST was founded on September 1, 2003.
<p>KAIST established the Graduate School of Management in March, 1996.
In 2006, The Graduate School of Management joined with the Graduate School of Finance and the Graduate School of Information &amp; Media Management to form KAIST Business School.</p>
<p>&lt;!--<a>thumb|right|240px|KAIST Campus Painting Map</a>--&gt; KAIST is located in the <a>Daedeok Research Complex</a> in the city of <a>Daejeon</a>, 150 kilometers south of the capital <a>Seoul</a>.
<p>KAIST has two campuses in <a>Daejeon</a> and one campus in Seoul.
<p>KAIST Daejeon campus (besides Daejeon Expo Park) has total twenty nine dormitories where all students wishing to reside can stay.
<p>KAIST Daejeon campus (besides Munji-Dong) <a>KAIST Information Technology Convergence Campus</a> has total two dormitories.One for undergraduate students and the other for graduate students.
<p><a>thumb|left|240px|KAIST Digital Science Library</a> KAIST digital science library was established in 1971 as KAIS library, and it went through a merge and separation process with KIST library.
<p>KAIST always does its best to provide optimal facilities to create a cozy atmosphere where students can complete their courses satisfactorily.</p>
<p>Seven KAIST Institutes (KIs) have been set up: the KI for the BioCentury, the KI for Information Technology Convergence, the KI for the Design of Complex Systems, the KI for Entertainment Engineering, the KI for the NanoCentury, the KI for Eco-Energy, and the KI for Urban Space and Systems.
KAIST is currently conducting research planned by the government and private businesses that are worth mounts as much as 100 billion won.
In terms of ownership of intellectual property rights, KAIST holds 1,591 domestic patents and 500 international patents so far.</p>
<p><a>KAIST Institute (KI)</a></p>
<p>Researchers at the <a>Korea Advanced Institute of Science and Technology</a> (KAIST) have developed an electric transport system (called <a>Online Electric Vehicle</a>,  OLEV)  where the vehicles get their power needs from cables underneath the surface of the road via <a>non-contact magnetic charging</a>, (where a power source is placed underneath the road surface and power is wirelessly picked up on the vehicle itself.
In July 2009 the researchers successfully supplied up to 60% power to a bus over a <a>gap</a> of  from a power line embedded in the ground using power supply and pick up technology developed in-house.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.gizmag.com/kaist-olev-electric-vehicle/12557/</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>In 2010 <a>QS World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked KAIST 79th overall in the world, coming 24th in Engineering &amp; IT.
KAIST was again recognized as a number one University in Korea by Joong Angh Ill Bo Review.
In the year of 2009, KAIST's department of industrial design has also been listed in the top 30 Design Schools by Business Week.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
KAIST ranked the best university in <a>Republic of Korea</a> and the 7th university in <a>Asia</a> in the Top 100 Asian Universities list, the first regional ranking issued by <a>THE-QS World University Rankings</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>In the Top 100 Asian Universities List, HKU won the first, KAIST 7th, SNU 8th(2009 &#xc544;&#xc2dc;&#xc544; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xd3c9;&#xac00; &#xd64d;&#xcf69;&#xb300; 1&#xc704;, &#xce74;&#xc774;&#xc2a4;&#xd2b8; 7&#xc704;, &#xc11c;&#xc6b8;&#xb300; 8&#xc704;)</a> <a>Chosun Ilbo</a> 2009.5.12.
The cluster is built around KAIST, Korea's leading technical university, Chungnam University, a group of government research institutes in applied technologies, corporate research centers and more than 900 venture companies.</p>
<p>The Times-QS World University Rankings 2009 - KAIST 69th overall, 21st in the field of Engineering/Technology &lt;references /&gt; <a>http://www.topuniversities.com/university-rankings/world-university-rankings/2009/results</a></p>

<p><strong>Kent State University</strong> (also known as <strong>Kent</strong>, <strong>Kent State</strong>, and <strong>KSU</strong>) is a <a>public</a> research <a>university</a> located in <a>Kent, Ohio</a>, <a>United States</a>.
What would become Kent State University was established in 1910 as an institution for training public school teachers.
journal |last= Johnson|first= Christopher |date= 1 August 2005|title= Liquid Crystal Institute blazes new trails at Kent State|journal= Inside Business|publisher=Great Lakes Publishing |url= <a>http://www.highbeam.com/doc/1G1-160029070.html</a>|accessdate=2009-09-23 |quote= ...the world's No. 1 liquid crystal research center is at Kent State University: the Liquid Crystal Institute (LCI).}}&lt;/ref&gt;
|work= Kent State University Special Collections and Archives |publisher= Kent State University|accessdate=23 September 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p><a>thumb|left|200px|Kent State Gateway Arch on Kent Campus</a> Kent State University is an eight-campus system in northeastern Ohio, with the main administrative center in <a>Kent</a>.
Within the Kent State University system, the main campus is officially referred to as the &quot;Kent Campus&quot;.&lt;ref
The university also operates the 18-hole Kent State Golf Course and Centennial Research Park just east of campus in <a>Franklin Township</a> and the  <a>Kent State University Airport</a> in <a>Stow</a>.</p>
In addition to the Salem Campus, Kent State University Salem owns and operates the old Salem Middle School called the &quot;City Center&quot; in which administrative offices, classes, and student services are located.</p>
<p> The Stark Campus is the largest regional campus of Kent State University, serving around 10,300 students each year (5,300 in academic programs, 5,000 in executive and graduate education).
<p>::<em>See also: <a>Kent State University Airport</a>.</em></p>
  <li>Kent State University is one of few universities with graduate programs in Information Architecture and Knowledge Management (IAKM [<a>http://iakm.kent.edu/</a>])
<li><em><a>Fusion Magazine (Kent State University)</a></em> is published twice a year by KSU students in print and on the Internet.
<a>Fusion Magazine (Kent State University)</a> addresses sexual minority issues within the general population using illustrative photo essays and in-depth feature articles.</li>
<p><a>thumb|left|225px| May 4 Memorial at Night</a> The Kent State University Press is the publishing arm of Kent State University.

<p>{{Infobox University |native_name= Lunds universitet |name= Lund University |latin_name= Universitas Lundensis <em>or</em> Universitas Gothorum Carolina.
The lion in Lund University's seal holds a book in one hand, and a sword in the other.&lt;/ref&gt;
|established= 1666 |type= Public |city=  <a>Lund</a> |country= <a>Sweden</a> |image_name= Lund University seal.svg
|state= <a>Scania</a> |staff= 5,300 total (including non-scientific)  |students     = 46,000 (<a>FTE</a>, 2009)&lt;ref&gt;<a>Swedish Higher Education Authority (<em>H&#x00f6;gskoleverket</em>) - Annual report 2010 (Swedish), page 106ff</a>&lt;/ref&gt; |undergrad=  |doctoral= 3,200 |website= <a>http://www.lunduniversity.lu.se</a> |affiliations= <a>Universitas 21</a>&lt;br/&gt; <a>LERU</a>&lt;br/&gt; <a>EUA</a>&lt;br/&gt; <a>ASAIHL</a> |head_label=<a>Rector magnificus</a> and <a>Vice Chancellor</a> |head= Prof. <a>Per Eriksson</a> |campus= Urban }} <strong>Lund University</strong> (), located in <a>Lund</a> in the province of <a>Scania</a>, <a>Sweden</a>, is one of northern Europe's most prestigious <a>universities</a>&lt;ref&gt;<a>New Partnership with Swedish University: Lund University</a>&lt;/ref&gt; and one of <a>Scandinavia</a>'s largest institutions for education and research&lt;ref name=&quot;euro-scholars&quot;&gt;<a>Lund University, Sweden</a>, <em>Euro Scholars</em> Website&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;solander&quot;&gt;<a>Lund University</a>, <em>The Solander Program</em> Website&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;oeacademy&quot;&gt;<a>Universities in the &#x00d8;resund Region</a>, <em>&#x00d8;resund Entrepreneurship Academy</em> Website&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>Welcome to Lund University</a>&lt;/ref&gt;, frequently ranked among the world's top 100 universities&lt;ref&gt;<a>Top 200 Universities</a>, Website of <em>QS Top Universities</em>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a>'s <a>Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> - <a>2007</a>, <a>2006</a>, <a>2005</a>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>The Complete List: The Top 100 Global Universities</a>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;[<a>http://www.timeshighereducation.co.uk/world-university-rankings/2010-2011/top-200.html</a>]&lt;/ref&gt;.
<p>Lund University has eight <a>faculties</a>&lt;ref&gt;<a>Organisation</a>&lt;/ref&gt;, with additional campuses in the cities of <a>Malm&#x00f6;</a> and <a>Helsingborg</a>, with 27,780 students in more than 274 different programmes and 2000 separate courses.
<p>After the <a>Treaty of Roskilde</a> in 1658, the <a>Scanian lands</a> came under the possession of the Swedish Crown, which quickly founded the Lund University in 1666 as the means of Swedification.
The name was in some formal use until the late 19th century, when Lund University became the widespread denomination.</p>
name=Andersson&gt;<a>Lund University Medical Faculty</a> Hedda Andersson (1861-1950)&lt;/ref&gt; Hilma Borelius was the first woman who finished a doctorate in Lund, in 1910.
In 1992 <a>Boel Flodgren</a>, Professor of Business Law, was appointed <a>rector magnificus</a> (or, strictly speaking, <em>rectrix magnifica</em>) of Lund University.
<p>Lund University is internationally known as Scandinavia's largest research university.&lt;ref
Notable exchangees include United States Supreme Court Justice <a>Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a>, who spent time at Lund University in the 1960s conducting research.&lt;ref&gt;Linda,
<p>Lund University is also organised into more than 20 institutes and research centres [<a>http://www.lunduniversity.lu.se/o.o.i.s/24893</a>], such as</p>
<p><a>thumb|University Library</a> Lund University library was established in 1666 at the same time as the university and is one of Sweden's oldest and largest.

<p><a>ca:Universitat de Lund</a> <a>da:Lunds Universitet</a> <a>de:Universit&#x00e4;t Lund</a> <a>et:Lundi &#x00dc;likool</a> <a>es:Universidad de Lund</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; de Lund</a> <a>ga:Ollscoil Lund</a> <a>ko:&#xb8ec;&#xb4dc; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xad50;</a> <a>hi:&#x0932;&#x0941;&#x0902;&#x0921; &#x0935;&#x093f;&#x0936;&#x094d;&#x0935;&#x0935;&#x093f;&#x0926;&#x094d;&#x092f;&#x093e;&#x0932;&#x092f;</a> <a>id:Universitas Lund</a> <a>la:Universitas Lundensis</a> <a>lt:Lundo universitetas</a> <a>arz:&#x062c;&#x0627;&#x0645;&#x0639;&#x0629; &#x0644;&#x0648;&#x0646;&#x062f;</a> <a>nl:Universiteit van Lund</a> <a>ja:&#x30eb;&#x30f3;&#x30c9;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:Lunds universitet</a> <a>pnb:&#x0644;&#x0646;&#x0688; &#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0646;&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0631;&#x0633;&#x0679;&#x06cc;</a> <a>pl:Uniwersytet w Lund</a> <a>pt:Universidade de Lund</a> <a>ru:&#x041b;&#x0443;&#x043d;&#x0434;&#x0441;&#x043a;&#x0438;&#x0439; &#x0443;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442;</a> <a>simple:Lund University</a> <a>fi:Lundin yliopisto</a> <a>sv:Lunds universitet</a> <a>zh:&#x9686;&#x5fb7;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a></p>
<p>The 2008 edition of &quot;America's Best Colleges&quot;, compiled by U.S. News &amp; World Report, ranked Northern Michigan University as a Master's (Midwest) - Third Tier institution.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>  {{Infobox university |name = Massachusetts Institute of Technology |image = <a>200px</a> |motto = <em>Mens et Manus</em> |mottoeng = Mind and Hand&lt;ref name=&quot;seal&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |established = 1861 (opened 1865) |type = <a>Private</a> |calendar = 4-1-4 |president = <a>Susan Hockfield</a> |chancellor = Phillip Clay |provost = <a>L.
<a>billion</a>&lt;ref name=&quot;Endowment&quot;/&gt; |logo = <a>center|85px|MIT Logo</a> |affiliations = <a>NEASC</a>, <a>AAU</a>, <a>COFHE</a>, <a>NASULGC</a>}}  The <strong>Massachusetts Institute of Technology</strong> (<strong>MIT</strong>) is a private research institute located in <a>Cambridge</a>, <a>Massachusetts</a>. MIT has five schools and one college, containing a total of 32 academic departments, with a strong emphasis on scientific and technological research.</p>
In 1861, The Commonwealth of Massachusetts approved a charter for the incorporation of the &quot;Massachusetts Institute of Technology and <a>Boston Society of Natural History</a>&quot; submitted by <a>William Barton Rogers</a>.
<em>Geology at MIT 1865-1965: A History of the First Hundred Years of Geology at Massachusetts Institute of Technology.

<p>{{Infobox University |name = Millsaps College |image = <a>Image:Millsaps College.png</a>
<p><strong>Millsaps College</strong> is a private <a>liberal arts college</a> located in <a>Jackson, Mississippi</a>.
Millsaps College is featured in Loren Pope&#x2019;s <em>Colleges That Change Lives</em> and is one of only 24 private colleges nationwide named a <em>Best Buy</em> in the 2010 edition of Fiske&#x2019;s <em>Top Financial Finds on the College Tuition Market.</em></p>
<p><a>thumb|left|Millsaps College campus.</a>
<p><a>thumb|right|Mausoleum on the campus of Millsaps College, Jackson, Mississippi, containing the graves of Major Reuben Webster Millsaps and his wife.</a></p>
George Marion Harmon (1978-2000) - After 22 years of leading Millsaps College, Dr. Harmon announced his resignation in the Spring of 1999.
His last day as president of Millsaps College was June 30, 2000.&lt;ref
<p> {{Infobox university | name = Macquarie University | motto = <em>And gladly teche</em>&lt;br&gt;from the general Prologue to The Canterbury Tales, Geoffrey Chaucer c.1400 | established = 1964 | type = <a>Public</a> | endowment = AU$563m&lt;br /&gt;&lt;small&gt;(31 December 2008)&lt;/small&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; | chancellor = <a>The Hon.
| image = <a>center|The Arms of Macquarie University|170px</a> | coor= | logo = <a>230px</a> }} <strong>Macquarie University</strong> is an <a>Australian</a> <a>public</a> teaching and <a>research university</a> located in <a>Sydney</a>, with its main campus situated in <a>Macquarie Park</a>.
<p>Macquarie University also has the largest student exchange programme in Australia.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Also affiliated with the university are several research centres, schools and institutes including the <a>Macquarie Graduate School of Management</a>, Australian Proteome Analysis Facility, the Institute of Human Cognition and Brain Science, the <a>Macquarie University Research Park</a> and the <a>Macquarie University Hospital</a>.</p>
<p>Macquarie University's linguistics department developed the <a>Macquarie Dictionary</a>, the copyright on which it still owns.</p>
<p><a>thumb|left|First Students at Macquarie University</a>The idea of founding a third university in Sydney was flagged in the early 1960s when the <a>New South Wales Government</a> formed a committee of enquiry into higher education to deal with a perceived emergency in university enrolments in <a>New South Wales</a>.
<p>Macquarie University was formally established in 1964 with the passage of the Macquarie University Act 1964 by the New South Wales parliament.
The fledgling Macquarie University Council decided that planning for the campus would be done within the university, rather than by consultants, and this led to the establishment of the architect-planners office.&lt;ref
In their book <em>Liberality of Opportunity</em>, Bruce Mansfield and Mark Hutchinson describe the founding of Macquarie University as &#x2018;an act of faith and a great experiment&#x2019;.&lt;ref&gt;Liberality of Opportunity, Mansfield and Hutchinson, p. 317&lt;/ref&gt; An additional topic considered in this book is the <a>science reform movement</a> of the late 1970s that resulted in the introduction of a named science degree, thus facilitating the subsequent inclusion of other named degrees in addition to the traditional BA.&lt;ref&gt;Liberality of Opportunity, Mansfield and Hutchinson, pp.
The first Vice-Chancellor of Macquarie University was Alexander George Mitchell, who held the position until December 1975, when he was replaced by Edwin Webb, who served until 1986.
name=&quot;theaust&quot;/&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>They call her the grand dame of Sydney's Macquarie University but as Di Yerbury left her post as Vice Chancellor, controversy descended.
<em>Northern Michigan University: The First 75 Years.</em>
<p>During 2007, Macquarie University faced a restructuring of its student organisation after an audit raised questions about management of hundreds of thousands of dollars in funds by student organisations&lt;ref name=&quot;audit&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; At the centre of the investigation was Victor Ma, president of the Macquarie University Students' Council, who had previously been involved in a high-profile case of student election fixing at the <a>University of Sydney</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
The Federal Court ordered on 23 May 2007 that Macquarie University Union Ltd be wound up.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url = <a>http://www.austlii.edu.au/au/cases/cth/federal_ct/2007/844.html</a>
|title = Macquarie University v Macquarie University Union Limited (No 2) [2007] FCA 844 |date= 2007-05-23 |accessdate = 2008-01-25 |publisher = Commonwealth of Australia and Federal Court of Australia }}&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Following the dissolution of Macquarie University Union Ltd, the outgoing student organisation was replaced with a new wholly owned subsidiary company of the university, known as U@MQ Ltd.
The new student organisation originally lacked a true student representative union; however, following a complete review and authorisation from the university Council, a new student union known as Macquarie University Students Association (MUSRA) was established in 2009.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.uatmq.com.au/umqwr/_assets/main/lib90019/musra%20charter_final_24jun09.pdf</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<a>thumb|300px|Macquarie University Lake</a> The university introduced a new curriculum in January 2010 that was intended to broaden the knowledge of graduates and to include study in general education subjects.
<p>The <a>University Council</a> is the governing authority of the university under the <em>Macquarie University Act 1989</em>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p><a>thumb|left|140px|Information Board at Central Courtyard</a> Macquarie University's main campus is located about  north-west of the <a>Sydney CBD</a> and is set on 126&nbsp;hectares of rolling lawns and natural bushland.
The university&#x2019;s first architect-planner was <a>Walter Abraham</a>, one of the first six administrators appointed to Macquarie University.
<p><a>thumb|E4A Building at Entrance to University</a>Today, Macquarie University is served by the <a>Macquarie University railway station</a>, which opened in 2009, as well as a bus interchange within the campus that provides close to 800 bus services daily.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Apart from its centres of learning, the campus features the <a>Macquarie University Research Park</a>, museums, art galleries, a sculpture park, an observatory, a sport and aquatic centre, a fauna park and also the private <a>Macquarie University Hospital</a>.
  <li><strong>Macquarie City Campus</strong>: Macquarie City Campus is a teaching campus of Macquarie University which associates with <a>Navitas</a>.
In mid 2007, the university opened the Macquarie City Campus in the <a>Sydney CBD</a>, offering Macquarie University&#x2019;s foundation studies, selected undergraduate and postgraduate degrees.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
  <li><strong>Macquarie Manly Campus</strong>: In association with Macquarie University, the <a>International College of Management, Sydney</a>, offers a two-year Diploma programme (only in Hospitality, Event and International tourism), an Associate Degree Programme and a three-year Bachelor of Business Administration Degrees specialised in Hospitality, Event, International tourism, Retail, Property, and Sports Management as well as graduate certificates and master programmes.
Bachelor and master degrees are awarded by Macquarie University and students have access to the university library for study and research.</li>
Macquarie University showed a significant drop in the 2007 <a>THES - QS World University Rankings</a> (From 2010 two separate rankings will be produced by the <a>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> and the <a>QS World University Rankings</a>).
<p>The <a>Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a>&#x2019;s <a>Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> in 2009 ranked Macquarie University as 7th in Australia (following <a>University of Western Australia</a> and <a>UNSW</a>), while the UK&#x2019;s <em><a>Times Higher Education Supplement</a></em> World University Rankings published in October 2009 ranked Macquarie 9th in Australia (behind the <a>University of Adelaide</a> and the <a>University of Western Australia</a>).&lt;ref
&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Macquarie University teachers also have received numerous awards and citations from the Carrick Institute for Learning and Teaching in Higher Education since it was established in 2004.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Macquarie
<p><a>thumb|Macquarie University Library</a> The <a>Macquarie University Library</a> was opened in 1967 and contains over 1.8 million items.
<p>Located on the western side of the campus is the <a>Macquarie University Sport and Aquatic Centre</a>.
<p>The <a>Macquarie University Research Park</a> offers opportunities for collaboration with leading companies.
<p>The Macquarie University Observatory was originally constructed in 1978 as a research facility but, since 1997, has been accessible to the public through its Public Observing Program.&lt;ref&gt;<a>The
Macquarie University Observatory</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The <a>Macquarie University Hospital</a> was completed in 2010 and is the most advanced medical facility in Australia.
<p>Macquarie University has two residential colleges on its campus, <a>Dunmore Lang College</a> and <a>Robert Menzies College</a>, both founded in 1972.
In addition to these residential colleges is the <a>Macquarie University Village</a> which contains over 890 rooms inside multiple two storey townhouses and apartment block.</p>
Marquette, Michigan: Northern Michigan University Press, 1975.
<p> <a>thumb|Campus Hub</a> ;Campus Experience :Campus Experience was officially launched in January 2008 under the name of U@MQ, and is the new organisation that manages Macquarie University&#x2019;s non-academic services of food and retail, sport and recreation, student groups, child care, and entertainment.
<p>;2SER :Macquarie University has its own community radio station on campus, <a>2SER FM</a>.
The station is jointly owned by Macquarie University and <a>UTS</a> and broadcasts its programmes on the frequency 107.3 FM.</p>
<p>;Conception Day :Macquarie University students celebrate Conception Day each year to &#x2013; according to legend - commemorate the date of conception of Lachlan Macquarie, as his birthday fell at the wrong time of year for a celebration.
<p>The <a>Sydney Institute of Business and Technology</a> (SIBT) operates on the Macquarie University campus, offering Foundation Studies (Pre-University) and University-level Diplomas.
<p>The <strong>Centre for Macquarie English</strong> (<a>CME</a>), formerly known as NCELTR (National Centre for English Language Teaching and Research), is the English-language centre that offers a range of specialised, direct entry English programmes that are approved by Macquarie University.&lt;ref&gt;<a>The

<p><a>de:Macquarie University</a> <a>es:Universidad de Macquarie</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; Macquarie</a> <a>ko:&#xb9e5;&#xcffc;&#xb9ac; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xad50;</a> <a>id:Universitas Macquarie</a> <a>it:Universit&#x00e0; di Macquarie</a> <a>nl:Macquarie Universiteit</a> <a>ja:&#x30de;&#x30c3;&#x30b3;&#x30fc;&#x30ea;&#x30fc;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>pl:Macquarie University</a> <a>pt:Universidade Macquarie</a> <a>ru:&#x0423;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442; &#x041c;&#x0430;&#x043a;&#x043a;&#x0443;&#x043e;&#x0440;&#x0438;</a> <a>sr:&#x041c;&#x0430;&#x043a;&#x0432;&#x0430;&#x0440;&#x0438; &#x0443;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0437;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442;</a> <a>sv:Macquarie University</a> <a>tl:Macquarie University</a> <a>ta:&#x0bae;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bc1;&#x0bb5;&#x0bbe;&#x0bb0;&#x0bbf; &#x0baa;&#x0bb2;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb2;&#x0bc8;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb4;&#x0b95;&#x0bae;&#x0bcd;</a> <a>th:&#x0e21;&#x0e2b;&#x0e32;&#x0e27;&#x0e34;&#x0e17;&#x0e22;&#x0e32;&#x0e25;&#x0e31;&#x0e22;&#x0e41;&#x0e21;&#x0e04;&#x0e04;&#x0e27;&#x0e2d;&#x0e23;&#x0e35;&#x0e48;</a> <a>tr:Macquarie &#x00dc;niversitesi</a> <a>vi:&#x0110;&#x1ea1;i h&#x1ecd;c Macquarie</a> <a>zh:&#x9ea5;&#x89ba;&#x7406;&#x5927;&#x5b78;</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox University |name          = Northern Michigan University |image         =<a>200px|Northern Michigan University Seal</a>  |motto         = Northern.
<p><strong>Northern Michigan University</strong> is a 4 year college <a>public university</a> established in 1899 located in <a>Marquette</a>, in <a>Michigan</a>'s <a>Upper Peninsula</a>.
With a population of nearly 10,000 undergraduate and graduate students, Northern Michigan University is the Upper Peninsula's largest university.</p>
<p>Northern Michigan University, NMU for short, was established in 1899 by the <a>Michigan Legislature</a> as Northern State Normal School with the original purpose of providing teacher preparation programs in Michigan's then-wild and sparsely populated <a>Upper Peninsula</a>.
  <li>Northern's multi-purpose student events center, funded in part by a $2 million donation by 1971 alumnus John Berry, opened in 1999 and is the home of the Northern Michigan University hockey and men's and women's basketball teams.
<p><a>thumb|right|250px|University Center</a> Northern Michigan University is accredited by the <a>North Central Association of Colleges and Secondary Schools</a>.&lt;ref&gt;[<a>http://www.ncahlc.org/index.php?option=com_frontpage&amp;Itemid=113</a> &lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Northern Michigan University's vision for education in the 21st century is a learning environment that embraces technology to enhance student access, promote the development of independent learners and encourage greater student-faculty communication and collaboration.
<p>The <a>United States Olympic Education Center</a> on the campus of Northern Michigan University is one of four Olympic training centers in the country and the only one located on a college campus.
The Superior Edge encompasses a wide range of in- and out-of-classroom experiences that will provide Northern Michigan University students with a distinct advantage by better preparing them for careers, lifelong learning, graduate school, and life as engaged citizens.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The North Wind began in 1972 as Northern Michigan University's first independent, student newspaper.
<p><a>WUPX</a> is Northern Michigan University's non-commercial, student run, radio station.
<p>The Associated Students of Northern Michigan University (ASNMU) is made up of three distinct branches: Executive, Legislative and Judicial.
  <li><a>David Prychitko</a>, noteworthy researcher, author and professor of <a>Economics</a> at Northern Michigan University.
<p><a>Category:Northern Michigan University</a> <a>Category:Universities and colleges in Michigan</a> <a>Category:North Central Association of Colleges and Schools</a> <a>Category:American Association of State Colleges and Universities</a> <a>Category:Educational institutions established in 1899</a> <a>Category:Upper Peninsula of Michigan</a></p>

<p><strong>BI Norwegian School of Management</strong> () is the largest business school in <a>Norway</a> and the second largest in all of Europe.
<p>BI Norwegian School of Management was founded in 1943 by <a>Finn &#x00d8;ien</a> as 'Bedrift&#x00f8;konomisk Institut' (), hence the abbreviation'BI'.
