<p> {{Infobox university |name         =Ohio State University |image_name   = Seal of the Ohio State University.png
<p><strong>Ohio State University</strong>, commonly referred to as <strong>Ohio State</strong> or <strong>OSU</strong>, is a <a>public</a> research university located in <a>Columbus, Ohio</a>.
It also includes regional campuses in [[Ohio State University, Lima Campus|Lima]], [[Ohio State University, Mansfield Campus|Mansfield]], [[Ohio State University, Marion Campus|Marion]], [[Ohio State University, Newark Campus|Newark]], and [[Ohio State University Agricultural Technical Institute|Wooster]].</pre>
<p> Ohio State University was founded in 1870 as a <a>land-grant university</a> in accordance with the <a>Morrill Act of 1862</a> under the name of Ohio Agricultural and Mechanical College.
In 1878, and in light of its expanded focus, the college permanently changed its name to the now-familiar &quot;Ohio State University&quot;, with &quot;The&quot; as part of its official name,&lt;ref&gt;<a>Ohio State University Timeline 1870 TO 1899</a>, Ohio State University Archives&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Ohio 3335&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; although the state code that declares the &quot;The&quot; neglects it in sections&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; including in the title of the section that originally declares it.&lt;ref
<p>Internationally, in 2010 <a>QS World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked Ohio State University 124th in the world, and 40th in the United States.
<p><a>thumb|right|200px|Kottman Hall: Home of the School of Environment and Natural Resources</a> <a>thumb|Drinko Hall: Home of Ohio State University Michael E. Moritz College of Law</a> Ohio State University comprises the following colleges and schools:</p>
<p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a>commencement</a> and <a>convocation</a>, and athletic games are: <em>Across the Field</em>, Ohio State University <a>fight song</a> and &quot;Buckeye Battle Cry&quot;.</p>
Ohio Union is dedicated to the enrichment of the student experience, on and off Ohio State University campus.
It was a center of student life at Ohio State University for more than 50 years, providing facilities for student activities, organizations and events, and serving as an important meeting place for campus and community interaction.
<p><a>Student organizations</a> at Ohio State University provide students with opportunities to get involved in a wide variety of interest areas including <a>academic</a>, <a>social</a>, <a>religious</a>, <a>artistic</a>, <a>service-based</a>, <a>diversity</a> and many more.
<p>At Ohio State University, there are three recognized student governments that represent their constituents.</p>
USG seeks to outreach to and work for the students at Ohio State University.</li>

<p><strong>Oberlin College</strong> is a selective private <a>liberal arts</a> college in <a>Oberlin, Ohio</a>, noteworthy for having been the first American institution of higher learning to regularly admit female and black students.
<h3>Presidents of Oberlin College</h3>
The experiment was a success, and now all but one of Oberlin College's dormitories are coed.
<p><a>thumb|right|Conservatory of Music at Oberlin College</a> The top-ranked <a>Oberlin Conservatory of Music</a> is located on the Oberlin College campus.
<p><a>Oberlin College Library</a> system is one of the largest and finest undergraduate libraries in the nation.
Bot generated title --&gt;</a>&lt;/ref&gt;   In addition to the breadth of its holdings, the Oberlin College Library is recognized for its quality: it received the <a>Association of College and Research Libraries Excellence in Academic Libraries Award</a> in 2002, and in 2006 Director of Libraries Ray English was named the <a>ACRL</a>'s <a>Academic-Research Librarian</a> of the Year.
The entirely student-run Oberlin College Marching Band (OCMB), founded in 1998, performs at various sporting events including football games, women's rugby, and pep rallies throughout the year.
<p>Oberlin College is also home to the steel drum ensemble <a>Oberlin Steel</a>, formerly known as the Can Consortium.
<p>Oberlin College has demonstrated its commitment to the pursuit of <a>sustainability</a> on a  number of fronts.
Oberlin College Football Media Guide (web link: <a>Goyeo.com</a>,
The Oberlin College Men's Rugby team was founded in 1973, playing its first game against the Elyria Black River Rugby Club.
Oberlin, formed as the Oberlin College Rugby Club (OCRC), was sponsored by the Oberlin College Rathskeller, then the campus pub.
Since then, the Gruffs have continued to grow as a formal, chartered, club sports organization of Oberlin College.</p>

<pre>|name              = Occidental College
<p>}} [[Image:Occidental College in the 1920's.jpg|right|thumb|250px|Occidental
<p><strong>Occidental College</strong> is a selective, <a>private</a>, <a>coeducational</a> <a>liberal arts college</a> located in the <a>Eagle Rock</a> neighborhood of <a>Los Angeles, California</a>.
Founded in 1887, Occidental College, or &quot;<strong>Oxy</strong>&quot; as it is called by students and <a>alumni</a>, is one of the oldest liberal arts colleges on the <a>West Coast</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Occidental College was founded on April 20, 1887, by a group of <a>Presbyterian</a> clergy and laymen, including <a>James George Bell</a>.
<p>Art majors at Occidental College can take courses at the <a>Art Center College of Design</a> in Pasadena, one of the country&#x2019;s top-ranked art schools.
<p>Occidental College is one of the top colleges on the West Coast.
name=&quot;Occidental College Athletics&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
name=&quot;Occidental College Athletics&quot;/&gt;</p>
<p><a>da:Occidental College</a> <a>es:Occidental College</a> <a>fr:Occidental College</a> <a>ko:&#xc625;&#xc2dc;&#xb374;&#xd0c8; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xad50;</a> <a>ja:&#x30aa;&#x30af;&#x30b7;&#x30c7;&#x30f3;&#x30bf;&#x30eb;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>simple:Occidental College</a> <a>sv:Occidental College</a></p>
<p> {{Infobox university |name           = Purdue University |image_name     = Purdue University Seal.svg |image_size     = 150px |motto          = &lt;!--
<p>| Color1           = Old Gold | Color1Hex        = B1946C | Color2           = Black | Color2Hex        = 000000&lt;ref&gt; &lt;/ref&gt; |free_label     = <a>Athletics</a> |free           = 18 Division I / IA <a>NCAA</a> teams |mascot         = <a>Boilermaker Special</a> |nickname       = <a>Boilermakers</a> |affiliations   = <a>Purdue University System</a>&lt;br /&gt; <a>Association of American Universities</a>&lt;br /&gt; <a>Committee on Institutional Cooperation</a> |website        = <a>www.purdue.edu</a>
<p><strong>Purdue University</strong>, located in <a>West Lafayette</a>, <a>Indiana</a>, <a>U.S.</a>, is the <a>flagship university</a> of the six-campus <a>Purdue University System</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Purdue established the first <a>college credit</a> offered in <a>flight training</a>, the first four-year <a>bachelor's degree</a> in <a>aviation</a>, and the first university <a>airport</a> (<a>Purdue University Airport</a>).
On May 6, 1869, it was decided that the college would be founded near the city of <a>Lafayette</a> and legislators established the institution as Purdue University, in the name of the institution&#x2019;s principal benefactor.&lt;ref
<p>Purdue University is well known for its diverse majors in <a>aerospace</a>.
The <a>Purdue University Airport</a> was the first university-owned airport in the United States.
<p>In 2010, Purdue University received a $1.35 million grant from the <a>United States Air Force</a> to develop alternative fuels and test aircraft engines at a new facility.
<p>In 1930 Purdue became the first university in the country to offer college credit for flight training, and later became the first university to open its own airport, the <a>Purdue University Airport</a>.
<p>At one point, Purdue University owned and operated a <a>charter airline</a> operation under <a>FAR</a> part 121 simply called &quot;Purdue Airlines&quot;.
In fact, <a>Hugh Hefner</a>'s famous <a>Playboy</a> <a>DC-9</a> aircraft was leased from Purdue, and its permanent storage was at Purdue University.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>[[File:Purdue Engineering Fountain, angle.JPG|thumb|right|The [[Engineering Fountain]] at Purdue]] The Purdue Mall is the central quad of Purdue University.
Also near the Purdue Mall is Felix Haas Hall, which was constructed in 1909 as Memorial Gymnasium in memory of the 17 Purdue University football players, coaches, alumni, and fans who perished in the <a>Purdue Wreck</a> railroad accident on October 31, 1903.
<p>{| class=&quot;wikitable&quot; style=&quot;font-size:90%; width:100%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;&quot; |+ <strong>Colleges of Purdue University</strong> |- |<a>College of Agriculture</a>&lt;br/&gt;1869 |<a>College of Education</a>&lt;br /&gt;1908 |<a>College of Engineering</a>&lt;br/&gt;1876 |<a>College of Health and Human Sciences</a>&lt;br/&gt;1905 |<a>College of Liberal Arts</a>&lt;br/&gt;1953 |<a>College of Pharmacy</a>&lt;br/&gt;1884 |<a>College of Science</a>&lt;br/&gt;1907 |<a>College of Technology</a>&lt;br/&gt;1964 |} {| class=&quot;wikitable&quot; style=&quot;font-size:90%; width:100%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;&quot; |+ <strong>Engineering Schools of Purdue University</strong> |- |<a>School of Aeronautics and Astronautics</a> |Agricultural and Biological Engineering |<a>Weldon School of Biomedical Engineering</a> |School of Chemical Engineering |School of Civil Engineering |<a>School of Electrical and Computer Engineering</a> |- |School of Engineering Education |School of Industrial Engineering |School of Materials Engineering |School of Mechanical Engineering |School of Nuclear Engineering |Division of Construction Engineering and Management |Division of Environmental and Ecological Engineering |} {| class=&quot;wikitable&quot; style=&quot;font-size:90%; width:100%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;&quot; |+ <strong>Other Schools of Purdue University</strong> |- |<a>Krannert School of Management</a>* |School of Health Sciences |School of Nursing |<a>School of Veterinary Medicine</a>* |}</p>
The faculty and more than 400 research laboratories put Purdue University among the leading research institutions.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Purdue University is considered by the <a>Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a> to have &quot;very high research activity&quot;.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Purdue University generated a record $333.4 million in sponsored research funding during the 2007&#x2013;08 fiscal year with participation from <a>National Science Foundation</a>, <a>National Aeronautics and Space Administration</a>, and the U.S. departments of <a>Agriculture</a>, <a>Defense</a>, <a>Energy</a>, and <a>Health and Human Services</a>.&lt;ref
<p>Purdue University established the <a>Discovery Park</a> to bring innovation through multidisciplinary action.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
|title= Discovery Park at Purdue University: Engine for Academic and Commercial Growth |author= Buck, Charles; Sharma, Pankaj (2008) |accessdate= 2008-08-11}}&lt;/ref&gt; Purdue University's nanotechnology research program, built around the new Birck Nanotechnology Center in Discovery Park, ranks among the best in the nation.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p><a>thumb|left|Cary Quad and Spitzer Court at Purdue University</a> Purdue University operates fifteen separate <a>residence hall</a>s for its undergraduate and graduate students, including: Cary Quadrangle, <a>Earhart</a> Hall, First Street Towers, <a>Harrison</a> Hall, Hawkins Hall, Hillenbrand Hall, Hilltop Apartments, <a>McCutcheon</a> Hall, Meredith Hall, Owen Hall, Purdue Village, Shreve Hall, <a>Tarkington</a> Hall, <a>Wiley</a> Hall, and Windsor Halls.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
All cooperative houses are governed under the Purdue Cooperative Council which is led by Purdue University students who live in these houses.
<p>Purdue University hosts the nation's third largest <a>Greek community</a>, with approximately 5,000 students participating in one of the 46 men's fraternities or 29 women's sororities.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p><a>WBAA</a> is a <a>radio station</a> owned by Purdue University.
<p>W9YB is the <a>callsign</a> of the <a>Amateur Radio Club</a> at Purdue University.
<p><a>thumb|200px|Purdue Pete &#x2013; one of the most recognized symbols of Purdue University</a>  The moniker for the University's athletics teams has become a popular reference for all things Purdue.
Special]] - the official mascot of Purdue University]] --&gt; In the more than 130 years since the founding of the university, several mascots have emerged in support of the Boilermaker athletic teams, including: The <a>Boilermaker Special</a>, <a>Purdue Pete</a>, and more recently, Rowdy.</p>
<p>The <a>Boilermaker Special</a> has been the official mascot of Purdue University since 1940.
<p>As the unofficial mascot of Purdue Athletics, <a>Purdue Pete</a> is one of the most recognized symbols of Purdue University.</p>
<p>Purdue University adopted its school colors, <a>Old Gold</a> and Black, in the fall of 1887.
As on the older seal, the words &quot;Purdue University&quot; are set in the typeface Uncial.
<p> The official <a>fight song</a> of Purdue University, &quot;<a>Hail Purdue!</a>&quot;, was composed in 1912 by alumni Edward Wotawa (music) and James Morrison (lyrics) as the &quot;Purdue War Song&quot;.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;

<p>{{Infobox University |name = Reed College |image = <a>120px|Reed Griffin</a> |caption = Mascot of Reed College |established = 1908 |type = <a>Private</a> <a>liberal arts college</a> |president = <a>Colin Diver</a> |city = <a>Portland</a> |state = <a>Oregon</a> |country = <a>United States</a> |coor=  |mascot=<a>Griffin</a> |undergrad = 1,442 (1,402 full-time; 40 part-time)&lt;ref name=&quot;Headcount&quot; &gt;{{cite web | title = Historical Enrollment (Fall Census Headcount) | publisher = Institutional Research, Reed College | url = <a>http://web.reed.edu/ir/enrollment_hist.html</a> }}&lt;/ref&gt; |postgrad = 29  |faculty = 135 |endowment = $311.1 million (June 2009)&lt;ref&gt;National Association of College and University Business Officers (NACUBO), 2010.
<p><strong>Reed College</strong> is a <a>private</a>, <a>independent</a>, <a>liberal arts college</a> located in southeast <a>Portland, Oregon</a>.
<p><a>right|thumb|Reed College's Eliot Hall on a rare snowy day.</a>
The <strong>Reed Institute</strong> (the legal name of the college) was founded in 1908, and Reed College held its first classes in 1911.
<p>Reed has no fraternities or <a>sororities</a>, and few <a>NCAA</a> sports teams,&lt;ref&gt;One NCAA sports team at Reed has been the Reed College Ski Team, which as early as 1937, and as late as 1988, competed with the <a>University of Oregon</a> and other regional schools.
<p><a>right|thumb|The Reed College campus</a></p>
<p>{{main|Criticism of college and university rankings (North America)}} In 1995 Reed College refused to participate in the <a>U.S. News and World Report</a> &quot;best colleges&quot; rankings, making it the first educational institution in the United States to refuse to participate in college rankings.
According to an article in the college's alumni magazine, &quot;because of the decisive support expressed by Reed's faculty, students, and alumni for the three besieged teachers and for the principle of academic freedom, Reed College's experience with McCarthyism stands apart from that of most other American colleges and universities.
news | author=Munk, Michael | title=Oregon Tests Academic Freedom in (Cold) Wartime: The Reed College Trustees versus Stanley Moore | work=The Oregon Historical Quarterly | year=1996 }}&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
E. Doyle's 1920 Master Plan</a> The Reed College campus was established on a southeast <a>Portland</a> tract of land known in 1910 as Crystal Springs Farm, a part of the Ladd Estate, formed in the 1870s from original land claims.
At the same time the Willard House (donated to Reed in 1964), across from the college's main entrance at SE Woodstock and SE Reed College Place, was converted from faculty housing to administrative use.
<p><a>thumb|The Blue Bridge</a> The Reed College Canyon, a natural area and national wildlife preserve, bisects the campus, separating the academic buildings from many of the residence halls (the so called <em>cross-canyon halls</em>).
<p>The Reed College Co-op is a theme residence located in Garden House, after many years on the first floor of MacNaughton Hall.
The griffin was featured on the coat-of-arms of founder Simeon Reed&lt;ref name=&quot;coat-of-arms&quot; /&gt; and is now on the official seal of Reed College.</p>
The most common examples of &quot;Richmond Rose&quot; are the satin tapes securing the degree certificate inside a Reed College diploma.</p>
<p>An unofficial <a>motto</a> of Reed is &quot;Communism, Atheism, Free Love&quot;, and can be found in the Reed College Bookstore on sweaters, t-shirts, etc.
<p>Every year's <em>Reed College Student Handbook</em> (a manual on student life written by students, not to be confused with the <em>College Handbook</em>, which is written by college officials) contains a test called the &quot;Reed College Immorality Quotient&quot; that tests an individual's <a>immorality</a> on topics such as <a>sex</a>, <a>theft</a>, and <a>drug use</a>.</p>

<p><strong>William Marsh Rice University</strong> (commonly known as <strong>Rice University</strong>) opened in 1912 as <strong>The William Marsh Rice Institute for the Advancement of Letters, Science and Art</strong> is a <a>private</a> <a>coeducational</a> research university located in <a>Houston</a>, <a>Texas</a>, <a>United States</a>.

|logo = <a>center|225px</a> }} The <strong>Leland Stanford Junior University</strong>, commonly referred to as <strong>Stanford University</strong> or <strong>Stanford</strong>, is a <a>private research university</a> located in <a>Stanford, California</a>, United States with a strong emphasis on scientific, technological and social science research.
<p>The motto of Stanford University, selected by President Jordan, is &quot;<em>Die Luft der Freiheit weht.</em>&quot;
While some colleges dropped football entirely, a few, such as the University of California and Stanford University, replaced it with English rugby.

During 1955-85, solid state technology research and development at Stanford University followed three waves of industrial innovation made possible by support from private corporations, mainly Bell Telephone Laboratories, Shockley Semiconductor, Fairchild Semiconductor, and Xerox PARC.
In the College of Arts and Sciences, Seattle University's graduate program in psychology is notable as one of the few schools in the country to focus on <a>existential phenomenology</a> as a therapeutic method.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.seattleu.edu/artsci/</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>[[Image:Stanford Campus Aerial Photo.JPG|300px|thumb|right|An [[aerial photography|aerial photograph]] of the Stanford University campus]] Stanford University is located on an &lt;ref name=&quot;stanford_tours&quot;/&gt; campus on the <a>San Francisco Peninsula</a>, in the northwest part of the <a>Santa Clara Valley</a> (<a>Silicon Valley</a>) approximately  southeast of <a>San Francisco</a> and approximately  northwest of <a>San Jose</a>.
<p>Stanford University owns , which makes it the second largest university in the world in terms of contiguous area.
<p>Stanford University is actually its own <a>census-designated place</a> within <a>unincorporated</a> <a>Santa Clara County</a>, although some of the university land (including the <a>Stanford Shopping Center</a> and the <a>Stanford Research Park</a>) is within the city limits of Palo Alto.
<p> Contemporary campus landmarks include the <a>Main Quad</a> and <a>Memorial Church</a>, the <a>Cantor Center for Visual Arts</a> and <a>art gallery</a>, the <a>Stanford Mausoleum</a> and the <a>Angel of Grief</a>, <a>Hoover Tower</a>, the <a>Rodin</a> sculpture garden, the <a>Papua New Guinea Sculpture Garden</a>, the <a>Arizona Cactus Garden</a>, the <a>Stanford University Arboretum</a>, <a>Green Library</a> and <a>the Dish</a>.

And in 2009, the Sustainable Endowments Institute awarded Stanford University a grade of A- in its annual College Sustainability Report Card, making it one of the top fifteen of the 300 colleges and universities in the U.S. and Canada reviewed.
<p>Stanford University is a tax-exempt <a>corporate trust</a> owned and governed by a privately appointed 35-member <a>Board of Trustees</a>.&lt;ref
The Stanford trustees also oversee the <a>Stanford Research Park</a>, the <a>Stanford Shopping Center</a>, the <a>Cantor Center for Visual Arts</a>, <a>Stanford University Medical Center</a>, and many associated medical facilities (including the <a>Lucile Packard Children's Hospital</a>).&lt;ref name=&quot;FG facts&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The university is organized into seven schools: <a>School of Humanities and Sciences</a>, <a>School of Engineering</a>, <a>School of Earth Sciences</a>, <a>School of Education</a>, <a>Graduate School of Business</a>, <a>Stanford Law School</a> and the <a>Stanford University School of Medicine</a>.&lt;ref
<p>The <a>Associated Students of Stanford University</a> (ASSU) is the student government for Stanford University and all registered students are members.&lt;ref
<p><a>thumb|left|Walkway to the School of Education, near the Quad</a> Stanford University is a large, highly residential research university with a majority of enrollments coming from graduate and professional students.&lt;ref
name=&quot;Carnegie&quot;/&gt; Stanford University is accredited by the <a>Western Association of Schools and Colleges</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The Stanford University Libraries hold a collection of more than eight million volumes.
<p>[[Image:Stanford University campus from above.jpg|thumb|View from [[Hoover Tower]] observation deck of the Quad and surrounding area, facing west]] Stanford enrolled 6,602 undergraduate and 11,896 graduate students in 2009.&lt;ref
Stanford University is home to the <a>Cantor Center for Visual Arts</a> museum with 24 galleries, sculpture gardens, terraces, and a courtyard first established in 1891 by Jane and Leland Stanford as a memorial to their only child.

Mr. Wilson and his family have been long-time supporters of St. John Fisher College.</p>
At the time this accreditation was gained, all business programs at the College were brought together in 2003 to form St. John Fisher College&#x2019;s first professional school which was named the Bittner School of Business.</p>
<p>The school of Arts and Science is the largest school within St. John Fisher College and characterized by its ample degree programs and departments.
<p>The programs of the School of Arts and Sciences, serving both as a foundational component of the St. John Fisher College educational experience and as fields of specialized study, cultivate intellectual and ethical judgment and habits of thinking that prepare students to lead lives of integrity and thoughtful engagement in both the public and private spheres.
<p>Since 2000, St. John Fisher College has been home to the <a>Buffalo Bills</a>' <a>NFL</a> annual summer training camp.
  <li><a>John R. Cavanaugh</a> -  Professor Emeritus, St. John Fisher College</li>
<pre>|name              = Seattle University
|image_name        = Seattle University Seal.png
|logo              = [[File:Seattle University Wordmark.png|170px]]
<p>}} <strong>Seattle University (SU)</strong> is a Jesuit Catholic university located in the <a>First Hill</a> neighborhood of <a>Seattle</a>, <a>Washington</a>, USA.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.law.seattleu.edu/Office_and_Administration/Admission/Seattle_Living/Housing.xml</a> &quot;<strong>First Hill</strong>.
<a>U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>, in its &quot;Best Colleges 2011,&quot; ranked Seattle University 6th out of schools in the West that offer a full range of master's and undergraduate programs.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com/best-colleges/seattle-wa/seattle-university-3790</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>In 1948, Seattle College changed its name to Seattle University under Father Albert A. Lemieux, S.J.
In 1993, the <a>Seattle University School of Law</a> was established through purchase of the Law School from the <a>University of Puget Sound</a> in <a>Tacoma, Washington</a>.
[[Image:Seattle U St Ignatius 11.jpg|thumb|left|Interior, Chapel of St. Ignatius, Seattle University|Chapel of St. Ignatius, designed by [[Steven Holl]].]]
The Seattle University campus is  and is located on First Hill, near downtown Seattle, Wash.
Pastier, <a>Seattle University's Chapel of St. Ignatius</a>, HistoryLink.org
Accessed online 28 February 2007.&lt;/ref&gt;&#x2014;and a large glass sculpture in the PACCAR Atrium of Piggot Hall by <a>Tacoma, Washington</a> artist <a>Dale Chihuly</a>,&lt;ref name=Potterf&gt;Tina Potterf, <a>Home Is Where the Art Is</a>, <em>Seattle University Magazine</em> article reproduced on the Seattle University web site.
<p>Seattle University offers 61 bachelor's degree programs, 31 graduate degree programs and 27 certificate programs, plus a <a>law school</a> and a doctoral program in education.
A Seattle University education is estimated to cost $150,000, although much of this is covered by financial aid.&lt;ref&gt;<a>King 5 News</a>, King 5 News.
<p>Service-learning and social justice are components of the educational experience at Seattle University, which strives to &quot;empower leaders for a just and humane world.&quot;
<p>Seattle University's Albers School of Business and Economics, started in 1945, was named after the Albers family.
<p> <a>The Seattle University College of Arts and Sciences in</a> <a>Seattle</a>, <a>Washington</a> is the oldest undergraduate and graduate college affiliated with Seattle University, the Northwest's largest independent university.
<p>The vision of Seattle University is to be the premier independent university of the Northwest in academic quality, Jesuit Catholic inspiration, and service to society.</p>
<p>Between 1950 and 1971, Seattle University competed as a Division I independent school.
In the 1950s, the basketball team was a powerhouse with brothers Johnny and Eddie O&#x2019;Brien, who led Seattle University as the only team in history to defeat the world famous <a>Harlem Globetrotters</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Fifty years ago tonight, Seattle U. upset the mighty Globetrotters</a>, accessed January 24, 2008&lt;/ref&gt; In 1958, future <a>NBA Hall of Fame</a>r <a>Elgin Baylor</a> paced a men&#x2019;s basketball team that advanced to the <a>Final Four</a> and defeated top-ranked <a>Kansas State University</a> before losing to the <a>University of Kentucky</a>.
Seattle University was also a leader in the area of racial diversity, with an integrated squad known as &#x201c;the United Nations team.&#x201d;</p>
In the course of the 1960s, Seattle University produced more NBA players than any other school.
Seattle University would like to re-join the West Coast Conference, which is made up of other small, private, religiously affiliated institutions.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www2.seattleu.edu/d1/display.aspx?id=1558#5</a>&lt;/ref&gt; </p>

  <li><a>Seattle University's official student newspaper, The Spectator</a></li>

<pre>| name              = Syracuse University

<p>}} <strong>Syracuse University</strong> (also referred to as <strong>SU</strong>) is a private research university located in <a>Syracuse</a>, <a>New York</a>, <a>United States</a>.
Brief Report of Church Relatedness</em>: Syracuse University - INCORPORATION AND THE METHODIST CHURCH&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;William Joseph Whalen - Hospitals &amp; Universities&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;IAMSCU&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url = <a>http://public.gbhem.org/iamscu/search_results.asp?act=search_gen&amp;search_txt=Syracuse+University&amp;type=schools&amp;submit=GO</a>| title = Syracuse University |publisher = International Association of Methodist Schools, Colleges, and Universities (IAMSCU)|accessdate = 2007-06-30}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;SU &amp; UMC&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Syracuse was elected to the <a>Association of American Universities</a> in 1966.</p>
<p>Syracuse University athletic teams, known as the <a>Orange</a>, participate in 20 intercollegiate sports.
<p><a>thumb|left|400px|First Annual Class of Syracuse University.</a>
name=&quot;PioneerYears&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Greene&quot;/&gt; White pressed that the university should locate on the hill in <a>Syracuse</a> (the current location of Syracuse University) due to the city's attractive transportation hub, which would ease the recruitment of faculty, students, and other persons of note.
name=&quot;Greene&quot;&gt;{{cite book |author=Greene, John Edward |title=The Hill: an illustrated biography of Syracuse University (SU), 1870-present |publisher=Syracuse University Press |location=Syracuse |year=2000 |isbn=0-8156-0648-6}}&lt;/ref&gt; Rev. Daniel Steele, a former Genesee College president, served as the first administrative leader of Syracuse until its Chancellor was appointed.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Comstock intended Syracuse University and the hill to develop as an integrated whole; a contemporary account described the latter as &quot;a beautiful town ... springing up on the hillside and a community of refined and cultivated membership ... established near the spot which will soon be the center of a great and beneficent educational institution.&quot;&lt;ref
Dr. <a>Erastus Otis Haven</a>, Syracuse University chancellor and former president of the <a>University of Michigan</a> and <a>Northwestern University</a>, maintained that women should receive the advantages of higher education.
<p>The growth of Syracuse University from a small liberal arts college into a major comprehensive university were due to the efforts of two men, Chancellor <a>James Day</a> and <a>John Archbold</a>.
<p>John Dustin Archbold was a capitalist, philanthropist, and President of the Board of Trustees at Syracuse University.
He was a close friend of Syracuse University Chancellor James R. Day, and gave almost $6&nbsp;million to the University over his lifetime.&lt;ref
Archbold&#x2019;s ... is the president of the board of trustees of Syracuse University, an institution which has prospered so remarkably since his connection with it that its student roll has increased from hundreds to over 4,000, including 1,500 young women, placing it in the ranks of the foremost institutions of learning in the United States.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>After World War II, Syracuse University began to transform into a major research institution.
<p>[[Image:Library hc.JPG|thumb|250px|right|[[Hiram College Library]], designed to resemble a <a>Lake freighter</a>.
<p>From the early 1950s through the 1960s, Syracuse University added programs and staff that continued the transformation of the school into a research university.
In 1966, Syracuse University was admitted to the <a>Association of American Universities</a>, an <a>organization</a> of leading research <a>universities</a> devoted to maintaining a strong system of academic <a>research</a> and education.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>{| class=&quot;wikitable&quot; style=&quot;font-size:90%;width:100%;border:0px;text-align:center;line-height:120%;&quot; !colspan=&quot;12&quot;|<strong>Schools and colleges of Syracuse University (date of founding)</strong> |- !<strong>Undergraduate</strong> |colspan=&quot;2&quot;|College of Arts and Sciences&lt;br/&gt;1870 |University College&lt;br/&gt;1918 |rowspan=&quot;2&quot;|College of Visual and Performing Arts&lt;br/&gt;1873 |rowspan=&quot;2&quot;|<a>School of Architecture</a>&lt;br/&gt;1873 |rowspan=&quot;2&quot;|<a>School of Information Studies</a>&lt;br/&gt;1896 |rowspan=&quot;2&quot;|L.C.
<p><a>thumb|200px|right|SU's Flight 103 Memorial</a>  On December 21, 1988, 35 Syracuse University students were among the fatalities in the terrorist bombing of <a>Pan Am Flight 103</a> over <a>Lockerbie</a>, <a>Scotland</a>.
<p>That evening, Syracuse University went on with a <a>basketball</a> game just hours after the attack, for which it was severely criticized.&lt;ref
<p>In April 1990, Syracuse University dedicated a memorial wall to the students killed on Flight 103, constructed at the entrance to the main campus in front of the Hall of Languages.
<p>Since 2009, the Syracuse Center of Excellence in Environmental and Energy Systems, led by Syracuse University in partnership with <a>Clarkson University</a> and the <a>College Environmental Science and Forestry</a>, creates innovations in environmental and energy technologies that improve human health and productivity, security, and sustainability in urban and built environments.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The Syracuse University Bylaws also establish a University Senate with &quot;general supervision over all educational matters concerning the University as a whole....&quot;  The Senate consists of administrators, faculty, students and staff.&lt;ref
<p>The  College of Environmental Science and Forestry (ESF) operates its main academic campus immediately adjacent to Syracuse University.
ESF was founded in 1911 as the <a>New York State College of Forestry</a> at Syracuse University, under the leadership of Syracuse University Trustee <a>Louis Marshall</a>, with the active support of Syracuse University Chancellor Day.
The two schools share a common Schedule of Classes; students at both institutions may take courses at the other, and degrees from ESF bear the Syracuse University seal along with the State University of New York.
<p>The medical school was formerly a college within SU, known as the Syracuse University Medical School.
<h3>Former Syracuse University Satellite Colleges</h3>
Established in Endicott, New York, the college was a branch of Syracuse University.
Originally, Triple Cities College offered local students the first two years of their education, while the following two were spent at Syracuse University, but the inception of the college is dated at 1946 when students could first earn their degree entirely in the Binghamton branch.
<p> <a>Utica College</a>, an independent private university located in <a>Utica, NY</a>, was founded by Syracuse University in 1946.
Utica College became independent from SU in 1995, but still offers its students the option to receive a specialized bachelor's degree from Syracuse University through a mutual relationship between the two schools.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<a>Bachelor's degree</a>s are offered through the <a>Syracuse University School of Architecture</a>, the College of Arts and Sciences, the School of Education, the College of Human Ecology, the L.C. Smith College of Engineering and Computer Science,  the <a>School of Information Studies</a>, <a>Martin J. Whitman School of Management</a>, <a>S.I.
A 2008 survey in the Academic Ranking of World Universities places Syracuse University in the top 100 world universities in social sciences.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
The School of Information Studies offers <a>information management and technology</a> courses at the undergraduate level at Syracuse University.
<p>Syracuse University has 995 full time instructional faculty, 94 part-time faculty, and 440 <a>adjunct faculty</a>.
<h3>Syracuse University Press</h3>
<p>Syracuse University's main library is the Ernest S. Bird Library, which opened in 1972.
In July 2008, Syracuse University became the owner of the second largest collection of 78&nbsp;rpm records in the United States after the <a>Library of Congress</a> after a donation of more than 200,000 records.
<p>According to the <a>Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>, Syracuse University is a research university with a high level of research activity.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>[[File:Holden Observatory, Syracuse University.jpg|thumb|left|300px|
[[:en:Syracuse University|Syracuse University]].]]</p>
<p>Syracuse University has a diverse student population, representing all 50 US states and over 115 countries.
<a>Lou Reed</a> also hosted a free-format show on WAER during his time at Syracuse University; this free-format radio tradition at Syracuse is carried on by WERW.</p>
It is neither owned nor controlled by Syracuse University, but it does lease studio and transmitter facilities on Syracuse University property.</p>

The goals of the SA are to participate through a unified student voice in the formulation of Syracuse University rules and regulations.
<p>The graduate students at Syracuse University are represented by the Graduate Student Organization (GSO) while the law students at Syracuse University are represented by the Law Student Senate.
Each of the three organizations elects students to serve in the Syracuse University Senate, which also includes faculty and staff and is chaired by the SU Chancellor.</p>
<p><strong>University Union</strong> is a Syracuse University student organization.
Created in 1962 as the Syracuse University's Programming Board, the organization has gone through many transformations from student organization to &quot;official&quot; programming board back to student organization.</p>
<p> The Syracuse University <a>fraternity</a> and <a>sorority</a> system offers organizations that are members of the <a>Panhellenic Council</a> (NPC), the <a>Interfraternity Council</a> (IFC), the <a>National Association of Latino Fraternal Organizations</a>, the <a>National Multicultural Greek Council</a>, and the <a>National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> (NPHC).
<p>Current National Panhellenic Council Social Sororities and Syracuse University include Alpha Chi Omega, Alpha Epsilon Phi, Alpha Phi, Alpha Xi Delta, Delta Delta Delta, Delta Gamma, Gamma Phi Beta, Kappa Alpha Theta, Kappa Kappa Gamma, Phi Sigma Sigma, Pi Beta Phi, and Sigma Delta Tau.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://studentlife.syr.edu/greek/Panhellenic/index.aspx</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Current members of the Interfraternity Council at Syracuse University include Acacia, Alpha Chi Rho, <a>Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, Alpha Tau Omega, Delta Chi, Delta Kappa Epsilon, Delta Tau Delta, Phi Gamma Delta, Phi Kappa Psi, Phi Kappa Theta, Pi Kappa Alpha, Psi Upsilon, Sigma Alpha Epsilon, Sigma Alpha Mu, Sigma Chi, Sigma Phi Epsilon, Tau Kappa Epsilon, Theta Chi, and Zeta Beta Tau.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://studentlife.syr.edu/greek/IFC/ifc.aspx</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Syracuse University's sports teams have &quot;the Orange&quot; nickname since 2004, although the former names of Orangemen and Orangewomen are still used.

Bush</a> for their winning the <a>2008 National Collegiate Athletic Association Division I national championship</a>.]]</p>

Syracuse University decided to build a new stadium.

<p><a>az:Sirakuz Universiteti</a> <a>ca:Universitat de Syracusa</a> <a>cs:Syracuse University</a> <a>da:Syracuse University</a> <a>de:Syracuse University</a> <a>es:Universidad de Siracusa</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x0633;&#x06cc;&#x0631;&#x0627;&#x06a9;&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0632;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; de Syracuse</a> <a>ko:&#xc2dc;&#xb7ec;&#xd050;&#xc2a4; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xad50;</a> <a>id:Universitas Syracuse</a> <a>it:Syracuse University</a> <a>he:&#x05d0;&#x05d5;&#x05e0;&#x05d9;&#x05d1;&#x05e8;&#x05e1;&#x05d9;&#x05d8;&#x05ea; &#x05e1;&#x05d9;&#x05e8;&#x05e7;&#x05d9;&#x05d5;&#x05d6;</a> <a>nl:Universiteit van Syracuse</a> <a>ja:&#x30b7;&#x30e9;&#x30ad;&#x30e5;&#x30fc;&#x30b9;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:Syracuse University</a> <a>pt:Universidade de Syracuse</a> <a>simple:Syracuse University</a> <a>fi:Syracusen yliopisto</a> <a>ta:&#x0b9a;&#x0bbf;&#x0bb0;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bbf;&#x0baf;&#x0bc2;&#x0bb8;&#x0bcd; &#x0baa;&#x0bb2;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb2;&#x0bc8;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb4;&#x0b95;&#x0bae;&#x0bcd;</a> <a>th:&#x0e21;&#x0e2b;&#x0e32;&#x0e27;&#x0e34;&#x0e17;&#x0e22;&#x0e32;&#x0e25;&#x0e31;&#x0e22;&#x0e0b;&#x0e35;&#x0e23;&#x0e32;&#x0e04;&#x0e34;&#x0e27;&#x0e2a;&#x0e4c;</a> <a>zh:&#x96ea;&#x57ce;&#x5927;&#x5b78;</a></p>
<p>  The <strong>University of Michigan, Ann Arbor</strong> (commonly referred to as <strong>Michigan</strong>, <strong>U-M</strong>, <strong>UMich</strong>, or <strong>U of M</strong>) is a <a>public</a> research <a>university</a> located in the <a>state</a> of <a>Michigan</a> in the <a>United States</a>.&lt;ref name=&quot;Carnegie&quot; /&gt; It is the state's oldest university and the flagship campus of the University of Michigan.
<p>The university was founded in 1817 in <a>Detroit</a> as the <em>Catholepistemiad</em>, or University of Michigania, about 20 years before the <a>Michigan Territory</a> officially became a state.&lt;ref
| title=The Central Forty and The Diag (1837) | year=2006 | publisher=University of Michigan History and Traditions Committee | accessdate=April 29, 2007}}&lt;/ref&gt; Since its establishment in Ann Arbor, the university has physically expanded to include more than 584 major buildings with a combined area of more than 31 million gross square feet (712&nbsp;acres or 2.38&nbsp;km&#x00b2;),&lt;ref name=&quot;campus size&quot; /&gt; and transformed its academic program from a strictly classical curriculum to one that includes science and research.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
When presidential candidate <a>John F. Kennedy</a> visited the University on October 14, 1960, he gave an impromptu speech on the steps of the <a>Michigan Union</a> that led to a University of Michigan student movement which contributed to the establishment of the <a>Peace Corps</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
name=alumni&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; U-M owns the <a>University of Michigan Health System</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and has one of the largest research expenditures of any American university, passing the $1.14 billion dollar mark during the 2009-2010 academic year.&lt;ref
<p> [[File:JasperCropseyUniversityOfMichigan.jpg|thumb|<em>University of Michigan</em> (1855) by [[Jasper Francis Cropsey]]|alt=Painting of a rolling green landscape with trees with a row of white buildings in the background]] The University of Michigan was  established in Detroit in 1817 as the <em>Catholepistemiad</em>, or University of Michigania, by the governor and judges of <a>Michigan Territory</a>.
book | title=The Michiganensian Yearbook (Class of 1984) | publisher=University of Michigan | date=1984-1985 | page=164}}&lt;/ref&gt; During the 1980s and 1990s, the university devoted substantial resources to renovating its massive hospital complex and improving the academic facilities on the North Campus.
There is also leased space in buildings scattered throughout the city, many occupied by organizations affiliated with the University of Michigan Health System.
The University of Michigan's largest residence hall, Bursley Hall, is located on North Campus.</p>
The University of Michigan Golf Course was included in a listing of top holes designed by what <em><a>Sports Illustrated</a></em> calls &#x201c;golf&#x2019;s greatest course architect.&#x201d;
Alfred Taubman College of Architecture &amp; Urban Planning</a> || 1906 |- | Horace H. Rackham School of Graduate Studies || 1912 |- | <a>Gerald R. Ford School of Public Policy</a> || 1914 |- | <a>School of Education</a> || 1921 |- | <a>Stephen M. Ross School of Business</a> || 1924 |- | <a>School of Natural Resources &amp; Environment</a> || 1927 |- | School of Public Health ||1941 |- | School of Social Work || 1951 |- | <a>School of Information</a> || 1969 |- | <a>School of Art &amp; Design</a> || 1974 |- | <a>School of Kinesiology</a> || 1984 |} The University of Michigan consists of a flagship campus in Ann Arbor, with two regional campuses in <a>Dearborn</a> and <a>Flint</a>.
&lt;/ref&gt; Between the establishment of the University of Michigan in 1837 and 1850, the Board of Regents ran the university directly; although they were, by law, supposed to appoint a Chancellor to administer the university, they never did.
<p>The President of the University of Michigan is the principal executive officer of the university.
The office was created by the <a>Michigan Constitution</a> of 1850, which also specified that the president was to be appointed by the Regents of the University of Michigan and preside at their meetings, but without a vote.&lt;ref
name=&quot;size&quot; /&gt; The Medical School is partnered with the <a>University of Michigan Health System</a>, which comprises the university's three hospitals, dozens of outpatient clinics, and many centers for medical care, research, and education.</p>
| title=2009 Financial Report - The Michigan Difference {Campaign Summary} | publisher=The Regents of the University of Michigan | year=2009 | accessdate=August 31, 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; Like nearly all colleges and universities, U-M suffered significant realized and unrealized losses in its endowment during the second half of 2008.
The two largest colleges at the University of Michigan are the College of Literature, Science, and the Arts (LS&amp;A) and the <a>College of Engineering</a>.
The University of Michigan Engineering Council (UMEC) manages undergraduate student government affairs for the College of Engineering.
In addition, the students that live in the residence halls are represented by the University of Michigan Residence Halls Association.</p>
<p> The University of Michigan is a large, four-year, residential research university accredited by the <a>North Central Association of Colleges and Schools</a>.&lt;ref
| title=Academic Year Tuition and Fees for Full-Time Students (1) By Degree Level, Academic Unit, and Residency | date=June 18, 2010 | publisher=University of Michigan Office of Budget &amp; Planning | accessdate=August 31, 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; U-M provides financial aid in the form of need-based loans, grants, scholarships, work study, and non-need based scholarships, with 77% of undergraduates in 2007 receiving financial aid.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web | url=<a>http://provost.umich.edu/college_portrait/2009/page2.html</a>
| title=The University of Michigan - Financial Aid Awarded to Undergraduates (Fall 2007) | year=2009 | publisher=U-M Provost's Office | accessdate=August 31, 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; 8% were eligible for <a>Pell Grant</a>s.&lt;ref name=&quot;Student debt&quot;&gt; &lt;/ref&gt; For undergraduates in 2008, 46% graduated with about $25,586 of debt in 2008.&lt;ref
| title=University of Michigan-Enrollment by School and College, Gender, and Class Level For Term 1760 (Fall 2009) | publisher=University of Michigan Office of Budget &amp; Planning | date=September 28, 2009 | accessdate=January 3, 2010|format=PDF}}&lt;/ref&gt; in 600 academic programs, and each year about 5,400 new students are enrolled out of almost 30,000 applicants, of which almost 42% are admitted.&lt;ref
<p>U-M is home to the <a>National Election Studies</a> and the <a>University of Michigan Consumer Sentiment Index</a>.
The University of Michigan Transportation Research Institute and the Life Sciences Institute are located at the university.
The <a>University of Michigan Press</a> is also a part of the U-M library system.</p>
<p> <a>thumb|Mosher-Jordan Residence Hall|alt=Red brick facade with white stone fronts and angled roof</a> The University of Michigan's campus housing system can accommodate up to 10,900 people, or nearly 30 percent of the total student population at the university.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
The residence halls are organized into three distinct groups: Central Campus, Hill Area (between Central Campus and the University of Michigan Medical Center) and North Campus.
There are also several engineering projects teams, including the <a>University of Michigan Solar Car Team</a>, which placed first in the <a>North American Solar Challenge</a> five times and third in the <a>World Solar Challenge</a> three times.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The university also showcases many community service organizations and charitable projects, including <a>Foundation for International Medical Relief of Children</a>, Dance Marathon at the University of Michigan,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; <a>The Detroit Partnership</a>, <a>Relay For Life</a>, U-M Stars for the Make-A-Wish Foundation, InnoWorks at the University of Michigan, SERVE, Letters to Success, PROVIDES, Circle K, <a>Habitat for Humanity</a>,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and Ann Arbor Reaching Out.
A large percentage of the students involved in the University of Michigan Greek Life are from out of state.
The student-run and led <a>University of Michigan Pops Orchestra</a> is another musical ensemble that attracts students from all academic backgrounds.
The <a>University of Michigan Men's Glee Club</a>, founded in 1859, is a men's chorus with over 100 members.
Its eight member subset <a>a cappella</a> group, the <a>University of Michigan Friars</a>, which was founded in 1955, is the oldest currently running <em>a cappella</em> group on campus.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Other student publications at the university include the conservative <em><a>The Michigan Review</a></em>, the progressive <em>Michigan Independent</em>, the <em><a>Michigan Journal of Political Science</a></em>, the <em>Michigan Journal of International Affairs</em>, <em><a>The Michigan Journal of Business</a></em>, the <em>University of Michigan Undergraduate Research Journal (UMURJ)</em>, <em><a>Michigan Journal of History</a></em>, and the humor publications <em><a>The Michigan Every Three Weekly</a></em> and the <em><a>Gargoyle</a></em>.
<p> [[File:MichiganStadium2010UConn.JPG|thumb|A football game at [[Michigan Stadium]]|alt=Crowded stadium with yellow-colored &quot;Michigan&quot; written on a green field]] The University of Michigan's sports teams are called the <a>Wolverines</a>.
<p>The University of Michigan's <a>fight song</a>, <em><a>The Victors</a></em>, was written by student <a>Louis Elbel</a> in 1898 following the last-minute football victory over the <a>University of Chicago</a> that won a league championship.
The creators of <a><em>A Very Potter Musical</em></a>, known as <a>Team StarKid</a>, also graduated from the University of Michigan.</p>
|title=The Wallenberg Story | publisher=The Wallenberg Foundation (University of Michigan) | year=2008 | accessdate=February 14, 2007}}&lt;/ref&gt; and <a>Benjamin D. Pritchard</a>, the Civil War general who captured <a>Jefferson Davis</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
name=&quot;Heisman&quot; /&gt; Professional golfer <a>John Schroeder</a> and Olympic swimmer <a>Michael Phelps</a> also attended the University of Michigan, with the latter studying Sports Marketing and Management.

<p><a>ar:&#x062c;&#x0627;&#x0645;&#x0639;&#x0629; &#x0645;&#x064a;&#x0634;&#x064a;&#x063a;&#x0627;&#x0646;</a> <a>bg:&#x041c;&#x0438;&#x0447;&#x0438;&#x0433;&#x0430;&#x043d;&#x0441;&#x043a;&#x0438; &#x0443;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442;</a> <a>de:University of Michigan</a> <a>es:Universidad de M&#x00ed;chigan</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x0645;&#x06cc;&#x0634;&#x06cc;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0646;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; du Michigan</a> <a>gl:Universidade de Michigan</a> <a>ko:&#xbbf8;&#xc2dc;&#xac04; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xad50;</a> <a>io:Universitato di Michigan</a> <a>is:Michigan-h&#x00e1;sk&#x00f3;li</a> <a>it:Universit&#x00e0; del Michigan</a> <a>he:&#x05d0;&#x05d5;&#x05e0;&#x05d9;&#x05d1;&#x05e8;&#x05e1;&#x05d9;&#x05d8;&#x05ea; &#x05de;&#x05d9;&#x05e9;&#x05d9;&#x05d2;&#x05df;</a> <a>lv:Mi&#x010d;iganas universit&#x0101;te</a> <a>lt:Mi&#x010d;igano universitetas</a> <a>ms:Universiti Michigan</a> <a>nl:Universiteit van Michigan</a> <a>ja:&#x30df;&#x30b7;&#x30ac;&#x30f3;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:University of Michigan</a> <a>pnb:&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0646;&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0631;&#x0633;&#x0679;&#x06cc; &#x0443;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442;</a> <a>simple:University of Michigan</a> <a>fi:Michiganin yliopisto</a> <a>sv:University of Michigan</a> <a>ta:&#x0bae;&#x0bbf;&#x0b9a;&#x0bcd;&#x0b9a;&#x0bbf;&#x0b95;&#x0ba9;&#x0bcd; &#x0baa;&#x0bb2;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb2;&#x0bc8;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb4;&#x0b95;&#x0bae;&#x0bcd;</a> <a>th:&#x0e21;&#x0e2b;&#x0e32;&#x0e27;&#x0e34;&#x0e17;&#x0e22;&#x0e32;&#x0e25;&#x0e31;&#x0e22;&#x0e21;&#x0e34;&#x0e0a;&#x0e34;&#x0e41;&#x0e01;&#x0e19;</a> <a>ug:&#x0645;&#x0649;&#x0686;&#x0649;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0646; &#x0626;&#x06c7;&#x0646;&#x0649;&#x06cb;&#x06d0;&#x0631;&#x0633;&#x062a;&#x06d0;&#x062a;&#x0649;</a> <a>zh:&#x5bc6;&#x6b47;&#x6839;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a></p>
<pre>|name              = University of Washington
|image_name        = University of Washington Seal.png
|former_names      = The Territorial University of Washington
<p>The <strong>University of Washington</strong> (<strong>UW</strong>, commonly called <strong>U-Dub</strong>) is a public research <a>university</a>, founded in 1861 in <a>Seattle, Washington</a>, <a>United States</a>.
name=&quot;UW Annual Report&quot;&gt;<a>University of Washington Annual Report (January 2006)</a>.&lt;/ref&gt;
The UW occupies over 500 buildings, with over 20 million gross square footage of space, including the latest <a>University of Washington Plaza</a> consisting 325&nbsp;ft- 22 story UW Tower &amp; conference center.</p>
<p>In 2010, the University of Washington was ranked 16th worldwide by the <em><a>Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></em>,&lt;ref name=&quot;top 500&quot;&gt;<a>Top 500 World Universities (2008)</a> <em>Institute of Higher Education, Shanghai Jiao Tong University</em>&lt;/ref&gt; 23rd worldwide by the <a>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref name=&quot;timeshighereducation1&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and 55th worldwide by the <a>QS World University Rankings</a>.&lt;ref
<p>UW opened officially on November 4, 1861, as the <strong>Territorial University of Washington</strong>.
It would eventually grow into the <a>University of Washington Medical Center</a>, now ranked by <em><a>U.S. News and World Report</a></em> among the top ten hospitals in the <a>United States</a>.
It was during this era in University of Washington history in which many Japanese Americans were sent away from the university to <a>internment camps</a> along the West-coast of the United States as part of <a>Executive Order 9066</a> following the attacks on <a>Pearl Harbor</a>.
As a result, many Japanese American &quot;soon-to-be&quot; graduates were unable to receive their diplomas and be recognized for their accomplishment at the university until the University of Washington's commemoration ceremony for the <a>Japanese Americans</a> entitled <a>The Long Journey Home</a> held on May 18, 2008 at the main campus.</p>
<p>In the early 1950s, the University of Washington Police Department was established.
It currently has jurisdiction over the University of Washington campus and University-owned housing, except for the Radford Court apartments in <a>Sand Point</a>.</p>
Additionally, Washington <a>senators</a>, <a>Henry M. Jackson</a> and <a>Warren G. Magnuson</a> used their political clout to funnel federal research monies to the University of Washington and to this day, UW is among the top recipients of federal research funds in the United States.
<p>The University of Washington, Seattle campus is situated on the shores of <a>Union</a> and <a>Portage Bay</a>s, with views of the <a>Cascade Range</a> to the east and the <a>Olympic Mountains</a> to the west.
South Campus occupies the land between Pacific Street and the <a>Lake Washington Ship Canal</a> which used to be a <a>golf course</a> and is given over to the <a>health sciences</a>, <a>oceanography</a>, <a>fisheries</a>, and the <a>University of Washington Medical Center</a>.
<p> The current president of the University of Washington is Phyllis M. Wise, who had previously served as Provost and Executive Vice President.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The undergraduate student government is the <a>Associated Students of the University of Washington</a> (ASUW) and the graduate student government is the <a>Graduate and Professional Student Senate</a> (GPSS).</p>
<p>In 2006, the University of Washington research budget passed the $1 billion milestone.&lt;ref
<p>In 2009, the University of Washington admitted 61% of applicants.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
University of Washington.&lt;/ref&gt;
University of Washington.&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Library]] reading room]] The <a>University of Washington library system</a> is among the largest academic libraries in the <a>United States</a>, with holdings of more than 7.3 million volumes.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
name=&quot;Inside HigherEd Husky Promise&quot;&gt;<a>Inside HigherEd Husky Promise</a>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;UW Husky Promise&quot;&gt;<a>UW Husky Promise</a>&lt;/ref&gt; &quot;Last year, the University of Washington moved to a more comprehensive approach [to admissions], in which the admissions staff reads the entire application and looks at grades within the context of the individual high school, rather than relying on computerized cutoffs.&quot;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Recognized as one of the most prestigious early university entrance programs in the nation, this program facilitates early entry to the University of Washington for a carefully selected group of sixteen highly-capable young students younger than fifteen (15) years old.
Students apply to the UW Academy during their 10th grade year, and if accepted, withdraw from high school at the end of 10th grade to enroll as freshmen at the University of Washington.&quot;
<p>In 2010, the University of Washington was ranked 16th worldwide by the <em><a>Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></em>,&lt;ref name=&quot;top 500&quot;&gt;<a>Top 500 World Universities (2008)</a> <em>Institute of Higher Education, Shanghai Jiao Tong University</em>&lt;/ref&gt; 23rd worldwide by the <a>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref name=&quot;timeshighereducation1&quot;/&gt; and 55th worldwide by the <a>QS World University Rankings</a>.&lt;ref
<p>In 2006, the University of Washington ranked 22nd internationally by <em><a>Newsweek</a></em> &quot;Top 100 Global Universities&quot;.&lt;ref
<p>The Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index created by Academic Analytics ranks University of Washington overall at #19.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Global Language Monitor, produced at Austin that ranks college based on media presence, placed University of Washington at #16 in the nation.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>University of Washington ranks #1 in <a>Peace Corps</a> volunteers in 2007 and #3 throughout the years.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Kiplinger&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked the University of Washington #7 of the top 100 colleges in early 2009 as one of the Best values in Public Colleges.</p>
<p>The student newspaper is <em><a>The Daily of the University of Washington</a></em>, usually referred to as simply <em>The Daily</em>.
PACCAR Hall is one of two new state-of-the-art buildings being developed as part of an expanded campus for the University of Washington Michael G. <a>Foster School of Business</a>, designed by LMN Architects of Seattle.
<p>Many of the sustainable changes at the University of Washington have resulted from campus activism.
<p>The University of Washington Husky <a>Marching Band</a> performs at many Husky sporting events including all <a>football</a> games.
The University of Washington's mascot is <a>Harry the Husky</a>.
The University of Washington has hosted a long line of <a>Alaskan Malamute</a>s as mascots.
The University of Washington was one of only six universities to receive the highest grade on the Sustainable Endowments Institute's College Sustainability Report Card 2008, an &quot;A-&quot;.&lt;ref

<p>The <strong>University of Pennsylvania</strong> (commonly referred to as <strong>Penn</strong> or <strong>UPenn</strong>) is a <a>private</a> <a>Ivy League</a> <a>research university</a> located in <a>Philadelphia</a>, <a>Pennsylvania</a>, <a>USA</a>.
<p>Incorporated as <em>The Trustees of the University of Pennsylvania</em>, Penn is one of 14 founding members of the <a>Association of American Universities</a>.</p>
<em>History of the University of Pennsylvania 1740&#x2013;1940</em> University of Pennsylvania Press, Philadelphia.
In 1791 the legislature issued a new charter, merging the two institutions into the <strong>University of Pennsylvania</strong> with twelve men from each institution on the new board of trustees.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Penn's educational innovations include: the nation's first medical school in 1765; the first university teaching hospital in 1874; the <a>Wharton School</a>, the world's first collegiate school of business, in 1881; the first American student union building, <a>Houston Hall</a>, in 1896;&lt;ref&gt;<em>Building America's First University: An Historical and Architectural Guide to the University of Pennsylvania</em> George E. Thomas, David Bruce Brownlee, p3&lt;/ref&gt; the country's second school of veterinary medicine; and the home of <a>ENIAC</a>, the world's first electronic, large-scale, general-purpose digital computer in 1946.
The present core campus covers over  in a contiguous area of <a>West Philadelphia</a>'s <a>University City</a> district; the older heart of the campus comprises the <a>University of Pennsylvania Campus Historic District</a>.
<p>The University of Pennsylvania has four undergraduate schools:<a>250px|right|thumb|Lower Quad in Winter, from Riepe College House</a></p>
<p>The following schools offer graduate programs:<a>thumb|300px|right|University of Pennsylvania Dental School</a></p>
Penn has worked to address these issues by pooling its schools (as well as several hospitals and clinical practices) into the University of Pennsylvania Health System, thereby pooling resources for greater efficiencies and research impact.</p>
<p>The University of Pennsylvania's undergraduate business program at Wharton has retained its #1 ranking in U.S. News for many years.
According to MINE ParisTech rankings in 2008, University of Pennsylvania is one of the top five universities in the world, just behind <a>Tokyo University</a>, <a>Harvard University</a>, <a>Stanford University</a>, and <a>Keio University</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Penn's <a>Law School</a> is ranked 7th, and its <a>School of Education</a> and University of Pennsylvania School of Social Policy &amp; Practice (SP2)|School of Social Policy &amp; Practice (SP2) are ranked in the top 10 (see <em>U.S. News</em>).
<a>The University of Pennsylvania Glee Club</a>, founded in 1862, is one of the oldest continually operating collegiate choruses in the United States.
  <p>&quot;Such is the devotion to English rugby football on the part of University of Pennsylvania's students from New Zealand, Australia, and England that they meet on Franklin Field at 7 o'clock every morning and practice the game.
Dan</a> (1985) &quot;Fight On, Pennsylvania&quot; Trustees of University of Pennsylvania pg.
Dan</a> (1985) &quot;Fight On, Pennsylvania&quot; Trustees of University of Pennsylvania pg. 28, 33&#x2013;34.&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The <a>Olympic Boycott Games</a> of 1980 were held at the University of Pennsylvania in response to <a>Moscow</a>'s hosting of the <a>1980 Summer Olympics</a> following the <a>Soviet incursion in Afghanistan</a>.
<p>Notable University of Pennsylvania alumni include eight signers of the <a>Declaration of Independence</a>: <a>George Clymer</a>, <a>Francis Hopkinson</a>, <a>Thomas McKean</a>, <a>Robert Morris</a>, <a>William Paca</a>, <a>George Ross</a>, <a>Benjamin Rush</a>, and <a>James Wilson</a>; nine signers of the <a>Constitution</a>: <a>George Clymer</a>, <a>Thomas Fitzsimons</a>, <a>Jared Ingersoll</a>, <a>Rufus King</a>, <a>Thomas Mifflin</a>, <a>Gouverneur Morris</a>, Robert Morris, <a>Hugh Williamson</a>, and <a>James Wilson</a>; three <a>United States Supreme Court</a> justices: <a>William J. Brennan, Jr.</a>, <a>Owen Roberts</a>, and James Wilson; and one president of the United States: <a>William Henry Harrison</a>.&lt;ref&gt;William
Henry Harrison, Ohio History Central Online Encyclopedia [<a>http://www.ohiohistorycentral.org/entry.php?rec=190</a>]: &quot;At his father&#x2019;s insistence, [he] studied medicine from 1790 to 1791 at the University of Pennsylvania in Philadelphia.

<a>Lord Patten of Barnes</a> |vice_chancellor = <a>Andrew Hamilton</a> |city = <a>Oxford</a> |state = |country = <a>England</a>, <a>UK</a> |students = 20,330&lt;ref name=&quot;OXFACT&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;OXSTATS&quot; /&gt; |undergrad = 11,766&lt;ref name=&quot;OXFACT&quot; /&gt; |postgrad = 8,701&lt;ref name=&quot;OXFACT&quot; /&gt; |other = 461&lt;ref name=&quot;OXSTATS&quot;&gt; &lt;/ref&gt;&lt;!-- Visiting and Recognised students (VRO)--&gt; |colours = Oxford Blue&lt;ref&gt;from &lt;/ref&gt;  |type = <a>Public</a> |affiliations = <a>IARU</a>&lt;br /&gt;<a>Russell Group</a>&lt;br /&gt;<a>Coimbra Group</a>&lt;br /&gt;<a>Europaeum</a>&lt;br /&gt;<a>EUA</a>&lt;br /&gt;<a>G5</a>&lt;br /&gt;<a>LERU</a> |website = <a>www.ox.ac.uk</a> }} The <strong>University of Oxford</strong> (informally <strong>Oxford University</strong>, or simply <strong>Oxford</strong>) is a <a>university</a> located in <a>Oxford</a>, <a>United Kingdom</a>.
name=&quot;oxhist&quot;&gt;  &lt;/ref&gt; In <a>post-nominals</a> the University of Oxford was historically abbreviated as <strong>Oxon.</strong>
[[Arms of the University of Oxford|coat of arms]] of the University of Oxford.]]</p>
<p>The University of Oxford does not have a clear date of foundation.
From the mid-18th century onward, however, the University of Oxford took little part in political conflicts.
<p>The list of distinguished scholars at the University of Oxford is long and includes many who have made major contributions to <a>British politics</a>, the sciences, medicine, and literature.
More than forty Nobel laureates and more than fifty <a>world leaders</a> have been affiliated with the University of Oxford.&lt;ref
<a>Lady Margaret Hall</a> (1878&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;History&quot;,</a> Lady Margaret Hall, University of Oxford&lt;/ref&gt;) was followed by <a>Somerville College</a> in 1879;&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;History&quot;,</a> Somerville College, University of Oxford&lt;/ref&gt; the first 21 students from Somerville and LMH attended lectures in rooms above an Oxford baker's shop.&lt;ref
name=&quot;Lannon&quot;/&gt; The first two colleges for women were followed by <a>St Hugh's</a> (1886&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;History of the College&quot;,</a> St Hugh's College, University of Oxford&lt;/ref&gt;), <a>St Hilda's</a> (1893&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;Constitutional History&quot;,</a> St Hilda's College, University of Oxford&lt;/ref&gt;) and <a>St Anne's College</a> (1952&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;St Anne's History&quot;,</a> St Anne's College, University of Oxford&lt;/ref&gt;). Oxford though was long considered a bastion of male privilege,&lt;ref&gt;Joyce S. Pedersen <a>Book review,</a> H-Albion, May 1996, reprinted on H-Net Review website&lt;/ref&gt; and a quota of female students was instituted by the Universities dons in 1927 fixing the admission of women at about a quarter of the total, a ruling not abolished until 1957.&lt;ref
- <em>Handbook to the University of Oxford</em>.
- University of Oxford.
This was changed in 1925, and the first woman to hold a professorial chair at Uppsala University was <a>Gerd Enequist</a>, appointed professor of human geography in 1949.</p>
at Oxford&quot;,</a> University of Oxford&lt;/ref&gt; By 1988, 40% of undergraduates at Oxford were female;&lt;ref&gt;Jenifer Hart <a>&quot;Women at Oxford since the Advent of Mixed Colleges&quot;,</a> <em>Oxford Review of Education</em>, 15:3, 1989, p.217&lt;/ref&gt; the ratio is now about 48:52 in men's favour.</p>
The collection of University Professors is called the Statutory Professors of the University of Oxford.
College]], one of the constituent colleges of the University of Oxford]] There are 38 <a>colleges of the University of Oxford</a> and 6 <a>Permanent Private Hall</a>s, each with its own internal structure and activities.&lt;ref
<p><a>Academic dress</a> is still commonly seen at Oxford; until the 1960s students wore it at all times (see <a>Academic dress of the University of Oxford</a>).
<p>The University also launched a fundraising campaign in May 2008, called <em>Oxford Thinking - The Campaign for the University of Oxford</em>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Despite the University's claims that its admissions policies avoid bias against candidates of certain socioeconomic or educational backgrounds,&lt;ref name=&quot;Working with Schools and Colleges&quot;&gt;<a>Working with Schools and Colleges</a>, University of Oxford Gazette, 2006.
name=&quot;Admissions Statistics 2006&quot;&gt;<a>Admissions Statistics 2006</a>, University of Oxford Gazette, 2007.
About half of applications come from the state sector,&lt;ref name=&quot;Admissions Statistics 2006&quot;/&gt; and the University of Oxford funds many initiatives to attract applicants from this sector, including the new UNIQ Summer Schools, Oxford Young Ambassadors, Target Schools, and the FE Access Initiative.&lt;ref name=&quot;Working with Schools and Colleges&quot;/&gt; Most colleges also run their own access schemes and initiatives.
<p>In 2002, the University of Oxford commissioned a research project&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; under the auspices of Professor Anthony Heath.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite
<p>:<em>See:</em> <a>Departments of the University of Oxford</a></p>
These include <a>Oxford Brookes University</a>; <a>Ruskin College, Oxford</a> - an <a>adult education</a> college - which, although not part of the University of Oxford, has close links with it; and the former Lady Spencer Churchill teaching college (now the Wheatley campus of <a>Oxford Brookes</a>).</p>
<p>The University of Oxford is an Educational Alliance Partner of the <a>Meade 4M Community</a> which supports the University's 'Project Jetwatch' program.</p>

<p>{{Infobox university | name         =University of Bergen | native_name  =Universitetet i Bergen | latin_name   =Universitas Bergensis | image        =<a>225px|Seal of the University of Bergen</a> | motto        = | established  =1946 (1825) | type         =<a>Public University</a> | rector       =<a>Sigmund Gr&#x00f8;nmo</a> | students     =14,500 (2008) | staff        =3,200 (2007) | city         =<a>Bergen</a> | country      =<a>Norway</a> | campus       = | affiliations =<a>EUA</a>;<a>WUN</a>&lt;br /&gt; <a>Coimbra Group</a>, <a>Utrecht Network</a> | website      =<a>www.uib.no</a>
<p>The <strong>University of Bergen</strong> ()  is located in <a>Bergen</a>, <a>Norway</a>.
<p>[[Image:Faculty of Law in Bergen.JPG|thumb|The Faculty of Law at the University of Bergen, seen from [[Magnus VI of Norway|Magnus Lagab&#x00f8;te]]s plass.]]</p>
<p>The University of Bergen is the only institution in the Nordic countries where the study of <a>psychology</a> has been assigned to its own faculty.
<p> <a>Category:University of Bergen</a> <a>University of Bergen</a> <a>Category:Coimbra Group</a> <a>Category:Educational institutions established in 1946</a> <a>Category:Public universities</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox university |name          = Uppsala University |native_name   = Uppsala universitet |latin_name    = Universitas Regia Upsaliensis<em>, also </em>Academia Regia Upsaliensis |image_name    = Uppsala University logo.svg
<p>[[Image:Entrance hall of Uppsala University main building.jpg|thumb|right|The
<p><strong>Uppsala University</strong> () is a research <a>university</a> in <a>Uppsala</a> and is the oldest university in <a>Scandinavia</a>, founded in 1477.&lt;ref&gt;Ridder-Symoens,
Sten, <em>A history of Uppsala University 1477-1977</em> (Almqvist &amp; Wiksell 1976)]&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Architecturally, Uppsala University has traditionally had a strong presence in the area around <a>the cathedral</a> on the western side of the <a>River Fyris</a>.
<p>As with most medieval universities, Uppsala University initially grew out of an ecclesiastical center.
The first woman in Sweden to complete a doctoral degree was <a>Ellen Fries</a> (1855&#x2013;1900), who entered Uppsala university in 1877 and became a Ph.D. in history in 1883.
<h3>Uppsala University Hospital</h3>
<p> <a>thumb|The old main building of the Uppsala University Hospital, photograph from <em>c.</em> 1920</a> The Uppsala Academic Hospital or <em>Akademiska sjukhuset</em>, which functions as a teaching hospital for the Faculty of Medicine and the Nursing School, is run by the <a>Uppsala County Council</a> in cooperation with the university.
<p><a>thumb|The University Hall during a light exhibition, fall 2008</a> <a>thumb|Uppsala University Botanical Garden</a> <a>thumb|Main building at Campus Pollax</a> Buildings and locations where the university has activities or which are significantly connected to its history.
  <li><a>Uppsala University Botanical Garden</a></li>
  <li><a>Uppsala University Hospital</a></li>
nation]]]] Students at Uppsala University are obliged to become members of one of the <a>nation</a>s, corporations of students traditionally according to province of origin (not strictly upheld now, for practical reasons).
<p>Nations at Uppsala University: {| style=&quot;background-color: transparent; width: {}&quot; | width=&quot;{}&quot; align=&quot;{}&quot; valign=&quot;{}&quot; |</p>
Affiliated with the University are three choirs, the mixed <a>Uppsala University Choir</a> (<em>Allm&#x00e4;nna S&#x00e5;ngen</em>), founded in 1830, the male choir <a>Orphei Dr&#x00e4;ngar</a>, founded in 1853, and the <a>Academy Chamber Choir of Uppsala</a>, founded in 1957.
In honour of Ericson, the <a>F&#x00f6;reningsSparbanken</a> endowed the Eric Ericson Chair in Choral Directing, and the Uppsala University Choral Centre was inaugurated in 2000.
<p>Uppsala University has signed student exchange agreements with about 500 universities across all parts of the world.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Uppsala
University international office (Swedish)</a>&lt;/ref&gt; It takes part in the <a>Erasmus programme</a> programme and the Nordplus programme.Uppsala University has signed university-wide student exchange programmes with the following universities (selection)&lt;ref&gt;<a>Uppsala University International Office, 2009</a>&lt;/ref&gt;:</p>
<p>Uppsala University is a member of the <a>Coimbra Group</a> of universities.</p>
<p>Uppsala University places well in many rankings.&lt;ref&gt;<a>QS
<p>Uppsala University is associated with 8 <a>Nobel Prize</a> laureates,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and numerous royalty, academics and public figures.</p>
<p>As the dominant academic institution in Sweden for several centuries, Uppsala University has ever since its first period of expansion in the early part of the 17th century educated a large proportion of Swedish politicians and civil servants, from 17th century Chancellor of the Realm (<em>rikskansler</em>) <a>Johan Oxenstierna</a> (1611&#x2013;1657) and Lord Chief Justice (<em>riksdrots</em>) <a>Magnus Gabriel De la Gardie</a> (1622&#x2013;1686) to the first Social Democratic <a>Prime Minister of Sweden</a>, <a>Hjalmar Branting</a> (1860&#x2013;1925) and many later politicians.
<a>Niklas Zennstr&#x00f6;m</a>, co-founder of <a>KaZaA</a> and <a>Skype</a> is also a former student at Uppsala University.
On August 15, 2008 Zennstr&#x00f6;m donated 15 million <a>SEK</a> to Uppsala University for climate research.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<h2>Uppsala University in fiction and popular culture</h2>
Specifically, Uppsala University has appeared notably in <em>M&#x00e4;n som hatar kvinnor</em> or <em>The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo</em> by Steig Larsson.</p>
<p>The Norwegian pop singer <a>Kirsti Sparboe</a> dedicated one of her biggest successes to Uppsala University, publishing in 1969 the song &quot;Ein Student aus Uppsala&quot;.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Youtube, &quot;Ein Student aus Uppsala&quot;, by [[Kirsti Sparboe]]</a>&lt;/ref&gt; The song, originally written in German, lasted 14 weeks in the German charts.
