<p>{{Infobox university |image_name=University of Rochester logo.svg
|image_size=220px |name=University of Rochester |motto=<em><a>Meliora</a></em> (<a>Latin</a>) |mottoeng=Always Better (also, Ever Better) |established=1850 |type=<a>Private</a>, secular |calendar=  Semester |president=<a>Joel Seligman</a> |city = <a>Rochester</a> |state=<a>New York</a> |country=<a>U.S.</a> |undergrad=4,606 |postgrad=4,357 |staff=1,225 |free_label      = Annual Fees |free            = $52,690 (2009&ndash;2010) |campus=<a>Suburb</a>an/<a>Urban</a>,&lt;ref&gt;The <a>Eastman School</a> campus is in downtown Rochester (urban), while the majority of the university is located in a more suburban environment.&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The <strong>University of Rochester</strong> (<strong>U of R</strong>, <strong>UR</strong>, or URoc) is a <a>private</a>, nonsectarian, research university located in <a>Rochester, New York</a>.
The University of Rochester, along with its affiliated Strong Health System, is the largest employer in the Greater Rochester area and the sixth largest employer in New York.&lt;ref&gt;<a>State.NY.us</a>,
<p>The University of Rochester was founded in 1850 as a Baptist-sponsored institution.
<p>The university uses Dandelion Yellow and a shade of blue (Rochester blue) as its official colors, which are the prominent colors on the official regalia.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester Colors</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The impetus to form the university came primarily from the town of <a>Hamilton, New York</a>, which has been home to <a>Colgate University</a> since 1819.&lt;ref&gt;<a>History of the University of Rochester</a>&lt;/ref&gt; In 1848, the Baptist Education Society planned to move Colgate University (then known as Madison University) to the city of Rochester, but was halted by legal action.
Dissenting Colgate trustees, faculty, and students founded the University of Rochester, receiving a charter from the <a>Regents of the University of the State of New York</a> on January 31, 1850.
Arthur J. (1977) <em>A History of the University of Rochester</em>, Princeton: <a>Princeton University</a>&lt;/ref&gt; <a>thumb|Inside of the Great Hall of Rush Rhees.</a>
The University of Rochester's campus was originally in downtown Rochester at the United States Hotel, which was located on Buffalo Street near Elizabeth Street, which today is West Main Street near the <a>I-490</a> overpass.
name=&quot;May, Arthur J. 1977&quot;&gt;May, Arthur J. (1977) <em>A History of the university of Rochester</em>, Princeton: Princeton University&lt;/ref&gt; UR would remain on this campus until the current River Campus was constructed in 1930, and the university continues to own a small part of the University Avenue campus (where the university-owned Memorial Art Gallery is located).
In 1958, three new schools were created in <a>engineering</a>, <a>business administration</a>, and <a>education</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester:</a> History and Distinctions&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The university is headed by a board of trustees, with Edmund A. Hajim being the chairman.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester News Release:</a> University Names New Trustees and New Chairman&lt;/ref&gt; The board appoints the president of the university, currently <a>Joel Seligman</a>, who replaced <a>Thomas H. Jackson</a> on July 1, 2005.</p>
<p>{| class=&quot;wikitable&quot; |+ <strong>Presidents of the University</strong>&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester:</a> Presidents of the University&lt;/ref&gt; |- !
  <li><strong>University of Rochester Medical Center</strong></li>
<p> <a>thumb|The School of Medicine and Dentistry at the University of Rochester's Medical Center.</a>
The <strong>University of Rochester Medical Center (URMC)</strong> is the primary campus for the university's medical education and research as well as the main patient care facility.
<p>University of Rochester's <a>undergraduate</a> enrollment consists of about 4,500 full-time and about 100 part-time students from across the U.S. and over 90 countries.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Diversity
<p>The University of Rochester is known for its several unique 5th year programs.
<p>U.S. News and World Report, in their popular National University Rankings, placed the University of Rochester 35th in the nation for 2008, 2009, and 2010.&lt;ref&gt;<a>USNews.com:
Bot generated title --&gt;</a>&lt;/ref&gt; In 2007, the London Times rated the University of Rochester 48th among the best universities in the world and 21st among American educational institutions.
The University of Rochester also placed 21st on The Washington Monthly College Rankings list.
University of Rochester places within the top 10 for the staff-to-student ratio.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Times
<p><strong>Internationally</strong>, in 2010 <a>QS World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked the University of Rochester joint 127th alongside <a>Case Western Reserve University</a>, making it joint 41st in the United States.</p>
<p>Rush Rhees Library at The University of Rochester was featured on the cover of the &quot;Princeton Review 373 Best Colleges 2011 Edition&quot;.
<p>For more information on University of Rochester's history and distinctions, please go to: <a>http://www.rochester.edu/aboutus/history.html</a></p>
UR consistently ranks among the top 40 colleges and universities nationwide in federally financed <a>science</a>, <a>engineering</a>, <a>medical</a>, and other research, with a total research budget of around $350 million spread across many departments and research centers, including the <a>Laboratory for Laser Energetics</a>, a laser-based <a>nuclear fusion</a> facility, and the extensive research facilities at the <a>University of Rochester Medical Center</a>.
WeBWorK, a web-based system for checking homework and providing immediate feedback for students, was developed by University of Rochester professors Gage and Pizer.
<p>Academics at the University of Rochester are generally organized and administered by school.
Flaum Atrium between the School of Medicine and Dentistry and the [[Arthur Kornberg]] buildings in the <a>University of Rochester Medical Center</a>.]]</p>
The school is located in the <a>University of Rochester Medical Center</a>.</p>
<p>:The university also includes an accredited <strong>School of Nursing</strong>, located on the campus of the <a>University of Rochester Medical Center</a>.</p>
UR's official symbol is the seal of the university, which features a book, representing <a>arts and sciences</a>, a lyre symbolizing music, and a modified <a>symbol of medicine</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester Seal</a>&lt;/ref&gt; The official flower of the university is the <a>dandelion</a>, purportedly prolific on the cow pasture that became the university's first campus.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester: Dandelion</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
However, when the university re-designed the mascot during the 2007-2008 academic year, a new name was chosen and as of February 1, 2008, the school's mascot is now known as &quot;Rocky&quot;.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester Mascot: The Yellowjackets</a>&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>New University of Rochester Yellowjacket to debut Feb. 1</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The image of <a>Rush Rhees Library</a>'s main dome serves as an additional icon for the University of Rochester.</p>
Although less frequently used, the university also has an official <a>Alma Mater</a>, <em>The Dandelion Yellow</em>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Songs of the University of Rochester</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Past speakers include <a>Anderson Cooper</a>, <a>Stephen Colbert</a>, <a>Colin Powell</a>, and <a>United States Secretary of Energy</a> and University of Rochester alumnus <a>Steven Chu</a>.</li>
<p>The student body at the University of Rochester is both ethnically and socioeconomically diverse.
The campus also hosts a volunteer EMT squad (The University of Rochester MERT) which provides free New York State certified Basic Life Support services to the River Campus community.
The University of Rochester is also home to its own radio station, <a>WRUR</a>.</p>
Housing is provided at multiple locations spread across the several campuses.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Rochester Residential Life</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>

<p><a>ca:Universitat de Rochester</a> <a>cs:University of Rochester</a> <a>de:University of Rochester</a> <a>es:Universidad de Rochester</a> <a>eo:Universitato de Ro&#x0109;estro</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x0631;&#x0648;&#x0686;&#x0633;&#x062a;&#x0631;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; de Rochester</a> <a>ko:&#xb85c;&#xccb4;&#xc2a4;&#xd130; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xad50;</a> <a>is:H&#x00e1;sk&#x00f3;linn &#x00ed; Rochester</a> <a>it:University of Rochester</a> <a>ja:&#x30ed;&#x30c1;&#x30a7;&#x30b9;&#x30bf;&#x30fc;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:Universitetet i Rochester</a> <a>pnb:&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0646;&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0631;&#x0633;&#x0679;&#x06cc; &#x0622;&#x0641; &#x0631;&#x0648;&#x0686;&#x0633;&#x0679;&#x0631;</a> <a>pl:University of Rochester</a> <a>fi:Rochesterin yliopisto</a> <a>zh:&#x7f85;&#x5fb9;&#x65af;&#x7279;&#x5927;&#x5b78;</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox university | name        = University of California | image       = <a>220px</a> | motto       = <em>Fiat lux</em> (<a>Latin</a>) | mottoeng    = <a>Let there be light</a> | established = 1868 | type        = <a>Public</a> <a>university system</a> | endowment   = $4.9 billion [<a>http://www.nacubo.org/Documents/research/2009_NCSE_Public_Tables_Endowment_Market_Values.pdf</a>]
<p>The <strong>University of California</strong> (<strong>UC</strong>) is a <a>public university</a> <a>system</a> in the <a>state</a> of <a>California</a>.
Under the <a>California Master Plan for Higher Education</a>, the University of California is a part of the state's three-tier public <a>higher education</a> system, which also includes the <a>California State University</a> system and the <a>California Community Colleges</a> system.</p>
<p>The University of California has a combined <a>student</a> body of more than 191,000 students and over 1,340,000 living <a>alumni</a>.</p>
In addition, the independently administered <a>UC Hastings</a>&lt;ref&gt;Hastings has a unique relationship with the University of California.
In 1878, when Justice Serranus Clinton Hastings gave $100,000 to the University of California to start the law school bearing his name, he imposed two conditions: (1) the school must remain in San Francisco near the courts and (2) it could not be governed by the <a>Regents of the University of California</a>.
See: <a>University of California, Hastings College of the Law#History</a>.
<p>The University of California's campuses boast large numbers of distinguished <a>faculty</a> in almost every field and is widely regarded as one of the top public university systems in the world.
<p>[[File:Berkeley glade afternoon.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, Berkeley|Berkeley]] (1868)]] [[File:UC Davis Mondavi Center.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, Davis|Davis]] (1908)]] [[File:RHall.JPG|thumb|[[University of California, Los Angeles|Los Angeles]] (1919)]] [[File:Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, Santa Barbara|Santa Barbara]] (1944)]] [[File:Ucr-belltower.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, Riverside|Riverside]] (1954)]] [[File:Geisel library.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, San Diego|San Diego]] (1960)]] [[File:Uc irvine8300001.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, Irvine|Irvine]] (1965)]] [[File:Cowell College.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, Santa Cruz|Santa Cruz]] (1965)]] [[File:Ucmercedscienceandengineeringbuilding.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, Merced|Merced]] (2005)]] [[File:Mission Bay, UCSF.jpg|thumb|[[University of California, San Francisco|San Francisco]] (1873)]] [[File:Universityofcaliforniaofficeofthepresident.jpg|thumb|right|UC
<p>Governor <a>Frederick Low</a> favored the establishment of a state university based upon the <a>University of Michigan</a> plan, and thus in one sense may be regarded as the founder of the University of California.
Accordingly, the Organic Act, establishing the University of California, was signed into law by Governor <a>Henry H. Haight</a> (Low's successor) on March 23, 1868.&lt;ref&gt;Harvey
Helfand, <em>University of California, Berkeley: An Architectural Tour and Photographs,</em> (New York: Princeton Architectural Press, 2002), 6.&lt;/ref&gt;   </p>
<p>The University of California's second president, <a>Daniel Coit Gilman</a>, opened the <a>Berkeley</a> campus in September 1873.
In 1944, the former Santa Barbara State College&#x2014;renamed <a>UC Santa Barbara</a>--became the third general-education campus of the University of California system.</p>
<p>In 1932, <a>Will Keith Kellogg</a> donated his Arabian horse ranch in <a>Pomona, California</a> to the University of California system.
[[University of California, Davis, Arboretum|Davis Arboretum]] walkway and garden on The Waterway.]]
UC researchers create 3 new inventions per day.&lt;ref&gt;University of California, Office of the President, Press Release, September 28, 2005.[<a>http://www.universityofcalifornia.edu/news/2005/sep28.html</a>]&lt;/ref&gt;  </p>
<p>The University of California and most of its campuses are members of the <a>Association of American Universities (AAU)</a>.
<p> At 34 million items,&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of California Cultural Resources Libraries</a>.
Accessed January 26, 2008.&lt;/ref&gt; the University of California <a>library</a> system contains one of the largest collections in the world.
<p>The University of California is governed by the <a>Regents of the University of California</a>, as required by the current <a>Constitution of the State of California</a>.
Today, the UC Office of the President and the Office of the Secretary of the Regents of the University of California share an office building in downtown Oakland which serves as the UC system's <a>headquarters</a>.</p>

<p>The University of California has a long tradition of involvement in many enterprises that are often geographically or organizationally separate from its general campuses, including national laboratories, observatories, hospitals, continuing education programs, hotels, conference centers, an airport, and an art institute.</p>
The University of California directly manages and operates one <a>United States Department of Energy National Laboratory</a>:</p>
They also have much deeper ties to the university than the Los Alamos Lab, a fact seen in their respective original names; the University of California Berkeley Radiation Laboratory and the University of California Radiation Laboratory at Livermore.</p>
<p>The University of California's ties to the labs have so far outlasted all periods of internal controversy.
<p>On June 1, 2006, the University of California ended its direct involvement in operating Los Alamos National Laboratory, and management control of the laboratory was taken over by <a>Los Alamos National Security, LLC</a>.
<p>On October 1, 2007, the University of California ended its direct involvement in operating the Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory.
Management control of the laboratory was taken over by Lawrence Livermore National Security, LLC, a limited liability company whose members are Bechtel National, the University of California, Babcock and Wilcox, the Washington Division of URS Corporation, Battelle Memorial Institute, and The Texas A&amp;M University System.</p>
<p>The University of California is a founding and charter member of <a>CENIC</a>, the Corporation for Education Network Initiatives in California, the nonprofit organization which provides extremely high-performance Internet-based networking to California's K-20 research and education community.</p>
<p>The University of California also works with the <a>NASA Ames Research Center</a> at <a>Moffett Federal Airfield</a> in California.
<a>UC Santa Cruz</a> manages the UARC for the University of California, with the goal of increasing the science output, safety, and effectiveness of <a>NASA</a>'s missions through new technologies and scientific techniques.
Since 2002, the <a>NSF</a>-funded <a>San Diego Supercomputer Center</a> at <a>UC San Diego</a> has been managed by the University of California, taking over for the previous manager, <a>General Atomics</a>.</p>
<p>The University of California manages two <a>observatories</a> as a multi-campus research unit headquartered at <a>UC Santa Cruz</a>.</p>
<p>The University of California operates five medical centers throughout the state:</p>
<p>The University of California division of Agriculture and Natural Resources plays an important role in the State's agriculture industry, as mandated by the UC's legacy as a land-grant institution.
Currently, the division's <a>University of California 4-H Youth Development Program</a> and <a>4-H Center for Youth Development</a> are national leaders in studying <a>thriving</a> in the field of <a>youth development</a>.</p>

<p>The <strong>University of California, Berkeley</strong> (also referred to as <strong>Cal</strong>, <strong>California</strong>, <strong>Berkeley</strong> and <strong>UC Berkeley</strong>) is a <a>public research university</a> located in <a>Berkeley, California</a>, <a>United States</a>, in the San Francisco Bay Area.
Today <em>University of California</em> refers to a statewide school system and the official name is <em>University of California, Berkeley</em>, frequently shortened to <em>UC Berkeley</em>, <em>Berkeley</em>, <em>Cal.</em>
{{cite web|url=<a>http://www.haas.berkeley.edu/groups/pubs/calbusiness/current/alumni05.html</a>|title=Obituaries - Business Visionary Don Fisher, BS 51|date=2009 (Fall)|publisher=University of California, Berkeley's Haas School of Business}}&lt;/ref&gt;  <a>MySpace</a>,&lt;ref name=&quot;MySpaceByAnderson&quot;&gt;<a>MySpace</a> was co-founded by <a>Tom Anderson</a>(BA 1998).
Litwack's last stand|date=2007-05-08|author=Cathy Cockrell|publisher=UC Berkeley NewsCenter (University of California, Berkeley)}}&lt;/ref&gt; <a>three other</a> UC Berkeley professors have also received the Pulitzer Prize.
  <li><a>A Brief History of the University of California, Berkeley</a></li>
Students of Environmental Horticulture and other botanical sciences have many acres of campus farmland and the <a>University of California, Davis, Arboretum</a> at their disposal.
The Zona Zoo program is co-owned by the Associated Students of the University of Arizona (ASUA) and Arizona Athletics, the program is run by a team of spirited individuals called the Zona Zoo Crew.
<p>There are currently (2005) 44 <a>fraternity and sorority</a> chapters that are recognized by the University of Arizona.

|logo =<a>245px</a> }} The <strong>University of California, Santa Cruz</strong>, also known as <strong>UC Santa Cruz</strong> or <strong>UCSC</strong>, is a <a>public</a>, <a>collegiate</a> <a>university</a>; one of ten campuses in the <a>University of California</a>.
&lt;ref&gt; {{cite web |title=University of California, Santa Cruz (Statistics) |work=The Princeton Review |url=<a>http://www.princetonreview.com/college/research/profiles/academics.asp?listing=1023551&amp;ltid=1&amp;intbucketid=</a> |accessdate=2006-06-29 }} (Note: Registration required) &lt;/ref&gt; Interdisciplinary programs, such as Feminist Studies, American Studies, Environmental Studies, Digital Arts and New Media, and the unique <a>History of Consciousness</a> Department are also hosted alongside UCSC's more traditional academic departments.</p>

<p>{{Infobox university | name         = University of California, Davis | motto        = Fiat lux (<a>Latin</a>) | mottoeng     = <a>Let there be light</a> | image_name   = UniversityofCalifornia,Davis.JPG | image_size   = 200px | established  = 1905 as the University Farm (of UC Berkeley)&lt;br /&gt;1959  established as a general UC campus | type         = <a>Public</a>, <a>Land-grant</a>, <a>Space-grant</a> | calendar     = Quarter | endowment    = US$540 <a>million</a> (June 30, 2009) &lt;ref&gt;<a>UC Annual Endowment Report</a> <em>Office of the Treasurer of The Regents'.' Retrieved March 31, 2010.&lt;/ref&gt;</em>
<p>The <strong>University of California, Davis, (UC Davis)</strong> is a <a>public</a> research university located in <a>Davis, California</a>, and one of ten campuses in the <a>University of California</a> system.
<p>The University of California, Davis campus is the largest campus in the UC system, spanning over  across two counties: <a>Yolo</a> and <a>Solano</a>.
<p><a>thumb|left|University of California, Davis Fire Department|UC Davis fire engine</a> Towards the northeast end of campus is the Quad, a large rectangular field which sits adjacent to Freeborn Hall and the Memorial Union, which houses various establishments such as the UC Davis Bookstore, ASUCD Coffee House, food courts, Post Office, Sky Room, and the MU Games Area.
<p> <a>Category:University of California, Davis</a> <a>Davis</a> <a>Category:Davis, California</a> <a>California Davis, University of</a> <a>California Davis, University of</a> <a>Category:Association of Public and Land-Grant Universities</a> <a>California Davis, University of</a> <a>California Davis, University of</a> <a>Category:Agricultural universities and colleges</a> <a>Category:Schools accredited by the Western Association of Schools and Colleges</a> <a>Category:Central Valley of California</a> <a>Category:Universities and colleges in Yolo County, California</a></p>

&#x0e40;&#x0e14;&#x0e27;&#x0e34;&#x0e2a;</a> <a>zh:&#x6234;&#x7dad;&#x65af;&#x52a0;&#x5229;&#x798f;&#x5c3c;&#x4e9e;&#x5927;&#x5b78;</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox university | name            = The University of Sydney | motto           = <em>Sidere mens eadem mutato</em> (<a>Latin</a>) | mottoeng        = <a>Literal</a>: &quot;Though the constellations change, the mind is universal&quot; &lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;<a>Meaning</a>: The traditions of the older universities of the Northern Hemisphere are continued here in the Southern | latin_name        = Universitas Sidneiensis | established     = 1850 | type            = <a>Public</a> | endowment       = AU$937m&lt;br /&gt;&lt;small&gt;(31 December 2009)&lt;/small&gt;&lt;ref&gt;<a>INVESTMENT AND CAPITAL MANAGEMENT REPORT&quot;</a>&lt;/ref&gt; | chancellor      = <a>Her Excellency Professor Marie Bashir AC, CVO</a>&lt;ref&gt;<a>Faculty alumna elected University Chancellor</a>, Retrieved on 2007-06-02.&lt;/ref&gt;
<p><strong>The University of Sydney</strong> (informally <strong>Sydney University</strong> or <strong>USyd</strong>) is a university located in <a>Sydney</a>, <a>Australia</a>.
<p>The University of Sydney is a member of Australia's <a>Group of Eight</a>, Academic Consortium 21, the <a>Association of Pacific Rim Universities</a> (APRU) and the <a>Worldwide Universities Network</a>.</p>
<p>The university was established via the passage of the University of Sydney Act,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; which was signed on 1 October 1850.
On 27 February 1858 the university received its <a>Royal Charter</a> from <a>Queen Victoria</a>, giving degrees conferred by the university rank and recognition equal to those given by universities in the UK.&lt;ref name=&quot;royal_charter&quot;&gt;<a>Royal Charter of the University of Sydney</a>&lt;/ref&gt;  By 1859, the university had moved to its current site in the Sydney suburb of <a>Camperdown</a>.</p>
<p>The New England University College was founded as part of the University of Sydney in 1938, and separated to become the University of New England in 1954.</p>
<p>During the late 1960s, the University of Sydney was at the centre of rows to introduce courses on <a>Marxism</a> and <a>feminism</a> at the major Australian universities.
<p><a>thumb|250px|Front lawns</a> The <a>Orange Agricultural College</a> (OAC) was originally transferred to the <a>University of New England</a> under the Act, but then transferred to the University of Sydney in 1994, as part of the reforms to the University of New England undertaken by the University of New England Act 1993&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and the Southern Cross University Act 1993.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
In January 2005, the University of Sydney transferred the OAC to <a>Charles Sturt University</a>.</p>
<p>In 2010, the <a>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> placed the University of Sydney 184st in the world and 3rd in Australia behind the <a>University of Melbourne</a> (36th) and the Macquarie University (43rd).&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p><a>QS World University Rankings</a> 2010 placed the University of Sydney 48th in the world and 2nd in Australia ahead of the University of Melbourne (38th).&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
The University of Sydney currently has financial endowments totaling $829 million.
<p>Latest figures show that the University of Sydney has received the highest amount of research grants, which may demonstrate its research competitiveness and the size of its students and staff body.&lt;ref
name=&quot;usyd_facts&quot;/&gt; The University of Sydney also has the second largest (behind <a>Monash University</a>) body of students and researchers among Australian universities.</p>
<p>The University of Sydney secured more than $46 million in funding in the 2007 round of National Health and Medical Research Council (NHMRC) Project Grant, Capacity Building and Fellowship awards, the largest allocation to any university in the state.
<li><strong><a>University of Sydney Union</a></strong>: The University of Sydney Union (USU) is the oldest and largest university union in Australia.

<p>The <strong>University of Arizona</strong> (also referred to as <strong>UA</strong>, <strong>U of A</strong>, or <strong>Arizona</strong>) is a <a>land-grant</a> and <a>space-grant</a> <a>public</a> institution of <a>higher education</a> and <a>research</a> located in <a>Tucson, Arizona</a>, United States.
The University of Arizona was the first <a>university</a> in the state of <a>Arizona</a>, founded in 1885 (twenty-seven years before the Arizona Territory achieved statehood).
The university includes the <a>University of Arizona College of Medicine</a> which is one of three medical schools and the only <a>MD</a> granting medical school in Arizona.
name=&quot;Fact Book&quot;/&gt; The University of Arizona is governed by the <a>Arizona Board of Regents</a>.
The mission of the University of Arizona is, &quot;To discover, educate, serve, and inspire.&quot;&lt;ref
<p><a>right|thumb|200px|Old Main, the oldest building on the University of Arizona campus</a> The University of Arizona was approved by the Arizona Territory's &quot;<a>Thieving Thirteenth</a>&quot; Legislature in 1885.
<a>thumb|left|University of Arizona Mall</a> <a>thumb|right|Wildcat Family Statue</a></p>
<p>The University of Arizona offers 334 fields of study leading to bachelor's, master's, doctoral, and professional degrees.
The University of Arizona is the only remaining <a>Pac-10</a> conference school to not award plus and minus grades for courses.
<p>The <a>James E. Rogers College of Law</a> was ranked 42nd nationally by U.S. News &amp; World Report in for 2011.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Arizona (Rogers) - Law -Best Graduate Schools - Education - US News and World Report&lt;!-- Bot generated title --&gt;</a>&lt;/ref&gt; The Systems and <a>Industrial Engineering</a> (SIE) Department is ranked 10th in the 'America's Best Graduate Schools 2009' by US News and World Report.
name=&quot;Highlights and rankings 22&quot;/&gt; The <a>Doctor of Pharmacy</a> program at the <a>University of Arizona College of Pharmacy</a> is ranked 4th nationally by U.S. News &amp; World Report in 2005.&lt;ref
Internationally, the 2010 <a>Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked University of Arizona 95th in the world and the 2010 <a>QS World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked this university 160th.
<p>The libraries at University of Arizona are expecting a 15 percent budget cut for the 2009 fiscal year.
<p><a>The University of Arizona Poetry Center</a> is among the nation&#x2019;s finest and most extensive collections of contemporary poetry.
<p>The University of Arizona generates renewable energy with solar panels that have been installed on campus buildings.
<p>The University of Arizona, like its sister institutions <a>Arizona State University</a> and <a>Northern Arizona University</a>, is governed by the <a>Arizona Board of Regents</a> or the ABOR, a 12-member body.
name=&quot;Swedlund&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Notable past UA presidents include Likins, Manuel Pacheco (the first person of <a>Hispanic</a> descent to lead the university and for whom the <a>Integrated Learning Center</a> is named), <a>Homer L. Shantz</a>, Henry Koffler, John Schaefer, and Richard Harvill.&lt;ref&gt;<a>&quot;Past Presidents of The University of Arizona&quot;, from UA Office of the President website.
<p> &lt;!-- Image with inadequate rationale removed: <a>thumb|right|200px|University of Arizona &quot;A&quot; Logo</a> --&gt; Like many large public universities in the U.S., sports are a major activity on campus, and receive a large operating budget.
name=&quot;History 8&quot;&gt; &lt;/ref&gt;  The University of Arizona participates in the <a>NCAA</a>'s Division I-A in the <a>Pacific-10 Conference</a>, which it joined in 1978.</p>
<p> <a>thumb|Arizona Stadium</a> The <a>football</a> team began at The University of Arizona in 1899 under the nickname &quot;Varsity&quot; (a name kept until the 1914 season when the team was deemed the &quot;Wildcats&quot;).&lt;ref
Although surprising to some, the University of Arizona has a noteworthy history in <a>ice hockey</a>.
<p>A strong athletic rivalry exists between the University of Arizona and <a>Arizona State University</a> located in <a>Tempe</a>.
<p> <strong>The Official Student Section and Student Ticketing Program for University of Arizona Athletics</strong></p>
<p>Officially implemented in 2003, Zona Zoo is the official student section and student ticketing program for the University of Arizona Athletics.
The University of Arizona is home to more than 500 philanthropic, multi-cultural, social, athletic, academic, and student clubs and campus organizations.
Through funding from the CSIL and the Associated Students of the University of Arizona, clubs are given the resources and encouragement to explore unusual interests.</p>
<p>In 2008 University of Arizona students started <a>their own branch</a> (reinstated as of April 21, 2010&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;) of the <a>Arizona Students for Life (ASFL)</a> <a>pro-life</a> association, whose goal is to help pregnant college women and raise awareness about <a>elective abortion</a>, of which college women are half all those affected.</p>
<p>The University of Arizona is also home to one of the oldest <a>Model United Nations</a> organizations in the United States, which each year hosts several hundred students high school students in a bilingual simulation of the <a>United Nations</a> and other international bodies.</p>
<p>The campus comedy group, <a>Comedy Corner</a> is a sketch and improv comedy group at the University of Arizona.
<p>The University of Arizona <a>marching band</a>, named <a>The Pride of Arizona</a>, played at the halftime of the first <a>Super Bowl</a>.
--&gt; Overall, students at the University of Arizona have been represented by the Associated Students of the University of Arizona (ASUA) since 1913.
Each of the 10 Senators and all Administrative Officers also are appointed to serve on the various University of Arizona Faculty and Administrative Committees.</p>
Much like ASUA, the GPSC appoints representatives to serve on various University of Arizona Faculty and Administrative Committees and 1 Director to serve on the Arizona Students' Association.</p>
<p>The University of Arizona Residence Hall Association has hosted 3 regional IACURH Residence Hall Conferences, which were hosted in 1961, 1997, and 2004.
In 2005, the University of Arizona's Residence Hall Association was voted by <a>NACURH</a> (National Association of College and University Residence Halls) as the National School of the Year out of over 400 schools across the United States.
In May 2009, the University of Arizona hosted the NACURH National Residence Hall Conference (also hosted in 1963), bringing more than 2,200 on-campus residents from over 250 schools across the United States and Canada for 3 days of school spirit and learning how to become more sustainable and socially just.
The film <em><a>Revenge of the Nerds</a></em> (1984) was filmed at the University of Arizona.
The film <em><a>Eating Out</a></em> was shot around the University of Arizona campus in Tucson.
<p>The University has also been the setting for portions of <a>David Foster Wallace</a>'s novel <em><a>Infinite Jest</a></em> takes place at the University of Arizona campus, including a scene in the administration building satirizing the school's <a>bureaucracy</a>.

<p>{{Infobox University |name = The University of Tulsa |image_name = UTULSEA1.png
<p>The University of Tulsa was founded in <a>Muskogee, Oklahoma</a>, as the Presbyterian School for Indian Girls in 1882 under the leadership of <a>Alice Mary Robertson</a>, but was re-chartered as the <strong>Henry Kendall College</strong> in 1894 under the auspices of the Presbyterian Women's Board of Home Missions.
A university was formed in 1920 when the college merged with the proposed <a>McFarlin College</a> to become the University of Tulsa.</p>
<p>The University of Tulsa is noted for having one of the world's premier programs in <a>petroleum engineering</a>, and has distinguished programs in <a>English</a>, <a>computer science</a>, <a>natural sciences</a>, <a>Clinical and Industrial/Organizational Psychology</a>, and several <a>engineering</a> disciplines.
The University of Tulsa College of Law Review ranks in the top 15% of most cited legal periodicals as ranked by <a>Washington and Lee University</a>.[<a>http://law.wlu.edu/library/mostcited/index.asp</a>]
In its focus on energy, the University of Tulsa maintains both the National Energy Policy Institute and the National Energy-Environment Law and Policy Institute.&lt;ref&gt;Davis,
<p>Currently, there are six colleges, programs, and departments at the University of Tulsa:</p>
The University of Tulsa also placed sixth among all colleges for &quot;Happiest Students,&quot; was ranked eleventh in the &quot;Lots of Class/Race Interaction&quot; category, and in &quot;Town-Gown Relations&quot; Tulsa was ranked fifth in the country.
In the 2006 edition, the university was described as follows: &#x201c;The University of Tulsa is one of the sleeper gems of the <a>Great Plains</a>, a private school large enough to house numerous top-flight programs but small enough to facilitate one-on-one instruction provided in a homey atmosphere.&#x201d;</p>
<p>The University of Tulsa is known for the large number of National Merit scholars in attendance, approximately one in every ten undergraduate students.
According to &quot;The Chronicle of Higher Education&quot; for 2004 The University of Tulsa's freshman class ranked 9th nationally among research universities in the number of National Merit Scholars per capita.&lt;ref&gt;<a>The
<p>The campus of the University of Tulsa centers on a wide, grassy, quad-like space known as &quot;The U.&quot; The predominant architectural style is English Gothic.
<p>The University of Tulsa is home to more than 200 student organizations, registered with and partially funded by the Student Association.</p>
<p>The Student Association is the University of Tulsa student government body.
The University of Tulsa currently fields a varsity team in eight men's sports and ten women's sports.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Sean Latham, editor of the <em><a>James Joyce Quarterly</a></em>, brought the 2003 <a>North American James Joyce Conference</a> to the University of Tulsa.</p>

<p> <strong>Utrecht University</strong> (<em>Universiteit Utrecht</em> in <a>Dutch</a>) is a <a>university</a> in <a>Utrecht</a>, <a>Netherlands</a>.
Utrecht University is led by the University Board, consisting of <a>Yvonne van Rooy</a> (President), prof.dr.
<p> :<em>This section incorporates text translated from the Dutch wikipedia article</em> Utrecht University was founded on March 26, 1636.
<p>Utrecht University flourished in the seventeenth century, despite of the competition with the older universities of <a>Leiden</a> (1575), <a>Franeker</a> (1585) and <a>Groningen</a> (1614) and the schools of <a>Harderwijk</a> (1599, university since 1648) and Amsterdam (1632).
<p>The <a>French occupants of the Netherlands</a> in 1806 degraded Utrecht University to '&#x00e9;cole secondaire' (high school), but after the establishment of the <a>Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> in 1813, Utrecht University regained its original rights.

<p> {{Infobox university |name              = Upper Iowa University |image = <a>220px|The Arch marks the west entrance to the Fayette campus, a gift from the graduating Class of 1909.</a>
}} Established in 1857, <strong>Upper Iowa University</strong> (UIU) is a <a>private</a> <a>institution of higher education</a> with its residential <a>campus</a> located in northeast <a>Iowa</a> near the <a>Volga River of Iowa</a> in the rural community of <a>Fayette, Iowa</a>, where around 900 students are enrolled.
<p>Upper Iowa University is fully accredited by the <a>Higher Learning Commission</a> of the <a>North Central Association of Colleges and Schools</a>.</p>
The Pioneering spirit: <em>Upper Iowa University celebrating 150 Years 1857-2007</em>.
<p>Upper Iowa University participates in the <a>North Central Association</a> (NCA) Academic Quality Improvement Program (AQIP), has a UIU chapter of the <a>Alpha Chi National College Honor Society</a>, and 165 student athletes were honored in 2010 for academic excellence.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.upperiowaathletics.com/</a>&lt;/ref&gt;  Average ACT is 22; average high school grade point average is 2.94; tuition for 2009-2010 is $22,350, with 100 percent of UIU students receiving need- and/or merit-based financial aid.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.petersons.com/collegeprofiles/Profile.aspx?inunid=9488&amp;reprjid=12&amp;sponsor=1&amp;tabid=10002</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p><a>thumb|right|200px|Upper Iowa University's <em>Team Peacock</em> has raised $350,000 to date riding RAGBRAI for student scholarships</a> UIU is recognized for being a military-friendly college by these publications--Military Advanced Education (MAE) magazine&#x2019;s &#x201c;3rd Annual Guide to Military-Friendly Colleges and Universities&#x201d; and the 2010 list for top-military friendly schools published by G.I. Jobs online magazine.&lt;ref&gt;Military
<p>Upper Iowa University awards more than $100,000 each year in merit-based scholarships to its current students.&lt;ref&gt;<a>2009
<p>Upper Iowa University has three international education centers located in the Pacific Rim. UIU offers undergraduate programs in business, communication and psychology to learners in Hong Kong, Malaysia and Singapore.
<p>In 2005, Upper Iowa University was accepted into full membership of the NCAA <a>Division II</a> athletics and became a member of the <a>Northern Sun Intercollegiate Conference</a> (NSIC).</p>

<p>The <strong>University of Utah</strong>, also known as <strong>the U</strong> or <strong>the U of U</strong>, is a <a>public</a>, <a>coeducational</a> <a>research university</a> in <a>Salt Lake City</a>, <a>Utah</a>, United States.
In 1892, the school's name was changed to the University of Utah, and <a>John R. Park</a> began arranging to obtain land belonging to the U.S. Army's <a>Fort Douglas</a> on the east bench of the <a>Salt Lake Valley</a>, where the university moved permanently in 1900.
health sciences complex and [[Utah Transit Authority|UTA]] <a>TRAX</a>]]The health sciences complex, at the northeast end of campus, includes the <a>University of Utah Medical Center</a>, <a>Primary Children's Medical Center</a>,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; the <a>Huntsman Cancer Institute</a>, the <a>Moran Eye Center</a>, and the Spencer Eccles Health Sciences Library.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
  <li><a>California State University Emeritus and Retired Faculty Association</a></li>

web | title=Bachelor of University Studies (B.U.S.) | url=<a>http://www.ugs.utah.edu/?pageId=1803</a> | publisher=University of Utah University College | accessdate=2009-05-18}}&lt;/ref&gt; In late 2009 the University announced that it would be adding a <a>Masters in Real Estate</a> program to their offerings.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The University of Utah has the only accredited <a>architecture</a> program in Utah,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; as well as the only <a>medical school</a>.&lt;ref
name=&quot;USUnivRankings_USNWR_Law&quot; &gt;{{cite web|url=<a>http://grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com/best-graduate-schools/top-law-schools/items/03157</a>|title=University of Utah (Quinney) - Best Law Schools|publisher=U.S. News and World Report|accessdate=2010-05-12}}&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The University of Utah was one of the original four nodes of <a>ARPANET</a>, the world's first <a>packet-switching</a> computer network and embryo of the current worldwide <a>Internet</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
name=&quot;ute traditions&quot; /&gt; In 1996 Swoop the Red Tailed Hawk was introduced as the new mascot of the University of Utah.

The University of Utah has a <a>dry campus</a>, meaning that alcohol is banned on campus.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The University of Utah tried to uphold its gun ban but the <a>Utah Supreme Court</a> rejected the ban in 2006.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>

<p> {{Infobox university |image_name=University_of_Chicago_Modern_Etched_Seal 1.svg |image_size=256px |image_alt=The seal of the University of Chicago.
|name=University of Chicago |motto=<em>Crescat scientia; vita excolatur</em> (<a>Latin</a>) |mottoeng=Let knowledge grow from more to more; and so be human life enriched&lt;ref name=&quot;Motto Translation&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |established=1890 |type=<a>Private</a> nondenominational coeducational |calendar= Quarter |president=<a>Robert Zimmer</a> |city=<a>Chicago</a> |state=<a>Illinois</a> |campus=<a>Urban</a>, 211&nbsp;acres (85&nbsp;ha)&lt;ref name=&quot;ffj&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |undergrad=5,134&lt;ref name=&quot;tcf&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |postgrad=10,304&lt;ref name=&quot;tcf&quot; /&gt; |faculty=2,168&lt;ref name=&quot;ffj&quot; /&gt; |staff=14,772 (including employees of the <a>University of Chicago Medical Center</a>)&lt;ref name=&quot;ffj&quot; /&gt; |athletics = <a>NCAA</a> <a>Division III</a> <a>UAA</a> |nickname=<a>Maroons</a> |mascot=<a>Phoenix</a>&lt;ref name=&quot;traditions&quot;/&gt; |affiliations = <a>Association of American Universities</a> <a>Committee on Institutional Cooperation</a> |endowment=<a>US $</a>5.578
&lt;/ref&gt; |nobel_laureates = 84&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Chicago Nobel Laureates</a>, University of Chicago Nobel Laureates&lt;/ref&gt; |website=<a>www.uchicago.edu</a>
|colors=Maroon  White &lt;ref name=&quot;traditions&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |logo= <a>260px|The University of Chicago Logo</a> |mascot=Phoenix |}} The <strong>University of Chicago</strong> (<strong>U of C</strong>, <strong>UC</strong>, or simply <strong>UChicago</strong>) is a <a>private</a>, <a>research university</a> in <a>Chicago</a>, <a>Illinois</a>, <a>USA</a>.
name=&quot;ucsmp&quot;&gt;{{cite web | title=The University of Chicago School Mathematics Project (UCSMP) | publisher=The University of Chicago | url=<a>http://socialsciences.uchicago.edu/ucsmp/</a>
It has a reputation of devotion to academic scholarship and <a>intellectualism</a>&lt;ref name=&quot;columbia&quot;&gt;{{cite web | title=The University of Chicago | publisher=The Fathom Archive (Columbia University) | url=<a>http://www.fathom.com/partners/uchic/index.html</a> | accessdate=July 30, 2006}} &quot;The University of Chicago was founded in 1892, and within a short time became internationally recognized as one of the world's great centers of scholarship, research, and teaching.&quot;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref
<p>The University consists of the <a>College of the University of Chicago</a>, various graduate programs and interdisciplinary committees organized into four divisions, six <a>professional school</a>s, and a school of <a>continuing education</a>.
name=&quot;nsf&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; University of Chicago scholars have played a role in the development of the <a>Chicago School of economics</a>, the <a>Chicago School of sociology</a>, the <a>law and economics</a> movement in legal analysis,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and the physics leading to <a>the world's first man-made, self-sustaining</a> <a>nuclear reaction</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
px|An early [[convocation]] ceremony at the University of Chicago]]</p>
<p>The University of Chicago was created and <a>incorporated</a> as a <a>coeducational</a>,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; secular institution in 1890 by the <a>American Baptist Education Society</a> and a donation from oil magnate and philanthropist <a>John D. Rockefeller</a>.
name=&quot;hutchins&quot; /&gt; In 1933, Hutchins proposed an unsuccessful plan to merge the University of Chicago and <a>Northwestern University</a> into a single university.&lt;ref
name=&quot;merger&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; During his term, the University of Chicago Hospitals (now called the <a>University of Chicago Medical Center</a>) finished construction and enrolled its first medical students,&lt;ref name=&quot;hospitalhistory&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; and the <a>Committee on Social Thought</a> was created.</p>
<p>[[File:ChicagoPileTeam.png|left|thumb|350px|The University of Chicago team that worked on the production of the world's first man-made, self-sustaining nuclear reaction, including [[Enrico Fermi]] in the front row|alt=A group of people in suits standing in three rows on the steps in front of a stone building.]]
<p>In 1978, <a>Hanna Holborn Gray</a>, then the provost and acting president of <a>Yale University</a>, became President of the University of Chicago, in which capacity she served for 15 years.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
In 2008, the University of Chicago announced plans to establish the <a>Milton Friedman Institute</a>.
Current construction projects include: the Jules and Gwen Knapp Center for Biomedical Discovery, a ten-story medical research center, as well as further additions to the medical campus of the <a>University of Chicago Medical Center</a>.&lt;ref
older buildings of the University of Chicago employ [[Collegiate Gothic]] architecture like that of the <a>University of Oxford</a>.
<p>The main campus of the University of Chicago consists of  in the Chicago neighborhoods of <a>Hyde Park</a> and <a>Woodlawn</a>, seven miles (11&nbsp;km) south of <a>downtown Chicago</a>.
<p>The first buildings of the University of Chicago campus, which make up what is now known as the Main Quadrangles, were part of a &quot;master plan&quot; conceived by two University of Chicago trustees and plotted by Chicago architect <a>Henry Ives Cobb</a>.&lt;ref
<p>The University of Chicago also maintains facilities apart from its main campus.
The University of Chicago also opened a new center in Beijing in fall 2010.</p>
<p>The University of Chicago is governed by a board of trustees.
<p>The academic bodies of the University of Chicago consist of the <a>College</a>, four divisions of graduate research, six professional schools, and the Graham School of General Studies (a <a>continuing education</a> school).
The University also contains a library system, the <a>University of Chicago Press</a>, the <a>University of Chicago Laboratory Schools</a>, and the <a>University of Chicago Medical Center</a>, and holds ties with a number of independent academic institutions, including <a>Fermilab</a> and <a>Argonne National Laboratory</a>.
Regulations and Procedures|accessdate=August 13, 2009|format=PDF|publisher=The University of Chicago|quote=Students register for three or four courses per quarter.
<p> The College of the University of Chicago grants <a>Bachelor of Arts</a> and <a>Bachelor of Science</a> degrees in 49 <a>academic major</a>s and 22 minors.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p><a>thumb|left|200px|The University of Chicago Lab Schools, a private day school run by the University</a> The University runs a number of academic institutions and programs apart from its undergraduate and postgraduate schools.
It operates the <a>University of Chicago Laboratory Schools</a> (a private <a>day school</a> for K-12 students and <a>day care</a>),&lt;ref name=&quot;lab&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; the <a>Sonia Shankman Orthogenic School</a> (a residential treatment program for those with behavioral and emotional problems),&lt;ref&gt; &lt;/ref&gt; and four public <a>charter school</a>s on the <a>South Side</a> of Chicago administered by the university's Urban Education Institute.&lt;ref
name=&quot;charter&quot;&gt; &lt;/ref&gt; In addition,  the Hyde Park Day School, a school for students with learning disabilities, maintains a location on the University of Chicago campus.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite
With two Illinois locations on the University of Chicago campus in Chicago and north suburban Northfield, HPDS is the only school of its kind in the Chicago area.|accessdate=September
9, 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt; Since 1983, the University of Chicago has maintained the <a>University of Chicago School Mathematics Project</a>, a mathematics program used in urban primary and secondary schools.&lt;ref
name=CAS&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; The University also operates the <a>University of Chicago Press</a>, the largest <a>university press</a> in the United States.&lt;ref
<p>The <a>University of Chicago Library</a> system encompasses six libraries&lt;ref name=&quot;libabout&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; that contain a total of 8.5&nbsp;million volumes, the 12th most among library systems in the United States.&lt;ref
<p>[[Image:Fermilab.jpg|thumb|left|225px|Aerial view of [[Fermilab]], one of the science research laboratories partially operated by the University of Chicago]]</p>
<p>In fiscal year 2006, the University of Chicago spent US$305,301,000 on scientific research.&lt;ref
<p>The University of Chicago has been the site of some important experiments and academic movements.
<p> There have been 85&nbsp;Nobel Laureates affiliated with the University of Chicago,&lt;ref name=&quot;uchicago1&quot;/&gt; 17 of whom were pursuing research or on faculty at the University at the time of the award announcement.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>In the 2009 Spring Quarter, the University of Chicago enrolled 4,920 students in the College, 3,633 students in its four graduate divisions, 5,088 students in its professional schools, and 14,000 students overall.&lt;ref&gt;
<p>In 2004, the University of Chicago claimed 133,155 living alumni.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The University of Chicago hosts 19 varsity sports teams: 10 men's teams and 9 women's teams,&lt;ref name=&quot;sportsfacts&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; all called the <a>Maroons</a>, with 585 students participating in the 2008&#x2013;2009 school year.&lt;ref
--&gt; Students at the University of Chicago run over 400 clubs and organizations known as Recognized Student Organizations (RSOs).&lt;ref
name=&quot;rsodatabase&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Among notable RSOs are the renowned improvisational comedy troupe <a>Off-Off Campus</a>, organizing committee for the <a>University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt</a>, the twice-weekly student newspaper <em><a>The Chicago Maroon</a></em>, and the University-owned radio station <a>WHPK-FM</a>.</p>
<p>There are fourteen <a>fraternities</a> and six <a>sororities</a> at the University of Chicago,&lt;ref name=&quot;Greek&quot; /&gt; as well as one co-ed community service fraternity, <a>Alpha Phi Omega</a>.&lt;ref&gt;
&lt;/ref&gt; Three of the sororities are members of the <a>National Panhellenic Conference</a>,&lt;ref name=&quot;frats&quot; /&gt; and ten of the fraternities form the University of Chicago Interfraternity Council.&lt;ref
<p> On-campus undergraduate students at the University of Chicago participate in a <a>house system</a> in which each student is assigned to one of the university's 10 <a>residence hall</a> buildings and to a smaller community within their residence hall called a &quot;house&quot;.
<p>[[Image:Scavrace1.jpg|thumb|180px|right|Qwazy Quad Rally, [[University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt|Scav Hunt]] 2005, item #38]]</p>
--&gt; {{Main|Doc Films|Summer Breeze (concert)|University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt}}</p>
<p>Every May since 1987, the University of Chicago has held the <a>University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt</a>, in which large teams of students compete to obtain notoriously esoteric items from a list.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
  <li><a>Scientific Research Activity at University of Chicago</a></li>

{{Infobox University  |name           = University of Canterbury |native_name    = Te Whare W&#x0101;nanga o Waitaha |image_name     = Canterbury uni arms.jpg
<p>The <strong>University of Canterbury</strong> (; postnominal abbreviation <strong><em><a>Cantuar</a>.</em></strong> or <strong><em>Cant.</em></strong>
<p><a>thumb|left|The James Hight building at the University of Canterbury</a></p>
Outside the Central Library, University of Canterbury, New Zealand</a> --&gt;</p>
<p>In 2010 <a>QS World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked the University of Canterbury 189th overall in the world, making it the third highest ranked university in New Zealand.
<p>The <a>University of Canterbury Students' Association</a> (UCSA)&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; operates on campus with its own radio station (<a>RDU</a>) and magazine (<a><em>Canta</em></a>).
The most prominent of these include the <a>University of Canterbury Engineering Society (ENSOC)</a>, the Law Society (LAWSOC), the Commerce Society (UCom), as well as the largest non-faculty clubs such as BYCSOC (Backyard Cricket Society), CUBA (<a>Canterbury University Boardriders' Association</a>), CurrySoc, <a>The Gentlemen's Club</a>, and <a>KAOS</a> (Killing As Organised Sport).
The <a>University of Canterbury Drama Society</a> (Dramasoc) achieved fame for its 1942-1969 Shakespeare productions under Dame <a>Ngaio Marsh</a>, but regularly performs as an active student- and alumni-run arts fixture in the small Christchurch theatre-scene.
<p>[[File:Arts Center Christchurch.JPG|thumb|right|Former University of Canterbury campus in the city centre, today the [[Christchurch Arts Centre]]]]</p>
In 1957 the name changed again to the present <em>University of Canterbury</em>.</p>
That year saw the dissolution of the federal system of tertiary education in New Zealand, and the University of Canterbury became an independent University awarding its own degrees.
Upon the UNZ's demise, <a>Canterbury Agricultural College</a> became a constituent college of the University of Canterbury, as <em>Lincoln College</em>.&lt;ref&gt;[<a>http://www.lincoln.ac.nz/story_images/952_LincolnUniversity_s3422.pdf</a> &lt;/ref&gt; Lincoln College became independent in 1990 as a full university in its own right.</p>
<p>With the dissolution of the University of New Zealand, the newly independent University of Canterbury devised its own coat of arms, <a>blazoned</a>: :<em>&quot;murrey a fleece argent, in base a plough or, and on a chief wavy or an open book proper bound murrey, edged and clasped or between a pall azure charged with four crosses formy fitchy or and a cross flory azure.&quot;</em>
  <li><strong><a>University of Canterbury</a></strong></li>
<p> <a>Category:University of Canterbury</a> <a>Canterbury</a> <a>Category:Film schools in New Zealand</a> <a>Category:Educational institutions established in 1873</a> <a>Category:Association of Commonwealth Universities</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox University  |name           = Victoria University |image          = <a>130px</a> |latin_name     =  |motto          = <em>Abeunt studia in mores</em>  |mottoeng       = Studies pass into character |established    = October 12, 1836 |affiliation    =  |type           = <a>Federated college</a> of the <a>University of Toronto</a> (1890&#x2013;) |endowment      = C$114 million&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |chancellor     = Wendy Cecil |president      = Paul W. Gooch |principal      = David Cook |undergrad      = 3,351 |former_names   = Upper Canada Academy (1836&#x2013;1841); Victoria College (1841&#x2013;1884)  |city           = <a>Toronto</a>  |province       = <a>Ontario</a>  |country        = <a>Canada</a>  |campus         = <a>Urban</a> |website        = <a>vicu.utoronto.ca</a>
}} <strong>Victoria University</strong> is a <a>federated school</a> of the <a>University of Toronto</a>, consisting of Victoria College and <a>Emmanuel College</a>.
Victoria University is somewhat separated from the rest of the university geographically, bordering <a>Queen's Park</a>, and being located on the eastern portion of the campus along with <a>St.
<p>Victoria University was formed in 1884 when Victoria College and <a>Albert University</a> federated with each other.
In 1890, Victoria University federated with the University of Toronto.
In 1892, Victoria University moved from Cobourg to its current campus on Queen's Park Crescent, south of <a>Bloor Street</a> (at Charles Street West), in Toronto.
<p>Built in 1961 and located at the south end of the quadrangle, the <strong>E.J. Pratt Library</strong> the main library of Victoria University, with some 250,000 volumes.
<p><a>thumb|left|Northrop Frye Hall</a> Victoria University is governed bicamerally by the Victoria University Board of Regents and the Victoria University Senate.
Victoria's governing charter was most recently amended in 1981, with the enactment of the Victoria University Act.&lt;ref&gt;
Victoria University Act www.vicu.utoronto.ca/about/senate/bylaws.htm&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Recently, the administration of Victoria University has been actively promoting international experiences as a part of the undergraduate student experience.[<a>http://www.vicu.utoronto.ca/Assets/Alumni/vicreports/Winter+07/President$!27s+Page.pdf?method=1</a>]</p>
<p>Centre for Reformation and Renaissance Studies (CRRS) is a research and teaching centre in Victoria University devoted to the study of the period from approximately 1350 to 1700.
Victoria College has both clubs and levy receivers, which are overseen by the Victoria University Students' Administrative Council (VUSAC)[<a>http://www.vusac.ca/</a>].
Over the past few years the theatre has been used as a lecture hall for University of Toronto students, an active learning space for Victoria University students groups, numerous concerts, theatrical productions, film screenings, and conferences.</p>
<p><a>thumb|Stephenson House</a>  <a>Stephenson House</a> is a community involvement residence at Victoria University, hosting ten undergraduate students per year.

<p>{{Infobox University | name            =  Victoria University | image_name      =  Logo_vu.gif
| established     =  1916 | type            =  <a>Public</a> | endowment       =   | chancellor      =  George Pappas | vice_chancellor =  Professor Elizabeth Harman | city            =  Melbourne | state           =  | country         =  Australia | undergrad       =  23,999 (2008) &lt;ref name=&quot;AnnualReport08&quot;&gt;<a>Victoria University Annual Report 2008</a>&lt;/ref&gt; | postgrad        =  4,568 (2008) &lt;ref name=&quot;AnnualReport08&quot; /&gt; | other           =  28,587 TAFE (2008) &lt;ref name=&quot;AnnualReport08&quot; /&gt; | staff           =  2,854 (2008) &lt;ref name=&quot;AnnualReport08&quot; /&gt; | campus          =  Urban | affiliations    =  <a>ASAIHL</a> | website         =  <a>www.vu.edu.au</a>
<p><strong>Victoria University</strong> (VU) is a multi-sector tertiary institution (higher education and <a>TAFE</a>) based in Melbourne, Australia with 10 campuses.</p>
<p>Victoria University's Faculty o&#x2202; Business and Law is one of the largest and prestigious business schools in Australia, with over 10,000 students studying at campuses spread across the city's west, as well as two city campuses.
<p>All graduates of Victoria University and its forerunner institutions are alumni of VU.
<p>Victoria University emphasises research and research training that is of relevance to the community,industry and government &#x2013; both nationally and internationally, but particularly in the western region of Melbourne.
<a>Victoria University has five research centres</a> four institutes and two research groups.</p>
<p>Victoria University campuses are located across Melbourne's western suburbs and the city centre.
<p>Victoria University courses are also delivered by a number of affiliates in Asia.
&lt;ref&gt;<a>Victoria University Performance 2006</a>&lt;/ref&gt;  Two of the largest affiliates are <a>Sunway University College</a> in <a>Malaysia</a> and <a>Liaoning University</a> in China.</p>
<p><a>|thumb|left|200px|Victoria University City Campus in Queens Street</a> The City Queen Campus occupies two heritage buildings in the heart of Melbourne's legal precinct.
295 Queen Street houses the University's School of Law, the Law Library, The Sir Zelman Cowen Centre for Continuing Legal Education, and Victoria University's Judicial Administration and Justice Studies Institute.
<p>Victoria University (VU) was founded in 1916 as Footscray Technical School.
After successive mergers with TAFE colleges in Melbourne&#x2019;s western suburbs, Victoria University of Technology was established by legislation of the Victorian Parliament in 1990.
It was renamed Victoria University in 2005.</p>

<p><a>de:Victoria University</a> <a>it:Universit&#x00e0; di Victoria</a> <a>ja:&#x30d3;&#x30af;&#x30c8;&#x30ea;&#x30a2;&#x5927;&#x5b66; (&#x30aa;&#x30fc;&#x30b9;&#x30c8;&#x30e9;&#x30ea;&#x30a2;)</a> <a>pt:Victoria University</a> <a>ta:&#x0bb5;&#x0bbf;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b9f;&#x0bcb;&#x0bb0;&#x0bbf;&#x0baf;&#x0bbe; &#x0baa;&#x0bb2;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb2;&#x0bc8;&#x0b95;&#x0bcd;&#x0b95;&#x0bb4;&#x0b95;&#x0bae;&#x0bcd;</a> <a>zh:&#x7dad;&#x591a;&#x5229;&#x4e9e;&#x5927;&#x5b78; (&#x6fb3;&#x5927;&#x5229;&#x4e9e;)</a></p>
<p>{{About|the New Zealand university|other universities with &quot;Victoria&quot; in their name|Victoria University (disambiguation)}} {{Infobox university |name           = Victoria University of Wellington |native_name    = Te Whare W&#x0101;nanga o Te &#x016a;poko o te Ika a M&#x0101;ui |image_name     = Vuw-logo.jpg
<p><a>thumb|Victoria University of Wellington's Pipitea Campus: the Faculty of Law on the left</a> [[Image:Wellington Railway Station west wing.jpg|thumb|left|Victoria
University of Wellington's Pipitea Campus: the west wing of [[Wellington Railway Station]]]] [[Image:Hunter_Building.jpg|thumb|Victoria University of Wellington's Kelburn Campus: the [[Hunter Building]]]] <a>thumb|Victoria University of Wellington's Kelburn Campus</a></p>
The original name was <a>Victoria University College</a>, but on the dissolution of the <a>University of New Zealand</a> in 1961 Victoria or &quot;Vic&quot; became the independent Victoria University of Wellington, conferring its own degrees.</p>
<p>The Victoria University of Wellington Library &lt;ref&gt;<a>the Victoria University of Wellington Library</a>&lt;/ref&gt; was established in 1899.
<p>Victoria University of Wellington has more than 40 research centres and institutes, including</p>

<p><a>de:Victoria-Universit&#x00e4;t Wellington</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x0648;&#x06cc;&#x06a9;&#x062a;&#x0648;&#x0631;&#x06cc;&#x0627; &#x062f;&#x0631; &#x0648;&#x0644;&#x06cc;&#x0646;&#x06af;&#x062a;&#x0648;&#x0646;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; Victoria de Wellington</a> <a>ko:&#xbe45;&#xd1a0;&#xb9ac;&#xc544; &#xb300;&#xd559;&#xad50; &#xc6f0;&#xb9c1;&#xd134;</a> <a>ja:&#x30f4;&#x30a3;&#x30af;&#x30c8;&#x30ea;&#x30a2;&#x5927;&#x5b66;&#x30a6;&#x30a7;&#x30ea;&#x30f3;&#x30c8;&#x30f3;</a> <a>no:Victoria University of Wellington</a> <a>pl:Uniwersytet Wiktorii</a> <a>zh:&#x60e0;&#x7075;&#x987f;&#x7ef4;&#x591a;&#x5229;&#x4e9a;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a></p>
<p>{{Infobox university |name=Wabash College |image= |motto=Wabash Always Fights |type=<a>private</a> all-male |endowment=$272.2
}} <strong>Wabash College</strong> is a small, private, <a>liberal arts college</a> for <a>men</a>, located in <a>Crawfordsville, Indiana</a>.
<p>Wabash College was founded in 1832 by a number of men including several <a>Dartmouth College</a> graduates.
<p>Joseph F. Tuttle, after whom Tuttle Grade School in Crawfordsville was named in 1906, (and Tuttle Middle School in 1960), became President of Wabash College in 1862 and served for 30&nbsp;years.
<p>According to <a>Forbes magazine's</a> 2010 ranking for academic institutions, <em>America's Best Colleges</em>, Wabash College ranked 42nd.[<a>http://www.forbes.com/lists/2010/94/best-colleges-10_Americas-Best-Colleges_Rank_2.html</a>]
[<a>http://colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com/best-colleges/liberal-arts-rankings/page+3</a>] Wabash College is also listed in <a>Loren Pope</a>'s <em><a>Colleges That Change Lives</a></em>.</p>
<p>The <a>student government</a>, referred to collectively as the Student Body of Wabash College, comprises <a>executive</a> and <a>legislative</a> branches.
<p>The Student Senate of Wabash College is the legislative authority, consisting of <a>senators</a> from each residence hall and fraternity, four <a>representatives</a> from each of the three underclasses, and the chairmen of the Senate's standing committees.
<p>The Senior Council of Wabash College is a special quasi-legislative body comprising the presidents of certain student organizations and self-selected at-large councilmen.
Power to interpret the Constitution of the Student Body of Wabash College is vested in the legislature; questions of interpretation are generally delegated to the Constitution, Bylaw, and Policy Review Committee.</p>
Every year since 1911, Wabash College has played rival <a>DePauw University</a> in a football game called the <a>Monon Bell</a> Classic.
Wabash College is a member of the <a>North Coast Athletic Conference</a>.
The rallying cheer of Wabash College athletics is &quot;Wabash always fights.&quot;
Wabash College competes in Men's Intercollegiate Baseball, Basketball, Tennis, Cross Country, Track and Field, Golf, Football, Soccer, Swimming &amp; Diving and Wrestling.</p>
<p>:<em>See also: <a>Monon Bell Classic</a></em> Voted &quot;Indiana's Best College Sports Rivalry&quot; by viewers of <a>ESPN</a> in 2005, DePauw University and Wabash College play each November &#x2014; in the last regular season football game of the year for both teams &#x2014; for the right to keep or reclaim the Monon Bell.

}} <strong>Williams College</strong> is a private <a>liberal arts college</a> located in <a>Williamstown</a>, <a>Massachusetts</a>, <a>United States</a>.

In 1887, as the college continued to grow under the presidency of <a>Timothy Dwight V</a>, <em><a>Yale College</a></em> was renamed <em>Yale University</em>.

<p>The <a>Board of Trustees</a> of Williams College has 25 members and is the governing authority of the College.&lt;ref
<p>College Council (CC) is the student government of Williams College.
<p>Williams College is the site of the <a>Hopkins Observatory</a>, the oldest extant astronomical observatory in the United States.&lt;ref

<p>Women studied at Yale University as early as 1876, in graduate-level programs at the <a>Yale Graduate School of Arts and Sciences</a>.</p>
<p> Much of Yale University's staff, including most maintenance staff, dining hall employees, and administrative staff, are unionized.
Also included in FHUE are the dietary workers at <a>Yale-New Haven Hospital</a>, who are members of <a>1199 SEIU</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>YaleUnions.org</a>&lt;/ref&gt;  In addition to these unions, officers of the Yale University Police Department are members of the Yale Police Benevolent Association, which affiliated in 2005 with the <a>Connecticut Organization for Public Safety Employees</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;

<p>Notable nonresidential campus buildings and landmarks include <a>Battell Chapel</a>, <a>Beinecke Rare Book Library</a>, <a>Harkness Tower</a>, <a>Ingalls Rink</a>, Kline Biology Tower, <a>Osborne Memorial Laboratories</a>, <a>Payne Whitney Gymnasium</a>, <a>Peabody Museum of Natural History</a>, Sterling Hall of Medicine, <a>Sterling Law Buildings</a>, <a>Sterling Memorial Library</a>, <a>Woolsey Hall</a>, <a>Yale Center for British Art</a>, <a>Yale University Art Gallery</a>, and <a>Yale Art &amp; Architecture Building</a>.</p>

<p>In addition to the Yale University Police Department, founded in 1894,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; a variety of safety services are available including blue phones, a <a>safety escort</a>, and a shuttle service.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Memorial Library|right|thumb|Yale University's [[Sterling Memorial Library]], as seen from <a>Maya Lin's</a> sculpture, <em>Women's Table</em>.
<a>Yale University Library</a>, which holds over 12 million volumes, is the second-largest university collection in the United States.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
The <a>Yale University Art Gallery</a> is the country's first university-affiliated art museum.
The <a>Yale University Collection of Musical Instruments</a>, affiliated with the Yale School of Music, is perhaps the least well-known of Yale's collections, because its hours of opening are restricted.</p>

<p><strong>Columbia Business School</strong> (<strong>CBS</strong>) is the <a>business school</a> of <a>Columbia University</a> in <a>Manhattan</a>, <a>New York City</a>.
<p>Columbia Business School is known for its close ties to <a>Wall Street</a> and the seminal work completed in the field of <a>Finance</a> by professors <a>Benjamin Graham</a> and <a>David Dodd</a>.
<p>In 1945, Columbia Business School authorized the awarding of the <a>Master of Business Administration</a> degree (MBA).
Glenn Hubbard</a> became Columbia Business School's eleventh dean.
<p>Today, Columbia Business School is primarily housed in Uris Hall, a recently renovated 1960s structure at the center of Columbia's <a>Morningside Heights</a> campus.
<p>In October 2010, Columbia Business School announced that alumnus <a>Henry Kravis</a>, the billionaire co-founder of private-equity firm <a>Kohlberg Kravis Roberts</a> (KKR &amp; Co.), pledged $100 million to fund expansion of Columbia Business School, the largest gift in its history.
name=&quot;Columbia Business School&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; </p>
name=&quot;http&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Among the most popular electives at Columbia Business School are the Economics of Strategic Behavior, Financial Statement Analysis and Earnings Quality, Launching New Ventures, Modern Political Economy, and the Seminar in Value Investing.&lt;ref
According to <em><a>Forbes</a></em> magazine, 90% of billionaires with MBAs who derived their fortunes from finance obtained their master's degree from one of three schools: <a>Harvard Business School</a>, Columbia Business School, or <a>The Wharton School</a> at the <a>University of Pennsylvania</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Forbes:
Columbia Business School offers the following areas of focus:&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>As part of its <a>MBA curriculum</a>, Columbia Business School offers the Value Investing Program at the prestigious <a>Heilbrunn Center for Graham &amp; Dodd Investing</a>, for a handful of selected business school students.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Columbia Business School's <a>Entrepreneurship Program</a> strives to provide students with the skills required for venturing and providing opportunities for them to start an entrepreneurial career in four career paths: entrepreneurship in new ventures, entrepreneurship in large organizations, private equity financing and social entrepreneurship.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
name=&quot;Columbia Business School&quot;/&gt;</p>
<p>Columbia Business School's <a>Executive MBA (EMBA) Program</a> is a 20-month graduate program designed specifically for businesspeople that are looking to enhance their education without interrupting their careers.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Columbia Business School's Executive Education programs offer graduate Executive Certificate Programs such as the <a>Columbia Senior Executive Program</a> (CSEP),&lt;ref name=&quot;CSEP Program&quot;&gt;[<a>http://www4.gsb.columbia.edu/execed/programs/detail/10407/Columbia+Senior+Executive+Program</a>&quot;CSEP
<p>Columbia Business School&#x2019;s eminence is rooted in the strength, leadership and experience of its 136 full-time faculty members,&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; including <a>Joseph Stiglitz</a>, the 2001 <a>Nobel laureate</a> in economics who also teaches at the university's <a>School of International and Public Affairs</a>; <a>Ray Fisman</a>, the Lambert Family Professor of Social Enterprise; and <a>Bernd Schmitt</a>, the Robert D. Calkins Professor of International Business.
<p>Research centers, special programs, institutes, and cross-disciplinary areas at Columbia Business School include:&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Held each year on the first Monday in May, the Annual Dinner is a highlight of the Columbia Business School calendar and brings together more than 1,000 business leaders, faculty members, students, alumni and friends for an evening of support for the School's many programs and initiatives.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Since 1977, two awards have been presented at each Annual Dinner, the Distinguished Leadership in Business Award and the Distinguished Leadership in Government Award, to honorees whose careers exemplify the professional, ethical, and leadership principles that define Columbia Business School.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>The <a>Columbia Business School Follies</a> is a student club that works throughout each semester to put together a production in which students write, choreograph, and perform <a>comedy skits</a>.
<p>Columbia Business School has over 39,000 living alumni.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www4.gsb.columbia.edu/about/facts/alumni</a>&lt;/ref&gt;
For a further listing of notable Columbia Business School Alumni see: <a>Columbia Business School alumni</a> and <a>List of Columbia University people</a>.</p>

<p>The <strong>Jagiellonian University</strong> (, often shortened to <em>UJ</em>; historical names: , University of Krakow, Krak&#x00f3;w Academy, The Main Crown School, Main School of Krak&#x00f3;w) was established in 1364 by <a>Casimir III the Great</a> in <a>Krak&#x00f3;w</a>.
<p>In 1817 it was renamed <em>Jagiellonian University</em> to commemorate Poland's <a>Jagiellonian dynasty</a>, which had revived the University of Krakow after it had fallen upon hard times.&lt;ref
name=&quot;officialhistory&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; In 2006 <em><a>The Times Higher Education Supplement</a></em> ranked Jagiellonian University as the top Polish university.&lt;ref&gt;Times
Jagiellonian University was the first university in Europe to establish independent chairs in <a>Mathematics</a> and <a>Astronomy</a>.</p>

<p>{{Infobox university |name               = Manchester Metropolitan University |native_name        =  |latin_name         = |image_name         = MMU logo.png
-2.23872 |campus             = All Saints, Aytoun, Hollings, Elizabeth Gaskell, <a>Didsbury</a>, <a>Alsager</a>, <a>Crewe</a> |free_label         =  |free               =  |colours            = Blue, turquoise, burgundy, gold &lt;br /&gt;&lt;table cellspacing=&quot;0&quot; width=&quot;100%&quot;&gt;     &lt;/table&gt; |mascot             =  |affiliations       = <a>University Alliance</a>&lt;br/&gt; <a>Association of Commonwealth Universities</a>&lt;br/&gt;<a>NWUA</a>&lt;br/&gt;<a>Association of MBAs</a>&lt;br/&gt;<a>EUA</a> |website            = <a>http://www.mmu.ac.uk/</a> |logo               =  }} <strong>Manchester Metropolitan University</strong> (<strong>MMU</strong>) is a university in <a>North West England</a>.
<p>It was granted university status as &quot;Manchester Metropolitan University&quot; by the <a>Privy Council</a> on 15 September 1992 under the provisions of the <a>Further and Higher Education Act, 1992</a>.
The Students' Union MMUnion exists to represent all members at the Manchester Metropolitan University and students on accredited external courses.
<p>This partial list of alumni of Manchester Metropolitan University includes those who attended institutions which became part of present-day MMU.

<p>The <a>Archives of the University of Glasgow</a> are the central place of deposit for the records of the University, created and accumulated since its foundation in 1451.</p>
