<p>The Johns Hopkins University Library system houses more than 3.6 million volumes.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The Johns Hopkins University Press is the publishing division of the Johns Hopkins University.
Since 1993, the Johns Hopkins University Press has run <a>Project MUSE</a>, a large online collection of over 250 full-text, peer-reviewed journals in the humanities and social sciences.
<p>The <strong>University of Glasgow</strong> is the <a>fourth-oldest university</a> in the <a>English-speaking world</a> and one of Scotland's four <a>ancient universities</a>.
<p>Since 1870, the main University campus has been located on <a>Gilmorehill</a> in the West End of the city.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow :: Location, maps and travel :: Location, maps and travel&lt;!-- Bot generated title --&gt;</a>&lt;/ref&gt; Additionally, there are a number of university buildings elsewhere in the city, a facility at <a>Loch Lomond</a>, the <a>University Marine Biological Station Millport</a> and the <a>Crichton Campus</a> in <a>Dumfries</a> (which is jointly operated alongside a number of other institutions).</p>
<p>[[Image:University of Glasgow Gilbert Scott Building - Feb 2008-2.jpg|thumb|left|The
The University of Glasgow was founded in 1451 A.D by a <a>papal bull</a> of <a>Pope Nicholas V</a>, at the suggestion of <a>King James II</a>, giving Bishop <a>William Turnbull</a> permission to add the university to the city's cathedral.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Who, Where and When</a>, retrieved 22 April 2006 &lt;/ref&gt; It is the second-oldest university in Scotland, and the fourth-oldest in the English-speaking world.
<p>[[Image:Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum from the University of Glasgow Tower.jpg|thumb|left|The
view over the [[Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum]] from the University of Glasgow tower]] The University's teaching quality was assessed in 2009 to be among the top 10 in the United Kingdom, along with its reputation as a &quot;research powerhouse&quot;, whose income from annual research contracts also placing among the top 10 the UK.
The university overall generates a total income of over &#x00a3;421,000,000 per year- also amongst the top 10 in the UK.&lt;ref name=&quot;autogenerated3&quot;&gt;<a>University of Glasgow :: Facts and figures :: Facts and figures&lt;!--
The University aims to be recognised as one of the UK's top 10 universities and as one of the world's top 50 research-intensive universities.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Building on Excellence</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Twenty-three subject areas, and 96 per cent of staff, were awarded 5 or 5* ratings in the 2001 <a>Research Assessment Exercise</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Facts and Figures 2005 - Research</a>, retrieved 22 April 2006 &lt;/ref&gt;</p>
As well as this there is the Garscube Estate in <a>Bearsden</a>, housing the <a>Veterinary School</a> and much of the University's sports facilities, the <a>Dental School</a> in the city centre, and the Crichton campus in Dumfries, operated jointly by the University of Glasgow, the <a>University of the West of Scotland</a> and the <a>Open University</a>.
<p><a>right|thumb|200px|&lt;center&gt;The University of Glasgow in 1650.</a>
<p>[[Image:Tower of The University of Glasgow.jpg|thumb|250px|The
Scotland - Universities - The University of Glasgow</a>&lt;/ref&gt; An illustration of the Main Building currently features on the reverse side of the current series of <a>&#x00a3;100 notes</a> issued by the <a>Clydesdale Bank</a>.&lt;ref
<p>The University's <a>Hunterian Museum</a> resides in the Main Building, and the related Hunterian Gallery is housed in buildings adjacent to the University Library.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Facts and Figures 2005 - Visitors</a>, retrieved 22 April 2006 &lt;/ref&gt; The latter includes &quot;The Mackintosh House&quot;, a rebuilt terraced house designed by, and furnished after, architect <a>Charles Rennie Mackintosh</a>.</p>
<p>&lt;!-- Deleted image removed: <a>left||thumb|374px|Wolfson Medical School</a>  --&gt; The Wolfson <a>Medical School</a> Building, with its award-winning glass-fronted atrium, opened in 2002,&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Wolfson Medical School Building</a>, retrieved 22 April 2006 &lt;/ref&gt; and in 2003, the St Andrews Building was opened, housing the Faculty of Education.
The <a>Crichton campus</a>, designed to meet the needs for tertiary education in an area far from major concentrations of population, is operated jointly by the University of Glasgow, the <a>University of the West of Scotland</a> and the <a>Open University</a>.
It offers a modular undergraduate curriculum, leading to one of a small number of liberal arts degrees, as well as providing the region's only access to postgraduate study.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow, Crichton Campus, Dumfries</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>As well as these teaching campuses the University has halls of residence in and around the North-West of the city, accommodating a total of approximately 3,500 students.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Facts and Figures 2005 - Accommodation</a>, retrieved 22 April 2006 &lt;/ref&gt; These are the Murano Street halls in Maryhill; Wolfson halls on the Garscube Estate; Queen Margaret halls, in <a>Kelvinside</a>; Cairncross House and Kelvinhaugh Gate, in <a>Yorkhill</a>.
<p>The University's constitution, academic regulations, and appointments are authoritatively described in the University calendar,&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - University Calendar</a>&lt;/ref&gt; while other aspects of its story and constitution are detailed in a separate &quot;history&quot; document.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Who,
Where and When: The History &amp; Constitution of the University of Glasgow</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The current principal is Professor <a>Anton Muscatelli</a> who replaced Sir <a>Muir Russell</a> in October 2009.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - University News - New Principal for the University of Glasgow</a>, retrieved 2 October 2009 &lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The current Secretary of Court is Mr. David Newall.&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Facts and Figures 2005 - Senior officers</a>, retrieved 22 April 2006 &lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>[[Image:AdamSmith.jpg|thumb|right|[[Adam Smith]]]] There are currently four <a>Colleges</a> within the University of Glasgow, each containing a number of Schools.
<p>Many distinguished figures have taught, worked and studied at the University of Glasgow, including six Nobel laureates and two <a>Prime Ministers</a>, <a>Sir Henry Campbell-Bannerman</a> and <a>Andrew Bonar Law</a>.
<p><a>thumb|right|250px|The Glasgow University Union's building at the bottom of University Avenue</a>  In addition to the Students' Representative Council, students are commonly members of one of the University's two <a>students' union</a>s, the Glasgow University Union (GUU) and the Queen Margaret Union (QMU).&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Glasgow - Facts and Figures 2005 - Student organisations and activities</a>, retrieved 22 April 2006 &lt;/ref&gt;  These are largely social and cultural institutions, providing their members with facilities for debating, dining, recreation, socialising, and drinking, and both have a number of meeting rooms available for rental to members.

<p>{{Infobox University | name = Hiram College | image = <a>center|100px</a> | motto = <em>Fiat Lux</em> | mottoeng = <a>Let there be light</a> | established = March 1, 1850 | type = <a>Private</a>, <a>Liberal Arts College</a> | endowment = <a>US$</a>54.9
<p><strong>Hiram College</strong> ( ) is a private <a>liberal arts college</a> located in <a>Hiram, Ohio</a>.
Founded by Amos Sutton Hayden of the <a>Disciples of Christ</a> Church in 1850, the institution has, since its first days, been nonsectarian and coeducational, and throughout its existence Hiram College has sustained this egalitarian tradition of educating men and women from diverse backgrounds.
Hiram College is accredited by <a>The Higher Learning Commission</a> of the <a>North Central Association of Colleges and Schools</a>.
The school attained collegiate rank in 1867 and changed its name to Hiram College.&lt;ref
<p>Three years after the Institute attained collegiate rank and became known as Hiram College, Burke A. Hinsdale, who had been a student of Garfield's, was appointed president.
Because of the fairly brief terms of the two presidents who preceded him, Hinsdale is known as the first permanent president of Hiram College.
<p>In September 2004, <a>Thomas V. Chema</a> was appointed as the 21st president of Hiram College.</p>
<p><a>thumb|250px|left|Hiram College Athletic Complex</a> <a>100px|thumb|right|Athletics logo</a> <a>100px|thumb|right|Athletics logo</a> </p>
The Hiram College basketball team, competing as the United States national team, won the <a>1904 Olympic</a> gold medal in <a>St.
<p>The Hiram College undergraduate chapter of the <a>Association for Computing Machinery</a> is a club for technology enthusiasts and students with interest in computer science.
The Hiram College Association for Computing Machinery meets periodically throughout the academic year.</p>
<p>Established in 1929, Phi Gamma Epsilon (or &quot;Phi Gams&quot;) is currently the oldest existing Greek social club at Hiram College.
<a>thumb|250px|right|The Kennedy Center</a> Another one of the social clubs at Hiram College is Delta Chi Lambda.
<p>Terrier Productions is Hiram College's film and video production club.
<p>Hiram College created its first marching band in Spring of 2006 emerging from an already established pep band.
The first marching band in Hiram College history sprang from student initiative.

Wagner</a> |city=<a>Druid Hills</a> |state=<a>Georgia</a> |country= US|coor= |students=12,756 |undergrad=6,890 |postgrad=5,865 |campus=<a>Suburb</a>an&lt;br /&gt;631 acres (2.6 km&#x00b2;) |nickname=Emory Eagles |colors=Blue and Gold  |endowment=<a>US $</a>4.7 <a>billion</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; |athletics = <a>NCAA</a> <a>Division III</a> <a>UAA</a> |affiliations = <a>Southern Association of Colleges and Schools</a>, <a>AAU</a> |website= <a>Emory.edu</a>
<p><strong>Emory University</strong> is a private research university located in the metropolitan <a>Atlanta</a> area of <a>Druid Hills, Georgia</a>.
The school initially struggled financially until a generous land-grant by <a>Asa Candler</a>, the president of the <a>Coca-Cola Company</a>, allowed the small college to move to metropolitan Atlanta in 1915 and become rechartered as Emory University.</p>
<p><strong></strong> <a>200px|left|thumb|Glenn Memorial United Methodist Church near the main entrance of Emory University</a></p>
name=&quot;english&quot;&gt;English, Thomas H. <em>Emory University 1915&#x2013;1965: A Semicentennial History</em> (Atlanta: Emory University, 1966).&lt;/ref&gt;
<p><a>175px|left|thumb|Administration Building</a>The College of Arts and Sciences is the undergraduate institution of Emory University with 66 majors, 53 minors, 17 joint concentrations, and 10 interdepartmental programs leading to a bachelor's degree.
The <a>Oxford College of Emory University</a>, located in <a>Oxford, Georgia</a>, enrolls about 700 students.
The <a>Emory University School of Medicine</a> enrolls approximately 425 medical students, 1,000 residents and fellows, and 350 allied health students.
<p>There are six degree programs within the <a>Emory University School of Medicine</a>: M.D., M.D./PhD, Physician Assistant (MMSc), Medical Imaging (BMSc), Anesthesiology and Patient Care (MMSc), and Physical Therapy (DPT).
<p>Students in the <a>Emory University School of Law</a> may earn a Doctor of Law degree (JD), a Doctor of Judicia Science (SJD) or one of four dual degrees with the Goizueta Business School, Candler School of Theology, or Rollins School of Public Health.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Degrees Awarded (2009-2010)|publisher=Emory University|date=2010-09-01 |accessdate=2010-10-20}}&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Many of the graduate schools of Emory University were ranked as some of the best and most competitive in their fields by <em>U.S. News and World Report</em> in 2010.
<p>[[Image:Thompson dooley.jpg|120px|right|thumb|Dooley, the unofficial [[mascot]] of Emory University]] Traditions at Emory include Dooley, the &quot;Spirit of Emory&quot; and the unofficial mascot of the university.
Dooley's Week culminates with Dooley's Ball, a grand celebration that takes place in the center of campus on McDonough Field held in celebration of Dooley and Emory University.
<h3>Emory University Transforming Community Project</h3>
<p>In 2005, the Emory University president&#x2019;s office began a five-year program called the Transforming Community Project (TCP).
The first five years of TCP's work engaged all sectors of the Emory University community in a process of discovery and dialogue about Emory&#x2019;s racial history.
campus between main building and [[mensa]] (the university canteen)]] The University of Cologne is a statutory corporation (K&#x00f6;rperschaft des &#x00f6;ffentlichen Rechts), operated by the Federal State of <a>North Rhine-Westphalia</a>. </p>
<li>The 2005 independent film <em>Kathy T</em> (also known as <em>Kathy T Gives Good Hoover</em>), about a college student whose life becomes more exciting after he reads some graffiti about Kathy T and decides to track her down, was written and directed by Emory University professor of film studies Ken Lieberman.
<li>Scenes from <em><a>The Simple Life of Noah Dearborn</a></em>, a 1999 made-for-TV movie about a 91-year-old carpenter that must protect his land from being turned into a strip mall were shot on Emory University&#x2019;s Druid Hills campus.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</li>

<p><strong>Los Angeles Pierce College</strong>, also known as <strong>Pierce College</strong>, <strong>Pierce</strong>, is a two-year <a>community college</a> that serves more than 23,000 students in the northern <a>Chalk Hills</a> of <a>Woodland Hills</a>, a community within the <a>San Fernando Valley</a> region of the <a>city of Los Angeles</a>, <a>California</a>.</p>
Nine years later, in 1956, the school was renamed to <em>Los Angeles Pierce College</em>, retaining the name of its founder, Dr. Pierce, as well as his commitment to agricultural and veterinary study.
[[Image:RustyTankAndBarn.jpg|thumb|right|300px|The western [[rural]] Farm Area, at Los Angeles Pierce College in <a>Woodland Hills</a>.]]
<p>The Associated Students Organization (ASO) is the official Student Government of the 23,000 students at Los Angeles Pierce College.

<p>{{Infobox University |name        = University of Cologne |native_name = Universit&#x00e4;t zu K&#x00f6;ln |image_name  = Universitaet zu Koeln-Siegel.jpg
<p>The <strong>University of Cologne</strong> (<a>German</a> <strong>Universit&#x00e4;t zu K&#x00f6;ln</strong>) is one of the oldest <a>universities</a> in <a>Europe</a> and, with over 44,000 students, one of the largest universities in <a>Germany</a>.
<p>In 2010 <a>QS World University Rankings</a>&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; ranked the University of Vienna 143rd overall in the world.
<p><a>thumb|lecture hall</a>  The University of Cologne maintains eighteen official partnerships&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Cologne, partner universities</a>&lt;/ref&gt; with universities from ten countries.
In addition, Cologne has further cooperations&lt;ref&gt;<a>University of Cologne, cooperation agreements</a>&lt;/ref&gt; with more than 260 other universities.

|image_size     = 150px |name           = Lehigh University |motto          = Homo minister et interpres naturae (<em>Man, the servant and interpreter of nature</em>) |established    = 1865 |type           = <a>Private</a> |calendar       = Semester |endowment      = $978&nbsp;million&lt;ref&gt;As of December 31, 2009.
<p><strong>Lehigh University</strong> is a <a>private</a>, co-educational university located in <a>Bethlehem, Pennsylvania</a>, in the <a>Lehigh Valley</a> region of the United States.
While the College of Arts and Sciences is the largest college today, home to roughly 40% percent of the university's students,&lt;ref name=&quot;class_summary&quot;&gt;<a>Class Summary</a>&lt;/ref&gt; the university is historically known for engineering&lt;ref name=&quot;academicinfo&quot;&gt;<a>Introduction to Lehigh University at AcademicInfo.com</a>&lt;/ref&gt; and business.
name=&quot;usnews&quot;&gt;<a>Lehigh University at a Glance</a> from </em><a>US News &amp; World Report</a><em>.&lt;/ref&gt;
name=&quot;princeton_review&quot;&gt;<a>Lehigh University on the Princeton Review</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</em></p>
<p>Lehigh University offers undergraduate enrollment in all colleges but the College of Education: the P.C. Rossin School of Engineering and Applied Science, the College of Business and Economics, and the College of Arts and Sciences.
<p>[[Image:Lafayette2006PLchampsboard.JPG|thumb|300px|right|[[Lafayette College]] won the 142nd edition of &quot;The Rivalry&quot; against Lehigh University, but lost the most recent contests in 2009 and 2010.]]
<a>100px|left|Lehigh University Mountain Hawks logo</a> Called the Engineers until 1995, Lehigh's teams are now officially known as <a>the Mountain Hawks</a>.
<p>{{Main|Lehigh-Lafayette football games (The Rivalry)}} Lehigh University is notable for its rivalry in sports and academics with nearby <a>Lafayette College</a>.
<p>Based on the experience of Lehigh engineers who went into industry&lt;ref name=&quot;Scrapbook&quot;&gt;Plotnicki, Rita M., <em>Looking Back: A Lehigh Scrapbook,</em> Lehigh University, 1991&lt;/ref&gt; a College of Business &amp; Economics was added in 1910.
<p>In July 2008, <a>the Dalai Lama</a> held a public lecture and conducted a series of teachings at Lehigh University.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Lehigh

<p>{{Infobox University | name            = University of California, Irvine | motto           = <em>Fiat lux</em> (<a>Latin</a>) | mottoeng        = <em><a>Let there be light</a></em> | image_name      = Ucirvine-seal.png

| address         = University of California, Irvine: Main Campus&lt;br /&gt;University of California, Irvine&lt;br /&gt;Irvine, CA 92697&lt;br /&gt;(949) 824-5011 | logo            = <a>150px</a> }}</p>
<p>The <strong>University of California, Irvine</strong> (<strong>UCI</strong> or <strong>UC Irvine</strong>), founded in 1965, is one of the ten general campuses of the <a>University of California</a>, located in <a>Irvine</a>, <a>California</a>, USA.
<p>UCI also maintains the UC Irvine Health Sciences system with its flagship <a>UCI Medical Center</a> in the <a>city of Orange</a>, the <a>University of California, Irvine, Arboretum</a>, and a portion of the <a>University of California Natural Reserve System</a>.</p>
<p>The University of California, Irvine was one of three new campuses established in the 1960s under the <a>California Master Plan for Higher Education</a> with the <a>San Diego</a> and <a>Santa Cruz</a> campuses.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite
web | title=Peter, the Anteater: History of the Mascot (Zot) | year=2006 | publisher=University of California, Irvine | url=<a>http://www.admissions.uci.edu/mascot.html</a>

<p>{{Infobox university |name           = Michigan Technological University |image          = <a>160px</a> |caption        = Seal of Michigan Technological University |motto          = Create the Future |established    = 1885 |type           = <a>Public</a> |endowment      = <a>US$</a>63.6
<p><strong>Michigan Technological University</strong> (<a>abbr.</a>
In the final years of his presidency the school changed from a college to a university, changing its name a final time to Michigan Technological University.&lt;ref
The name Michigan Technological University was chosen in order to retain the nickname of Michigan Tech that had already been in use since 1927.
Along with the new name, Michigan Technological University, the school gained new constitutional status in 1964.
<p>Michigan Technological University proposed to begin the construction of an environmentally friendly building in the summer of 1996.
  <li><strong>Douglass Houghton Hall</strong>, commonly called DHH, is the smallest and oldest residence hall at Michigan Technological University.
<p>Students attending Michigan Technological University have a wide range of activities to participate in, whether or not they are living in the <a>residence halls</a>.
<p>Michigan Technological University's Enterprise Program is considered by many to be the University's defining feature.
<p>The Pavlis Institute for Global Technological Leadership was formed at Michigan Technological University in 2006.

<p>{{Infobox University |name           = Carnegie Mellon University |image_name     = CarnegieMellonSeal.png
|logo           = <a>200px</a> }}  <strong>Carnegie Mellon University</strong> (also known as <strong>Carnegie Mellon</strong> or simply <strong>CMU</strong>) is a <a>private</a> <a>research university</a> in <a>Pittsburgh</a>, <a>Pennsylvania</a>.
In 1967, the <a>Carnegie Institute of Technology</a> merged with the <a>Mellon Institute of Industrial Research</a> to form Carnegie Mellon University.
In 1965, it merged with the <a>Mellon Institute of Industrial Research</a> to become Carnegie Mellon University.
The period starting with the construction of the Graduate School of Industrial Administration building (1952) and ending with Wean Hall (1971) saw the institutional change from Carnegie Institute of Technology to Carnegie Mellon University.
panoramic view of Carnegie Mellon University's Pittsburgh campus from the College of Fine Arts Lawn.&lt;br/&gt;From left to right: College of Fine Arts, Hunt Library, Baker and Porter Hall, Hamerschlag Hall, <a>University of Pittsburgh</a>'s Cathedral of Learning (in the background), Wean Hall and Doherty Hall, Purnell Center, and the University Center.
<p>In addition to its Pittsburgh campus, Carnegie Mellon has a branch campuses in the <a>Middle East</a>, <a>Carnegie Mellon University in Qatar</a>, which offers a full undergraduate curriculum with degree programs in computer science, business administration and information systems.
<p>The Carnegie Mellon University campus in Pittsburgh served as the locale for many of the on-campus scenes in the 2000 film <em><a>Wonder Boys</a></em>, starring <a>Michael Douglas</a> and <a>Tobey Maguire</a>.
<p><a>thumb|250px|right|The Hunt Library at Carnegie Mellon University is the largest library on the Pittsburgh Campus</a></p>
  <li><strong>The <a>School of Computer Science</a></strong>: Carnegie Mellon University helped define, and continually redefines, the field of <a>computer science</a>.
<p>Carnegie Mellon University Libraries include Hunt Library, the Engineering and Science Library, the <a>Mellon Institute</a> Library, the Posner Center, and the Qatar Library.
The Hunt Institute for Botanical Documentation (HIBD), a research division of Carnegie Mellon University, and its library collections are located on the top floor of Hunt Library, but are not part of the University Library System.&lt;ref
<p>The <strong><a>Pittsburgh Supercomputing Center</a></strong> (PSC) is a joint effort between Carnegie Mellon University, <a>University of Pittsburgh</a>, and <a>Westinghouse Electric Company</a>.
PSC was founded in 1986 by its two scientific directors, Dr. Ralph Roskies of the University of Pittsburgh and Dr. Michael Levine of Carnegie Mellon University.
<p>The <strong><a>Software Engineering Institute</a></strong> (SEI) is a <a>federally funded research and development center</a> sponsored by the U.S. Department of Defense and operated by Carnegie Mellon University, with offices in Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania, USA; Arlington, Virginia, and Frankfurt, Germany.
Mountaineer and Author <a>Aron Ralston</a> also graduated from Carnegie Mellon University.</p>
<p>The Greek tradition at Carnegie Mellon University began nearly 100 years ago with the founding of the first fraternity on campus, <a>Theta Xi</a>, in 1912.
<p>Currently, Carnegie Mellon University has ten active Fraternities: Alpha Epsilon Pi, Beta Theta Pi, Delta Tau Delta, Kappa Sigma, Pi Kappa Alpha, Sigma Alpha Epsilon, Sigma Nu, Sigma Phi Epsilon, Sigma Tau Gamma and Sigma Chi (colony).</p>

In 1994 the <a>University College London Hospitals NHS Trust</a> was established.
In August 2008 UCL formed <a>UCL Partners</a>, the largest <a>academic health science centre</a> in Europe, with <a>Great Ormond Street Hospital for Children NHS Trust</a>, <a>Moorfields Eye Hospital NHS Foundation Trust</a>, <a>Royal Free Hampstead NHS Trust</a> and <a>University College London Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust</a>.&lt;ref
Awarding, University College London</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>

<p><a>ar:&#x0643;&#x0644;&#x064a;&#x0629; &#x0644;&#x0646;&#x062f;&#x0646; &#x0627;&#x0644;&#x062c;&#x0627;&#x0645;&#x0639;&#x064a;&#x0629;</a> <a>bn:&#x0987;&#x0989;&#x09a8;&#x09bf;&#x09ad;&#x09be;&#x09b0;&#x09cd;&#x09b8;&#x09bf;&#x099f;&#x09bf; &#x0995;&#x09b2;&#x09c7;&#x099c; &#x09b2;&#x09a8;&#x09cd;&#x09a1;&#x09a8;</a> <a>bg:&#x041b;&#x043e;&#x043d;&#x0434;&#x043e;&#x043d;&#x0441;&#x043a;&#x0438; &#x0443;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442;&#x0441;&#x043a;&#x0438; &#x043a;&#x043e;&#x043b;&#x0435;&#x0436;</a> <a>ca:University College de Londres</a> <a>cs:University College London</a> <a>da:University College London</a> <a>de:University College London</a> <a>et:University College London</a> <a>es:University College de Londres</a> <a>fa:&#x06a9;&#x0627;&#x0644;&#x062c; &#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647;&#x06cc; &#x0644;&#x0646;&#x062f;&#x0646;</a> <a>fr:University College de Londres</a> <a>ko:&#xc720;&#xb2c8;&#xbc84;&#xc2dc;&#xd2f0; &#xce7c;&#xb9ac;&#xc9c0; &#xb7f0;&#xb358;</a> <a>is:University College London</a> <a>it:University College (Londra)</a> <a>he:&#x05e7;&#x05d5;&#x05dc;&#x05d2;' &#x05d0;&#x05d5;&#x05e0;&#x05d9;&#x05d1;&#x05e8;&#x05e1;&#x05d9;&#x05d8;&#x05ea; &#x05dc;&#x05d5;&#x05e0;&#x05d3;&#x05d5;&#x05df;</a> <a>hu:University College London</a> <a>nl:University College London</a> <a>ja:&#x30e6;&#x30cb;&#x30f4;&#x30a1;&#x30fc;&#x30b7;&#x30c6;&#x30a3;&#x30fb;&#x30ab;&#x30ec;&#x30c3;&#x30b8;&#x30fb;&#x30ed;&#x30f3;&#x30c9;&#x30f3;</a> <a>no:University College London</a> <a>nn:University College London</a> <a>pnb:&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0646;&#x06cc;&#x0648;&#x0631;&#x0633;&#x0679;&#x06cc; &#x06a9;&#x0627;&#x0644;&#x062c; &#x0644;&#x0646;&#x062f;&#x0646;</a> <a>pl:University College London</a> <a>pt:University College London</a> <a>ro:University College London</a> <a>ru:&#x0423;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442;&#x0441;&#x043a;&#x0438;&#x0439; &#x043a;&#x043e;&#x043b;&#x043b;&#x0435;&#x0434;&#x0436; &#x041b;&#x043e;&#x043d;&#x0434;&#x043e;&#x043d;&#x0430;</a> <a>simple:University College London</a> <a>fi:University College London</a> <a>sv:University College London</a> <a>tr:University College London</a> <a>zh:&#x4f26;&#x6566;&#x5927;&#x5b66;&#x5b66;&#x9662;</a></p>
<p>The <strong>University of Vienna</strong> () is a <a>public university</a> located in <a>Vienna</a>, <a>Austria</a>.
In 2010, according to University Ranking by Academic Performance (URAP),&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; University of Vienna is the best university in Austria and 158th university in the world.</p>
<p><a>thumb|240px|left|University of Vienna, main building, seen from across the Ringstra&#x00df;e</a> The University was founded on March 12, 1365 by <a>Rudolf IV, Duke of Austria</a> and his two brothers, <a>Albert III, Duke of Austria</a> and <a>Leopold III, Duke of Austria</a>, hence the additional name &#x201c;Alma Mater Rudolphina&#x201d;.
After the <a>Charles University</a> in <a>Prague</a> and <a>Jagiellonian University</a> in <a>Krakow</a>, the University of Vienna is the third oldest university in <a>Central Europe</a> and the oldest university in the German-speaking world.</p>
Approval was finally received from the Pope in 1384 and the University of Vienna was granted the status of a full university, including the Faculty of Catholic Theology.
<p>Following the <a>Anschluss</a>, the annexation of Austria into Greater Germany by the Nazi regime, in 1938 the University of Vienna was reformed under political aspects and a huge number of teachers and students were dismissed for political and &quot;racial&quot; reasons.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://gedenkbuch.univie.ac.at/index.php?L=2</a> Memorial Book for the Victims of National Socialism at the University of Vienna in 1938&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p><a>thumb|240px|Main Ceremonial Chamber (<em>Gro&#x00df;er Festsaal</em>) in the Main Building</a> The academic facilities of the University of Vienna occupy more than sixty locations throughout the city of Vienna.
The nearby <a>Campus of the University of Vienna</a> forms an additional, more spacious, focus of the University.
<p>The University of Vienna was placed 85th in the <a>Times Higher Education's</a> World University Rankings in 2007, rising from 87th place in 2006.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>The University of Vienna, like all universities and academies in Austria, once featured a system of democratic representation.
The reforms also separated the medical departments into separate medical schools, such as the <a>Medical University of Vienna</a>.</p>
<p><a>Nobel Prize</a> Laureates who taught at the University of Vienna include <a>Robert B&#x00e1;r&#x00e1;ny</a>, <a>Julius Wagner-Jauregg</a>, <a>Hans Fischer</a>, <a>Karl Landsteiner</a>, <a>Erwin Schr&#x00f6;dinger</a>, <a>Victor Franz Hess</a>, <a>Otto Loewi</a>, <a>Konrad Lorenz</a> and <a>Friedrich Hayek</a>.</p>
<p>The University of Vienna was the cradle of the <a>Austrian School</a> of economics.
The founders of this &#x00e9;cole who studied and later instructed at the University of Vienna included <a>Carl Menger</a>, <a>Eugen von B&#x00f6;hm-Bawerk</a>, <a>Friedrich von Wieser</a>, <a>Joseph Schumpeter</a>, <a>Ludwig von Mises</a> and <a>Friedrich Hayek</a>.</p>
<p>Other famous scholars who have taught at the University of Vienna are: <a>Theodor W. Adorno</a>, <a>Manfred Bietak</a>, <a>Theodor Billroth</a>, <a>Ludwig Boltzmann</a>, <a>Franz Brentano</a>, <a>Anton Bruckner</a>, <a>Rudolf Carnap</a>, <a>Conrad Celtes</a>, <a>Viktor Frankl</a>, <a>Sigmund Freud</a>, <a>Eduard Hanslick</a>, <a>Edmund Hauler</a>, <a>Hans Kelsen</a>, <a>Adam Franti&#x0161;ek Koll&#x00e1;r</a>, <a>Johann Josef Loschmidt</a>, <a>Fran Miklo&#x0161;i&#x010d;</a>, <a>Oskar Morgenstern</a>, <a>Otto Neurath</a>, <a>Johann Palisa</a>, <a>Pope Pius II</a>, <a>Baron Carl von Rokitansky</a>, <a>August Schleicher</a>, <a>Moritz Schlick</a>, <a>Ludwig Karl Schmarda</a>, <a>Joseph von Sonnenfels</a>, <a>Josef Stefan</a>, <a>Leopold Vietoris</a>, <a>Jalile Jalil</a> and <a>Carl Auer von Welsbach</a></p>
<p>The University Library of the University of Vienna comprises the Main Library and the 50 departmental libraries at the various university locations throughout <a>Vienna</a>.
<p>Kalamazoo College is a member of the <a>Great Lakes Colleges Association</a>.

| logo                 = &lt;center&gt;<a>183px|upright|Logo of Duke University</a>&lt;/center&gt; }} <strong>Duke University</strong> is a <a>private</a> <a>research university</a> located in <a>Durham, North Carolina</a>, <a>United States</a>.
Duke University is also ranked 14th in the 2010 <a>QS World University Rankings</a>.&lt;ref
<a>William Preston Few</a>, the president of Trinity College, insisted that the university be named Duke University to honor the family's generosity and to distinguish itself from the myriad of other colleges and universities carrying the &quot;Trinity&quot; name.

Buchanan Duke|James B. Duke]] established the <a>Duke Endowment</a>, which provides funds to numerous institutions including Duke University.]]</p>

<a>Duke University Hospital</a> was finished in 1980 and the student union was fully constructed two years later.
<em>Duke University Admissions.</em>
<p>Duke University's growth and academic focus have contributed to the university's reputation as an academic and research powerhouse.
<p>[[File:Divinitychapelduke.jpg|right|thumb|Part of the [[Duke Divinity School|Divinity School]] addition, Goodson Chapel]] Duke University owns 220 buildings on 8,610&nbsp;acres (35&nbsp;km&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt;) of land, which includes the 7,200&nbsp;acre (29&nbsp;km&#x00b2;) Duke Forest.&lt;ref
All the campuses are connected via a free bus service or the <a>Duke University Medical Center Patient Rapid Transit</a> people mover.
<em>Duke University Archives.</em>
<em>Duke University Historical Notes.</em>
<p> With more than six million <a>volumes</a>, the <a>Duke University Library System</a> is one of the ten largest private research university library systems in the U.S. and is the 22nd largest among members of the Association of Research Libraries.&lt;ref&gt;<a>The
<em>Duke University Libraries.</em>
<em>Duke University Libraries.</em>
Museum of Art at Duke University</a>.
<em>Nasher Museum of Art at Duke University.</em>
<p> West Campus, the heart of Duke University, houses all the sophomores, along with some juniors and seniors.&lt;ref
<em>Duke University.</em>
standard sizing due to unusual picture dimensions--&gt; |} East Campus, the original location of Duke University,&lt;ref name = &quot;EastCamp&quot;/&gt; functions as a freshman campus as well as the home of several academic departments.
Duke Forest, established in 1931, today consists of 7,200&nbsp;acres (29&nbsp;km&#x00b2;) in six divisions, just west of Duke University's West Campus.&lt;ref
<p>Kalamazoo College was founded in 1833 by a group of Baptist ministers as the Michigan and Huron Institute.
<p>[[File:MedicalCenter.jpg|left|thumb|Entrance to the [[Duke University Medical Center|Medical Center]] from West Campus]] The <a>Sarah P. Duke Gardens</a>, established in the early 1930s, is situated between West Campus and the apartments of Central Campus.
<p><a>Duke University Medical Center</a>, located directly north of West Campus, combines one of the top-rated hospitals and one of the top-ranked <a>medical schools</a> in the U.S. Founded in 1930, the Medical Center occupies 8 million square feet (700,000&nbsp;m&#x00b2;) in 99 buildings on 210&nbsp;acres (8.5&nbsp;km&#x00b2;).&lt;ref&gt;<a>DukeMedNews</a>.
<p>Duke University Marine Lab, although located in the town of <a>Beaufort, North Carolina</a>, is also part of Duke's campus.
name=&quot;William Joseph Whalen - Hospitals &amp; Universities&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;IAMSCU&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url = <a>http://public.gbhem.org/iamscu/search_results.asp?act=search_gen&amp;search_txt=Duke+University&amp;type=schools&amp;submit=GO</a>| title = Duke University|publisher = <a>International Association of Methodist-related Schools, Colleges, and Universities</a> (IAMSCU)|accessdate = 2007-06-30}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;DU &amp; UMC&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Duke University Archives - Nature of Affiliation&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; For the undergraduate class of 2014, Duke received 26,784&nbsp;applications, and accepted approximately 14% of them.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Record
<a>College Search - Duke University</a>.
<p>Duke University has two schools for undergraduates: <a>Trinity College of Arts and Sciences</a> and <a>Pratt School of Engineering</a>.&lt;ref
name=&quot;admissions1&quot;/&gt; The University's graduate and professional schools include the <a>Graduate School</a>, the <a>Pratt School of Engineering</a>, the <a>Nicholas School of the Environment</a>, the <a>School of Medicine</a>, the <a>Duke-NUS Graduate Medical School</a>, the <a>School of Nursing</a>, the <a>Fuqua School of Business</a>, the <a>School of Law</a>, the <a>Divinity School</a>, and the <a>Sanford School of Public Policy</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Duke homepage - Schools tab</a> <em>Duke University.</em>
<p>Duke University's <a>endowment</a> had a market value of $5.0 billion as of March 31, 2010.&lt;ref
<em>Duke University.</em>
<em>Duke University.</em>
In the 2005 fiscal year, Duke University Medical Center received the fifth-largest amount of funding from the <a>National Institute of Health</a>, netting $349.8 million.
In the 2008 fiscal year, <a>Duke University School of Nursing</a>  jumped to 18th nationally in the rankings of the <a>National Institute of Health</a> funding for nursing schools, netting more than $2.34 million, up 54 percent from 2007, when it ranked 30th nationally.&lt;ref&gt;Stagg,
<em>Duke University.</em>
<em>Duke University.</em>
<em>Duke University News &amp; Communications</em>, August 18, 2006.
The Duke University Physician Assistant Program, the first of its kind when it began in 1965, also ranked first in the publication for physician assistant programs.
The administration has been very active in the past few years with efforts to help students re-establish a robust, on-campus social life and has worked with numerous student groups, especially the Duke University Union, to feature a wide array of events and activities.
<em>[[The Chronicle (Duke University)|The Chronicle]]<strong>s administrative office, the Mary Lou Williams Center for <a>Black</a> Culture, and the Center for <a>LGBT</a> Life are all located in the Union.]]</strong>
<em>Duke University Office of Student Activities and Facilities</em>, July 1, 2009.
Chartered by the Board of Trustees, the most prominent amongst these are the Duke Student Government, the Duke University Union, and Campus Council.
The Duke University Union (DUU) is the school's primary programming organization, serving a center of social, cultural, intellectual and recreational life.&lt;ref&gt;<a><em>Duke
Performance groups such as Hoof 'n' Horn, the country's second oldest student-run musical theater organization, a cappella groups such as the Duke Pitchforks, student bands such as <a>Alan Davis Band</a>, and <a>Duke University Improv</a> are also prominent on campus.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Hoof
'n' Horn</a>&lt;/ref&gt; The Duke University Student Dining Advisory Committee, or DUSDAC, provides guidance to the administration on issues regarding student dining, life, and restaurant choices.</p>

<p>The <strong>University of Idaho</strong> is the state of <a>Idaho</a>'s oldest public university, located in the rural city of <a>Moscow</a> in <a>Latah County</a> in the <a>northern portion</a> of the state.
The University of Idaho (officially abbreviated <strong>UI,</strong> but commonly referred to as the <strong>U of I</strong>) was the state's sole university for 71 years, until <a>1963</a>, and hosts the state's only <a>law school</a>, established in 1909 and accredited by the <a>ABA</a> in 1925.</p>
      <li>- College of Engineering established in cooperation with the College of Mines&lt;ref name=autogenerated1&gt;<a>1907-1957 Historical Events, Centennial 1907 - 2007 College of Engineering, University of Idaho&lt;!--
  <li>1948 - inaugural <a>Borah</a> Symposium&lt;ref&gt;<a>The Borah Foundation at the University of Idaho&lt;!--
name=autogenerated5&gt;<a>The University of Idaho Argonaut - LOST AND FOUND: University of Idaho's traditions have come and gone since its opening&lt;!--
Additionally, there is study space, wireless internet, laptop checkout, and many student services such as the offices of the Associated Students of the University of Idaho (ASUI), Academics Assistance, and Student Support.</p>
<p><a>thumb|250px|North entrance to the University of Idaho Arboretum and Botanical Garden</a> Referred to as &quot;Tree City&quot; or &quot;The Arb&quot; by UI students, the <a>Arboretum</a> is a 65 acre (26 hectare) site adjacent to the golf course which features display gardens, ponds, and a variety of trees and plants from <a>Asia</a>, <a>Europe</a>, and <a>North America</a>.</p>
Opened in 1928 to honor the Idaho citizens who died in <a>World War I</a> (1917&#x2013;18), the heavily <a>buttress</a>ed  structure was designed by the chairman of the university's architecture department, David C. Lang&lt;ref&gt;<a>Memorial Gym - University of Idaho Athletics Official Site &#x2014; GoVandals.com&lt;!--
<p>The University of Idaho is home to 17 housed <a>fraternities</a>, 10 housed <a>sororities</a>, and 7 multicultural Greek organizations that make up more than 20% of the student population, and over 44% of the students who live on campus (around 1,800 students).
name=autogenerated4&gt;<a>University of Idaho - Fast Facts&lt;!--
<p>From 1896 through fall 2006, the University of Idaho has granted 71,599 bachelor's degrees, 19,028 master's degrees, 2,270 doctoral degrees, 222 honorary degrees, 917 specialist degrees, and 3,157 law degrees.&lt;ref
  <li>Associated Students University of Idaho (ASUI)</li>
  <li><a>Idaho Gem</a>, the world's first cloned equine (a mule), was created by researchers at the University of Idaho and <a>Utah State University</a>.</li>
<li>The university of Idaho self-reports that its average freshman SAT scores are 543.23 (Verbal) and 548.72 (Math).&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.uihome.uidaho.edu/uihome/about/overview_fastfacts.aspx?utm_campaign=uihome&amp;utm_source=www_redirect/</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</li>
<li><em>Kiplinger</em> magazine ranks the University of Idaho among the top 50 best values in public universities.</li>
  <li>University of Idaho Master of Architecture program is internationally Accredited by the Northwest Commission on Colleges and Universities, and Also National Architectural Accrediting Board.&lt;ref&gt;[<a>http://www.uidaho.edu/about/universityoverview/accreditation</a>]&lt;/ref&gt;</li>
<p><strong>Go, Vandals, Go</strong> is the official <a>fight song</a> of the University of Idaho.</p>

<p><a>de:University of Idaho</a> <a>fa:&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0646;&#x0634;&#x06af;&#x0627;&#x0647; &#x0622;&#x06cc;&#x062f;&#x0627;&#x0647;&#x0648;</a> <a>fr:Universit&#x00e9; d'Idaho</a> <a>ja:&#x30a2;&#x30a4;&#x30c0;&#x30db;&#x5927;&#x5b66;</a> <a>no:University of Idaho</a> <a>ru:&#x0423;&#x043d;&#x0438;&#x0432;&#x0435;&#x0440;&#x0441;&#x0438;&#x0442;&#x0435;&#x0442; &#x0410;&#x0439;&#x0434;&#x0430;&#x0445;&#x043e;</a> <a>th:&#x0e21;&#x0e2b;&#x0e32;&#x0e27;&#x0e34;&#x0e17;&#x0e22;&#x0e32;&#x0e25;&#x0e31;&#x0e22;&#x0e44;&#x0e2d;&#x0e14;&#x0e32;&#x0e42;&#x0e2e;</a></p>
<p>   <strong>Kalamazoo College</strong>, also known as <strong>K College</strong> or simply <strong>K</strong>, is a <a>private</a> <a>liberal arts college</a> in <a>Kalamazoo</a>, <a>Michigan</a>, <a>United States</a>.
<p>James Stone, the first president of Kalamazoo College, led the school from 1842 through 1863 and was responsible for instituting the high academic standards that allowed the College to receive its charter.
<p>The first known student of African descent to attend Kalamazoo College was ex-slave Rufus Lewis Perry.
Kalamazoo College also served as a pioneer in <a>coed education</a>, granting its first degree to a woman, Miss Catherine V. Eldred, in 1870.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>In 1877, Kalamazoo College students published the first edition of <em>The Index</em>, a student-run newspaper that continues to publish today.
<p>Kalamazoo College's reputation as an academic powerhouse and a leader in international education was built during the presidency of <a>Weimer Hicks</a>, who served from 1954 to 1971.&lt;ref name=&quot;kpl.gov&quot;/&gt;
As part of the original &quot;K Plan,&quot; Kalamazoo College students could attend school year-round.
<p>Kalamazoo College is among the 100 oldest colleges and universities in the United States.
<p>Students at Kalamazoo College must fulfill specific degree requirements in order to graduate.
Ninety-five percent of Kalamazoo College's faculty have doctorates or terminal degrees in their fields.&lt;ref
<p>On January 3, 2006, Kalamazoo College opened the new Upjohn Library Commons which includes the completely renovated skeleton of the older library, and an extension which adds to its volume capacity.</p>
<p>Kalamazoo College is an academic leader among national liberal arts colleges and emphasizes the importance of an experiential education.
Kalamazoo College is also unique in that it requires its students to take comprehensive exams in their major field of study before graduating.
Kalamazoo College is the only undergraduate institution in the United States that requires both a senior project and a comprehensive examination.</p>
<p>Kalamazoo College initiated the service-learning program in the 1997.
In 2008, Kalamazoo College had twenty-three on-going service-learning programs.
<p><a>US News &amp; World Report</a> America's Best Colleges 2003 ranked Kalamazoo College's study-abroad program number one in the country.
Nearly 85% of Kalamazoo College students spend at least one term abroad and the college maintains partnerships with over 50 foreign universities on six continents.
<p>In 2009, the Center Career Development merged with the <a>Guilds of Kalamazoo College</a> to create the <a>Center for Career and Professional Development</a>.
The CCPD's mission is to create meaningful connections to the world of work, empowering Kalamazoo College students to explore, identify and pursue their diverse interests, values and passions, and to develop a framework of skills, networks and knowledge for successful lifelong career planning and professional development.
<p>A recent study by Higher Education Data Sharing lists Kalamazoo College in the top 1 percent of colleges and universities whose graduates go on to earn a <a>Ph.D</a>.
According to this study, Kalamazoo College is ranked number nine among all private colleges and&#x2014;when compared with all academic institutions&#x2014;it ranks number fourteen in Ph.Ds per capita.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Among all undergraduate institutions, Kalamazoo College was #1 per capita in 2005 for recruitment of Peace Corps volunteers.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
Kalamazoo College competes in the following sports:</p>
<p>The Kalamazoo College men&#x2019;s tennis team has won 72 consecutive Michigan Intercollegiate Athletic Association championships (1936&#x2013;2010) with a record of 426-2 in the MIAA from 1935 - 2007.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>Men's swimming and diving at Kalamazoo College has an impressive history.
The swimming and diving team is the second most successful athletic program at Kalamazoo College, after the men's tennis team, and it is also one of the top-10 most-successful teams in the MIAA with  25 MIAA championships.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>In 2001, the Kalamazoo College men's basketball team was at the center of a lengthy dispute regarding the outcome of a January 20 game with league rival <a>Olivet College</a>.
With Olivet leading 70-69, Kalamazoo College center Kevin Baird made a shot at the buzzer that was initially waved off by referees.
The referees reviewed videotape of the game and determined that Baird had, in fact, released his shot before the buzzer and then awarded Kalamazoo College a 71-70 victory.
name=&quot;Time-Travel: History of Kalamazoo College&quot;&gt;<a>&quot;Time-Travel: History of Kalamazoo College&quot;</a>, Kalamazoo College.
<p>Kalamazoo College has become a leading institution in the area of recycling and environmental awareness.
In 2005, Kalamazoo College came to national prominence with a 3rd-place finish in the Grand Champion category.
While annually placing in the top 5 in a variety of categories, in 2008 Kalamazoo College placed 1st in both the Grand Champion and Stephen K Gaski Per Capita Classic competitions.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
<p>Kalamazoo College signed the President's Climate Commitment in 2007 and has completed a greenhouse gas emissions inventory.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<h2>Presidents of Kalamazoo College</h2>
<p> In 2005 Dr. <a>Eileen Wilson-Oyelaran</a> became Kalamazoo College's 17th President and first female president, as well as the first African-American president of the school.

<p>{{Infobox University |name            = California State University |native_name     = |latin_name      = |image_name      = California State University Seal.png |image_size      = 176px |motto           = <em>Vox Veritas Vita</em> (<a>Latin</a>) |mottoeng        = &quot;Voice Truth Life&quot; (Speak the truth as a way of life.)
<p>The <strong>California State University</strong> (<strong>CSU</strong>) is a <a>public university</a> <a>system</a> in the <a>state</a> of <a>California</a>.
It is incorporated as <strong>The Trustees of the California State University</strong>.
The California State University system headquarters are at 401 Golden Shore in <a>downtown Long Beach</a>.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Home
<em>California State University</em>.
<p>Today's California State University system is the direct descendant of the <a>California State Normal School</a> (now <a>San Jose State University</a>), a <a>normal school</a> established by the California Legislature on May 2, 1862.
<p>In 1972 the system became The California State University and Colleges, and all of the campuses were renamed with the words &quot;California State University&quot; in their names.
Former San Diego State University student body president Calvin Robinson wrote the bill, signed into law by Ronald Reagan, that allowed every California State University the option to revert the schools back to their pre-1972 names: San Jose State, San Diego State, San Francisco State, etc.
<p><a>thumb|right|250px|Office of the Chancellor in Long Beach</a> The governance structure of the California State University is largely determined by state law.
The California State University is ultimately administered by the 25 member <a>Board of Trustees of the California State University</a>.
The Trustees appoint the <a>Chancellor of the California State University</a>, who is the <a>chief executive officer</a> of the system, and the Presidents of each campus, who are the chief executive officers of their respective campuses.</p>
<p>The <a>Academic Senate of the California State University</a>, made up of elected representatives of the faculty from each campus, recommends academic policy to the Board of Trustees through the Chancellor.</p>
<p>The California State University is administered by the 25 member Board of Trustees (BOT).
  <li>two students from the California State University appointed by the Governor</li>
  <li>a representative of the alumni associations of the state university selected for a two-year term by the alumni council of the California State University</li>
The delegation of authority from the BOT to the Chancellor has historically been controlled by a BOT resolution titled &quot;Statement of General Principles in the Delegation of Authority and Responsibility&quot; of August 4, 1961, and is now controlled by the Standing Orders of the Board of Trustees of the California State University.

Unlike the typical university extension courses, they are degree-granting and students have the same status as other California State University students.
The newest campus, the California State University, Channel Islands, was formerly an off campus branch of CSUN.
Riverside and Contra Costa counties, which have 3 million residents between them, have lobbied for their off campus branches to be freestanding California State University campuses.

As a result of recent legislation (SB 724 and AB 2382), the California State University may now offer the <a>Ed.D</a> (also known as the <a>Doctor of Education</a> or &quot;education doctorate degree&quot;) and <a>DPT</a> (Doctor of Physical Therapy) degrees to its graduate students.
Additionally, the California State University (CSU) offers Ph.D degrees and some professional doctorates (for instance, audiology, Au.D) as a &quot;joint degree&quot; in combination with other institutions of higher education, including &quot;joint degrees&quot; with the <a>University of California (UC)</a> and accredited private universities.
Thus, the CSU system has been referred to by former California State University authorities as &quot;The People's University.&quot;&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</p>

  <li>California State University, Fresno</li>

Some critics, including Donald Gerth (a former President of California State University, Sacramento), have claimed that the weak California State University identity has contributed to the CSU's perceived lack of prestige when compared to the <a>University of California</a>.&lt;ref
<p>The California State University (CSU) and most of its campuses are members of APLU and the <a>American Association of State Colleges and Universities (AASCU)</a>.</p>
The California State University has 17 ABET-accredited engineering colleges throughout California.&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.abet.org/schoolstate.asp</a>&lt;/ref&gt;</p>

<p>  The <strong>American Film Institute</strong> is an independent <a>non-profit organization</a> created by the <a>National Endowment for the Arts</a>, which was established in 1967 when President <a>Lyndon B. Johnson</a> signed the National Foundation on the Arts and the Humanities Act.
<p>The American Film Institute re-opened the <a>AFI Silver</a> theatre in <a>Silver Spring, Maryland</a>, near <a>Washington, D.C.</a>, in April 2003.
<p>The American Film Institute was founded in 1967 as a national arts organization to preserve the legacy of America&#x2019;s film heritage, educate the next generation of filmmakers and honor the artists and their work.

<p>The <strong>United States Naval Academy</strong> (also known as <strong>USNA</strong>, <strong>Annapolis</strong>, or <strong>Navy</strong>) is a four-year <a>coeducational</a> <a>federal service academy</a> located in <a>Annapolis</a>, <a>Maryland</a>, United States.
<p><a>thumb|right|Rotunda steps leading to Memorial Hall</a> The United States Naval Academy's campus is located in <a>Annapolis</a>, <a>Maryland</a>, at the confluence of the <a>Severn River</a> and the <a>Chesapeake Bay</a>.</p>
The decision to establish an academy on land may have been in part a result of the <a>Somers</a> Affair, an alleged mutiny involving the Secretary of War's son that resulted in his execution at sea. <a>Commodore</a> <a>Matthew Perry</a> had a considerable interest in naval education, supporting an apprentice system to train new seamen, and helped establish the curriculum for the United States Naval Academy.
The first superintendent of the <a>United States Naval Observatory</a>, Commander <a>Matthew Fontaine Maury</a>, advocate&lt;ref&gt;<a>http://www.history.navy.mil/library/online/maury_mat_bene.htm</a>&lt;/ref&gt; of the creation of the United States Naval Academy, after whom Maury Hall is named, similarly served in the <a>Confederate States Navy</a>.</p>
Honorary Advisor, ABETS, Combustion, Gasification &amp; Propulsion Laboratory of Aerospace Engineering, Indian Institute of Science.</li>

<p>{{Infobox university |name            =Chalmers University of Technology |native_name     =Chalmers tekniska h&#x00f6;gskola |latin_name      = |image           =<a>225px|Logo of Chalmers University of Technology</a> |motto           =Avancez |established     =1829 |type            =Private University |city            =<a>Gothenburg</a> |state           = |country         =<a>Sweden</a> |enrollment      = |students     = 8,400 (<a>FTE</a>, 2008)&lt;ref&gt;<a>Swedish Higher Education Authority (<em>H&#x00f6;gskoleverket</em>) - statistics for 2008 (Swedish), page 121</a>&lt;/ref&gt; |doctoral        =1,000 |staff           =2,500 |president       =Prof.
}} <strong>Chalmers University of Technology</strong> (, often shortened to <strong>Chalmers</strong>), is a <a>university</a> in <a>Gothenburg</a>, <a>Sweden</a>, that focuses on research and education in technology, natural science and architecture.
<p>Chalmers is an <a>aktiebolag</a> with 100 shares &#x00e0; 1000 <a>SEK</a>&lt;ref&gt;<a>Statues of Chalmers University of Technology Foundation, paragraph 3</a> (this is a translation of the <a>swedish text</a>.)&lt;/ref&gt;,
all of which is owned by a private foundation (<a>Chalmers University of Technology Foundation</a>) which appoints the university board and the president.
The foundation has its members appointed by the Swedish government (4 to 8 seats), the departments appoints one member, the <a>student union</a> appoints one member and the president automatically gains one chair.&lt;ref&gt;<a>Statues of Chalmers University of Technology Foundation, paragraph 5</a>&lt;/ref&gt; Each department is led by a department head, usually a member of the faculty of that department.
  <li><a>Chalmers University of Technology</a> - Official site</li>

<p><strong>Iowa State University of Science and Technology</strong>, more commonly known as <strong>Iowa State University</strong> (<strong>ISU</strong>), is a <a>public</a> <a>land-grant</a> and <a>space-grant</a> research university located in <a>Ames, Iowa</a>, <a>United States</a>.

<a>billion</a>&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web | title = Princeton endowment earns 14.7 percent return (10/15/10) | publisher = Princeton University | url = <a>http://www.princeton.edu/main/news/archive/S28/71/07M45/index.xml?section=topstories</a>| accessdate = October 15, 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; |president = <a>Shirley M. Tilghman</a> |students  = 7,567 |undergrad = 5,113&lt;ref&gt;[<a>http://registrar.princeton.edu/university_enrollment_sta/common_cds2009.pdf</a>].
Princeton University Common Data Set.
|logo = <a>150px</a> }} <strong>Princeton University </strong> is a <a>private</a> <a>research university</a> located in <a>Princeton</a>, <a>New Jersey</a>, <a>United States</a>.
<p>Founded in 1746 in <a>Elizabeth, New Jersey</a>, as the College of New Jersey, the university moved to Newark in 1747, then to Princeton in 1756 and was renamed Princeton University in 1896.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>In 1896, the college officially changed its name from the College of New Jersey to Princeton University to honor the town in which it resides.
<p> <a>thumb|200px|right|McCarter Theater</a>The Tony-award-winning&lt;ref&gt;<a>The American Theatre Wing's Tony Awards - Official Website by IBM</a>&lt;/ref&gt; <a>McCarter Theatre</a> was built by the <a>Princeton Triangle Club</a>, a student performance group, using club profits and a gift from Princeton University alumnus Thomas McCarter.
<p> The <a>Princeton University Art Museum</a> was established in 1882 to give students direct, intimate, and sustained access to original works of art that complement and enrich instruction and research at the university.
<p> <a>thumb|200px|right|Princeton University Chapel</a> <a>Princeton University Chapel</a> is the third-largest college chapel in the world, behind those of <a>Valparaiso University</a> and <a>King's College, Cambridge</a>, <a>England</a>.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
Construction on the Princeton University Chapel began in 1924 and was completed in 1927 at a cost of $2.4 million.
name= &quot;Princeton University adopts its Sustainability Plan in February 2008&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; Princeton has committed to reducing its carbon dioxide emissions to 1990 levels by 2020 without the purchase of offsets.&lt;ref
name= &quot;Princeton University Dining Services&quot;&gt;&lt;/ref&gt; The student organization &quot;Greening Princeton&quot; seeks to encourage the University administration to adopt environmentally friendly policies on campus.&lt;ref
<p>With an endowment of US$14.4 <a>billion</a>, Princeton University is among the wealthiest universities in the world.
The Trustees of Princeton University, a 40-member board, is responsible for the overall direction of the University.
In February 2007, Princeton became the 12th major library system to join Google's ambitious project to scan the world's great literary works and make them searchable over the Web.&lt;ref name=&quot;NewsMax&quot;&gt;&quot;<a>Princeton University Joins Google Literature-Scan Project</a>&quot;.
<p>From 2001 to 2010, Princeton University was ranked either first or second among national universities by <em><a>U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></em> (USNWR), holding the #1 spot for 9 of those 10 years.&lt;ref&gt;August
<p>In the &quot;America's Best Colleges&quot; rankings by <em><a>Forbes</a></em> in 2008, Princeton University was ranked first among all national colleges and universities.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;
<p>In <em>Princeton Review<strong>s rankings of &quot;softer&quot; aspects of students' college experience, Princeton University was ranked first in &quot;Students Happy with Financial Aid&quot; and third in &quot;Happiest Students&quot;, behind Clemson and Brown Universities.&lt;ref&gt;&lt;/ref&gt;</strong></em></p>
<p>Princeton University also participates in the (<a>NAICU</a>)'s <a>University and College Accountability Network (U-CAN)</a>.
<p>Princeton University has an IBM <a>BlueGeneL</a> supercomputer, called <em>Orangena</em>, which was ranked as the 89th fastest computer in the world in 2005 (<a>LINPACK</a> performance of 4713 compared to 12250 for other U. S. universities and 280600 for the top-ranked supercomputer, belonging to the <a>U.
&quot;Rowing at Princeton&quot;, Princeton University Rowing Association.&lt;/ref&gt;</p>
The game, between Rutgers College (now <a>Rutgers University</a>) and the College of New Jersey (now Princeton University), took place on November 6, 1869 at College Field (now the site of the College Avenue Gymnasium at Rutgers University) in New Brunswick, New Jersey.
<p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a>commencement</a>, <a>convocation</a>, and athletic games is Princeton Cannon Song, the Princeton University <a>fight song</a>.</p>
<p>&quot;<a>Old Nassau</a>&quot; has been Princeton University's anthem since 1859.
<p> Princeton University has been and is home to a renowned group of scholars, scientists, writers, chief justices, and statesmen who include four United States presidents, two of whom graduated from the university.
<p>The asteroid <a>508 Princetonia</a> is named for Princeton University by <a>R.

<p>The <strong>Indian Institute of Science</strong> (<strong>IISc</strong>) is a research institution of higher learning located in <a>Bangalore</a>, <a>India</a>.
